Tasawwur and Tasdiq
beginner
5 min
Distinguishing al-Haqq and al-Sidq in Correspondence
Commentator defines al-haqq and al-sidq as two types of correspondence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish al-haqq from al-sidq by identifying the direction of correspondence in any proposition-reality pair from Islamic texts.

Core Idea
Al-sidq is statement→reality; al-haqq is reality→statement — the direction flips.

In Islamic logic, truth is not a single concept. The commentator distinguishes two forms of correspondence: one from the side of the proposition (al-sidq) and one from the side of reality (al-haqq). This distinction clarifies how we speak about the truth of statements versus the truth of states of affairs. Understanding this difference is essential for precise reasoning in kalam, fiqh, and tafsir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key terms
Find 'al-haqq' and 'al-sidq' in the Arabic. Note that the commentator defines both in terms of correspondence (mutabaqa).
These are not synonyms; they are two sides of the same coin.
2
Extract the definition of al-sidq
Al-sidq is correspondence of the proposition (al-nisba) to reality (al-waqi'). This is the standard logical truth: a statement is true when it matches the way things are.
3
Extract the definition of al-haqq
Al-haqq is the reverse: correspondence of reality to the proposition. That is, when the actual state of affairs conforms to what is said about it.
This is a less common but important sense: reality being 'true' to the statement.
4
Analyze the direction of correspondence
Visualize two arrows: for al-sidq, arrow goes from proposition→reality; for al-haqq, arrow goes from reality→proposition. The commentator says 'al-mutabaqa fi al-awwal mu'tabarat min janib al-waqi' (correspondence in the first is considered from the side of reality) and 'fi al-thani min janib al-nisba' (in the second from the side of the proposition).
This reversal is crucial: what is 'al-haqq' is the reality itself, not the statement.
5
Apply the distinction to a concrete example
Take the proposition 'The world is temporally originated' (al-ʿālam ḥadith). If the world is indeed originated, then the statement is sidq (true statement). Moreover, the reality of the world being originated is haqq (true reality). The same fact yields both sidq and haqq from different perspectives.
This example from kalam shows the two concepts in action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قَوْلُهُ : غِيَاتُ) أي : مُغيثُ ومُنقذُ الحقِّ مِن إخفائه، والحقُّ مُطابقة الواقع للنِّسبة بخلافِ الصِّدق؛ فإِنَّهُ مُطابقةُ النِّسبة للواقع، فالمطابقة في الأوَّلِ : مُعتبرةٌ مِن جانبِ الواقع، وفي الثَّاني : مِن جانبِ النِّسبة، وقولُهُ: غياتُ الحقِّ يحتمل أنَّ المراد : الكلامُ الحقُّ الشَّامِلُ لِلقرآنِ والسُّنَّةِ وقضايا العلوم الشَّرعيَّة، أو مُغيثُ أهل الحقِّ.
His statement: 'Ghuyath' means helper and rescuer of truth (al-haqq) from its concealment. And al-haqq is the correspondence of reality to the proposition, unlike al-sidq (truthfulness), for it is the correspondence of the proposition to reality. So correspondence in the first is considered from the side of reality, and in the second from the side of the proposition. And his statement: 'Ghuyath al-haqq' may mean the true speech that includes the Qur'an, the Sunnah, and the issues of the religious sciences, or the helper of the people of truth.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage defines two key terms in Islamic epistemology: al-haqq (truth/reality) and al-sidq (truthfulness/veracity). The commentator is expanding on the meaning of 'ghuyath al-haqq' in the praise of the Sultan. He explains that al-haqq is the correspondence of external reality (al-waqi') to the proposition (al-nisba), meaning that the reality itself matches the statement. In contrast, al-sidq is the correspondence of the proposition to reality, which is the standard definition of truth in logic. Thus, the direction of correspondence is reversed: al-haqq looks from reality to statement, al-sidq from statement to reality. For example, the statement 'The world is temporally originated' (al-ʿālam ḥadith) – if the world is indeed originated, then the statement is sidq (true) and the reality is haqq (truth). The commentator also notes that 'ghuyath al-haqq' may refer to the true speech (the Qur'an and Sunnah) or to the helper of the people of truth. This distinction is crucial in Islamic logic and theology, especially in discussions of divine attributes and the truth of propositions.

Key Terms
الحق (al-haqq): Correspondence of reality to the proposition; the state of being true in reality. [Note: In later falsafa, al-haqq often refers to metaphysical truth (e.g., God as al-Haqq); here it is used in a logical-epistemic sense.]
الصدق (al-sidq): Correspondence of the proposition to reality; the standard definition of truth in logic. [Note: Stable across the tradition; used consistently in mantiq as the truth of statements.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, al-haqq is defined as:
A) Correspondence of the proposition to reality
B) Correspondence of reality to the proposition
C) The same as al-sidq
D) A synonym for al-mutābaqa

Key Takeaway
Truth has two directions: sidq when the statement fits reality, and haqq when reality fits the statement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the Qur'anic verse 'Allah is the Creator of everything' (Qur'an 13:16). Identify whether this verse is al-sidq, al-haqq, or both, and explain why using the definitions from the passage.
?
Consider the proposition 'The sun rises from the east.' According to the commentator's distinction, is this proposition al-sidq? Is its reality al-haqq? Give a one-sentence justification for each.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
7 min
Why Knowledge Must Be Defined as Absolute Apprehension
Commentary defining 'ilm as absolute apprehension and explaining the necessity of the unrestricted definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to justify why the definition of 'ilm must be unrestricted (mutlaq) for the division into tasawwur and tasdiq to be valid.

Core Idea
Only an unrestricted definition of knowledge allows its proper division into conceptualization and assent.

The commentator begins by stating that knowledge is apprehension absolutely. He then explains why the definition cannot be restricted to either singular apprehension (conceptualization) or relational apprehension (assent). Otherwise, dividing knowledge into those two would be dividing a thing into itself and another. This lesson unpacks that logical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two restrictions of 'ilm
The passage mentions that some restricted 'ilm to either idrak mufrad (apprehension of a single term) or idrak al-nisba (apprehension of a relation). Find where these are mentioned and note why each would make division into tasawwur and tasdiq problematic.
The two restrictions correspond to tasawwur and tasdiq respectively.
2
Understand why restricted definitions cause self-division
If 'ilm were defined as only tasawwur, then dividing 'ilm into tasawwur and tasdiq would be dividing it into itself (tasawwur) and something else (tasdiq), which is invalid because a thing cannot be divided into itself and another. Similarly for tasdiq.
3
Recognize the commentator's solution
The commentator defines 'ilm as idrak mutlaq (absolute apprehension) without restriction, so that when divided, tasawwur and tasdiq are both genuine parts of the whole without overlapping with the whole.
Mutlaq means unrestricted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتنِ (العِلْمُ) وهو : الإدراكُ مُطلقاً
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : الْعِلْمُ أي : الحادثُ؛ لأنَّهُ المنقسم للأقسام المذكورة.
(قَوْلُهُ : وَهُوَ الْإِدْرَاكُ مُطْلَقَاً) أي: من غير تقييد له بكونه إدراك مفرد، أو إدراك وقوع الـ النسبة أو لا وقوعها، فالمراد مُطلقُ الإدراك، وإنَّما قيَّدَهُ بِالإطلاق؛ ليصح تقسيمُهُ لِمَا يأتي; إذْ لو كان المراد به خصوص إدراك أن النسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعةٍ كَما قاله بعض الأصولتين، أو إدراك المفرد؛ كان التقسيم باطلاً؛ لأنه تقسيم الشَّيء لِنَفْسِهِ ولغيره .
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ: العِلْمُ وَهُوَ : الْإِدْرَاكُ مُطْلَقَاً) أي: سواءٌ كان على وجه الإذعان أو لا، بناءً على أنَّ المنقَسِمَ إلى التَّصوُّرِ والتَّصديقِ؛ هو العِلْمُ الحادث الحصولي، لا مُطلَقُ العِلْمِ الشَّاملِ للحضوري والقديم؛ لأنَّ الانقسام إلى البديهي والكسبي إنَّما يجري في العِلْم الحصوليّ والعِلْم الحادِثِ ؛ دونَ العِلْم الحضوري والعِلْم القديم، وَهُوَ عِلْمُهُ تَعالى، فإنَّ العِلْمَ الحضوري بديهي ، وعِلْمُهُ تَعَالَى لا يُوصَفُ بِبَداهِةٍ وَلَا كَسب، وهذا ما اختاره جماعةٌ مِنَ الفُضلاء المحققين كالمصنفِ والسَّيِّدِ والقُطبِ الرَّازي في رسالتِهِ المؤلَّفة في تحقيقِ التَّصورِ والتَّصديقِ، والعلامة الشيرازي في درَّةِ النَّاحِ وشرح حكمةِ الإشراق، واختار الجلالُ الدَّوَّانيُّ في حاشية المتنِ التَّعميم فقال : هو مطلقُ الصُّورةِ الحاضرة عند المدرك ؛ سواء كانت عين ماهيته؛ وهو في التَّصوُّرِ بالكُنْهِ أو غيرها ؛ وهو في غيره، وسواء كانت تلكَ الصُّورةُ غيرَ الصُّورةِ الخارجيَّة؛ وهو في العِلْم الحصوليّ أو عينها وهو العِلْمُ الحضوري، وسواء كانت في ذاتِ المدركِ كما في علم النَّفْسِ بالكليَّاتِ، أو في آلاتها؛ كما في عليها بالمحسوسات، وسواء كانت عين المدركِ كما في عِلْم الباري تَعَالى شأنُهُ بذاتِهِ أو غيره كما في علمِهِ بِسلسلة الممكناتِ، وقد يخصُّ هَهُنا بالعلم الحصوليّ أو الحادثِ مُعلِّلاً بأنَّ الانقسام إلى البديهية والكسبيَّةِ إنَّما يجري فيهما، ولا حاجة إليه ؛ فإنَّ الانقسام يجري في المطلق، وإن لم يجرِ في كل نوع منه على أنَّهُ تخصيص اللَّفْظِ مِن غير ضرورة داعية إليه، مع أنَّ التَّعميم أنسبُ بقواعد الفنّ ا.هـ. وأشار بقولِهِ : فإِنَّ الانقسام ... إلخ؛ لدفع ما عساه يقالُ : إِنَّ التَّعميم لهذهِ الأفرادِ ينافيهِ التَّقسيم، وحَاصِلُ الجوابِ أَنَّهُ يجوز أن يكون المقسمُ مُطلقاً، وجريان الأقسام فيهِ لا يستلزم جريانها في كل نوع منه ؛ إذْ لا يلزمُ مِنَ انقسام المطلقِ انقسامُ أنواعِهِ كُلّها ، وإلا ؛ لزمَ في كلِّ تقسيم انقسامُ الشَّيء إلى نفْسِهِ وإلى غَيْرِهِ، والحقُّ مَا ذهب إليه الجماعةُ مِنَ التَّخصيص.
الدسوقي
واعلَمْ أنَّ العِلْمَ يُطلقُ على القواعد والضوابط، وعلى الملكة الحاصلة من مزاولة القواعدِ ويُطلقُ على الإدراك، وهو حقيقة في الثالث؛ لأنَّ العِلْمَ مصدر، وإطلاقه على الأوَّلَيْن مَجاز، ولا يصح إرادة واحدٍ منهما هُنَا ؛ لأنَّ العِلْمَ المنقسم للأقسام الآتية إنَّما هو العِلْمُ بمعنى الإدراك.
العطار
ذهَبَ إليه الجماعةُ مِنَ التَّخصيص، وقولُ الجلالِ : إِنَّ التَّعميم أنسبُ بقواعدِ الفنّ؛ يقالُ عليهِ : إِنَّ التَّعميم يرتكب بقدر الحاجة هذا، والفرق بين العِلْم الحصولي والحضوري أن يُقالَ : العِلْمُ بالأشياء يكون على وجهين؛ أحدهما بحصولِ صورها في نَفْسِ العالم أو في آلاتِها ويُسمَّى حصوليا ، والآخَرُ بِحضورها أنفسها عند ؛ العالم ؛ ويُسمَّى حضوريًّا، كَعِلمِنًا بذاتِنَا وبالصِّفاتِ القائمة بها؛ إذْ ليسَ فِيهِ ارتسام. بل هناك حضور المعلوم بحقيقتِهِ لَا بِمِثَالِهِ عندَ العَالِمِ، وهذا أقوى من الحصولي؛ ضرورةَ أنَّ انكِشَافَ شَيْءٍ عن آخَرَ لأجل حضوره عنده أقوَى مِنَ انكِشَافِهِ عندَهُ لأجل حضورِ مثالِهِ ،وصورتِهِ ومِمَّا ينبغي أن يُنيَّة عليهِ هَهُنا أَنَّهُم اختلفُوا في أنَّ العِلْمَ مِن مقولة الكيفِ أو الانفعال أو الإضافة ؛ وربَّما وقعَ التَّصريح في كلام من لا تحقيق عندَهُ بأَنَّهُ مِن مَقولة الفعل وَهُوَ وَهُمْ، قال أبو الفَتْح: ومنشأ هذا الاختلافِ أنَّه ليس حاصلاً قبل حصولِ الصُّورةِ في الذهن بداهة واتّفاقاً، وحاصل عنده بداهة واتّفاقاً، والحاصل معه أمورٌ ثلاثةُ الصُّورةُ الحاصِلَةُ، وقبول الذهن لها ؛ مِنَ المبدأ الفياض، وإضافة مخصوصةٌ بينَ العَالِمِ والمعلُوم ؛ فذهبَ بعضُهُم إلى أنَّ العِلْمَ هو الأوَّلُ؛ فيكون من مقولة الكيف، وبعضُهم إلى أَنَّهُ الثَّاني؛ فيكونُ مِن مقولة الانفعال، وبعضُهُم إلى أنَّهُ الثَّالِثُ؛ فيكونُ مِن مَقولة الإضافة، وأمَّا أَنَّهُ نَفْسُ حصولِ الصُّورة في الذهنِ ؛ فَلَمْ يَقُلْ بِهِ أحدٌ مِنهُم ، كما لا يَحْفَى على مَن تَتَبَّعَ
Introduction of the author: Knowledge is apprehension absolutely. al-Dassuqi said: His saying: Knowledge, i.e., temporal, because it is divided into the mentioned divisions. His saying: And it is apprehension absolutely, i.e., without restricting it to being apprehension of a single term, or apprehension of the occurrence of the relation or its non-occurrence. So what is meant is absolute apprehension. He restricted it with absoluteness only to make its division into what follows correct. For if what was meant by it were specifically the apprehension that the relation occurs or does not occur, as some of the usuliyyun said, or apprehension of the single term, the division would be invalid, because it would be a division of a thing into itself and another. al-'Attar said: His saying: Knowledge, and it is apprehension absolutely, i.e., whether it is with conviction or not, based on the fact that the thing divided into conceptualization and assent is temporal acquired knowledge, not absolute knowledge encompassing presential and eternal. Because the division into axiomatic and acquired only occurs in acquired knowledge and temporal knowledge, not in presential knowledge and eternal knowledge, which is His knowledge, may He be exalted. Indeed, presential knowledge is axiomatic, and His knowledge, may He be exalted, is not described as axiomatic or acquired. This is what a group of excellent investigators chose, such as the author, al-Sayyid, and Qutb al-Din al-Razi in his treatise compiled on the verification of conceptualization and assent, and the scholar al-Shirazi in Durrat al-Nah and Sharh Hikmat al-Ishraq. And al-Jalal al-Dawwani chose in his gloss on the text generalization and said: It is any present form at the perceiver, whether it is the essence of its quiddity—which is in conceptualization by essence—or other than it—which is in other than that—and whether that form is other than the external form—which is in acquired knowledge—or identical to it—which is presential knowledge—and whether it is in the essence of the perceiver, as in the soul's knowledge of universals, or in its instruments, as in our knowledge of sensibles, and whether it is identical to the perceiver, as in the knowledge of Allah, exalted be His status, of His essence, or other than it, as in His knowledge of the chain of contingents. And it may be specified here as acquired or temporal knowledge, adducing that the division into axiomatic and acquired only occurs in them. There is no need for it, because division occurs in the absolute even if it does not occur in every type of it, on the grounds that it is specification of the word without necessity calling for it, while generalization is more suitable to the rules of the art. End of his speech. And he indicated by his saying: For division... etc., to repel what might be said: that generalization of these individuals is inconsistent with the division. The upshot of the answer is that it is permissible for the thing divided to be absolute, and the running of the divisions in it does not necessitate their running in every type of it, since from the division of the absolute, the division of all its types does not follow. Otherwise, in every division there would be a division of a thing into itself and another. And the truth is what the group of specification went to. al-Dassuqi said: And know that 'ilm is applied to rules and principles, and to the faculty resulting from practicing the rules, and it is applied to apprehension. It is literal in the third, because 'ilm is a verbal noun, and its application to the first two is metaphorical. It is not valid to intend one of them here, because 'ilm that is divided into the following divisions is only 'ilm in the sense of apprehension. al-'Attar said: The group of specification went to it. And al-Jalal's statement that generalization is more suitable to the rules of the art is objected to by saying that generalization is undertaken to the extent of need. And the difference between acquired and presential knowledge is that knowledge of things is of two types: one by the obtaining of their forms in the soul of the knower or in its instruments, called acquired; the other by the presence of the things themselves to the knower, called presential, like our knowledge of our own essence and the attributes subsisting in it, for there is no impression there. Rather, there is a presence of the known thing in its true reality, not by its image, to the knower. And this is stronger than acquired knowledge, necessarily, because the disclosure of a thing to another due to its presence to it is stronger than its disclosure to it due to the presence of its image and form. And among what should be noted here is that they differed on whether knowledge is from the category of quality, or passion, or relation. And sometimes it is explicitly stated in the speech of someone without verification that it is from the category of action, which is a delusion. Abu al-Fath said: The origin of this difference is that it does not obtain before the obtaining of the form in the mind, axiomatically and by consensus, and it obtains with it, axiomatically and by consensus. What obtains with it are three matters: the obtained form, the acceptance of the mind for it from the bestowing principle, and a specific relation between the knower and the known. Some held that knowledge is the first, so it is from the category of quality; some held it is the second, so it is from the category of passion; and some held it is the third, so it is from the category of relation. As for it being the very obtaining of the form in the mind, none of them said it, as is not hidden from one who investigates.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's definition of 'ilm (knowledge) as 'absolute apprehension.' It begins by clarifying that 'ilm here refers to temporal (hadith) knowledge, because it is divided into tasawwur and tasdiq. The commentary emphasizes that the definition is unrestricted (mutlaq) to allow this division; if it were restricted to only singular apprehension or relational apprehension, the division would be invalid (dividing a thing into itself and another). The commentator then engages in a scholarly debate about whether 'ilm should be restricted to acquired (husuli) knowledge or whether it includes presential (huduri) and eternal (qadim) knowledge. One group restricts it, because division into axiomatic and acquired only applies to acquired/temporal knowledge. Al-Dawwani argues for generalization, defining 'ilm as any form present to the perceiver, regardless of type. The commentary presents a counter-argument that division of the absolute does not require division in every species, and concludes that the truth is with the restrictors. Next, al-Dassuqi notes that 'ilm is used in three senses: rules, faculty, and apprehension; here it means apprehension. Finally, al-'Attar explains the difference between acquired and presential knowledge: acquired is by mental representation, presential is by direct presence (like self-knowledge). Presential is stronger. The passage ends with a discussion of the ontological category of 'ilm: whether it is quality (kayf), passion (infi'al), or relation (idafa). Abu al-Fath is cited explaining that three things accompany the form: the form itself, the mind's acceptance, and a relation. Scholars differ on which is 'ilm.

Key Terms
العلم (al-ʿilm)
الإدراك (al-idrāk)
التصور (al-taṣawwur)
التصديق (al-taṣdīq)
الحصولي (al-ḥuṣūlī)
الحضوري (al-ḥuḍūrī)
القديم (al-qadīm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the commentator insist that the definition of 'ilm (knowledge) be 'absolute apprehension' (idrak mutlaq) rather than a restricted one? Use an example from Islamic sciences.
A) Because absolute apprehension includes both conceptualization and assent, allowing the division into tasawwur and tasdiq without dividing a thing into itself.
B) Because the author of the matn required it for grammatical reasons.
C) Because the logicians wanted to include divine knowledge only.
D) Because absolute apprehension excludes any form of judgment.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge must be defined without restriction to permit a valid logical division into conceptualization and assent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the commentator's reasoning, evaluate the following definition: 'Knowledge is the apprehension that a proposition is true.' Would this definition allow a valid division into tasawwur and tasdiq? Explain.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
advanced
10 min
The Scope of 'ilm: Acquired, Presential, or Eternal?
Debate on whether 'ilm includes presential/eternal or is restricted to acquired/temporal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions on whether 'ilm in mantiq includes presential and eternal knowledge or only acquired temporal knowledge.

Core Idea
Scholars debate whether 'ilm in logic includes all knowledge or only the acquired kind that can be divided into axiomatic and acquired.

After setting the definition, the commentators discuss whether 'ilm here is restricted to acquired temporal knowledge or includes presential and eternal knowledge. Two positions emerge: specification (takhṣīṣ) by a group, and generalization (taʿmīm) by al-Dawwani. This lesson walks through their arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions on the scope of 'ilm
The passage mentions one group that restricts 'ilm to acquired temporal knowledge (al-ʿilm al-ḥuṣūlī al-ḥādith) and another, represented by al-Dawwani, that generalizes it to any form present to the perceiver.
The restrictors argue that division into axiomatic/acquired only applies to acquired/temporal knowledge.
2
Understand al-Dawwani's generalization
Al-Dawwani defines 'ilm as any form present to the perceiver, whether it is the essence of the thing or a representation, and whether the presence is through representation or direct presence. This includes presential and divine knowledge.
He argues that this is more suitable to the rules of the art (qawāʿid al-fann).
3
Analyze the rebuttal
The commentator (al-Attar) presents a rebuttal: division of the absolute does not require division in every type. So even if 'ilm is defined absolutely, the fact that it can be divided into tasawwur and tasdiq does not mean that every type of 'ilm (e.g., presential) must be so divided. This defends the specification position.
4
Conclude which view is favored
Al-Attar states that the truth is with the group of specification, i.e., restricting 'ilm to acquired temporal knowledge for the purpose of this logical division.
He considers al-Dawwani's generalization unnecessary.

مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتنِ (العِلْمُ) وهو : الإدراكُ مُطلقاً
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : الْعِلْمُ أي : الحادثُ؛ لأنَّهُ المنقسم للأقسام المذكورة.
(قَوْلُهُ : وَهُوَ الْإِدْرَاكُ مُطْلَقَاً) أي: من غير تقييد له بكونه إدراك مفرد، أو إدراك وقوع الـ النسبة أو لا وقوعها، فالمراد مُطلقُ الإدراك، وإنَّما قيَّدَهُ بِالإطلاق؛ ليصح تقسيمُهُ لِمَا يأتي; إذْ لو كان المراد به خصوص إدراك أن النسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعةٍ كَما قاله بعض الأصولتين، أو إدراك المفرد؛ كان التقسيم باطلاً؛ لأنه تقسيم الشَّيء لِنَفْسِهِ ولغيره .
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ: العِلْمُ وَهُوَ : الْإِدْرَاكُ مُطْلَقَاً) أي: سواءٌ كان على وجه الإذعان أو لا، بناءً على أنَّ المنقَسِمَ إلى التَّصوُّرِ والتَّصديقِ؛ هو العِلْمُ الحادث الحصولي، لا مُطلَقُ العِلْمِ الشَّاملِ للحضوري والقديم؛ لأنَّ الانقسام إلى البديهي والكسبي إنَّما يجري في العِلْم الحصوليّ والعِلْم الحادِثِ ؛ دونَ العِلْم الحضوري والعِلْم القديم، وَهُوَ عِلْمُهُ تَعالى، فإنَّ العِلْمَ الحضوري بديهي ، وعِلْمُهُ تَعَالَى لا يُوصَفُ بِبَداهِةٍ وَلَا كَسب، وهذا ما اختاره جماعةٌ مِنَ الفُضلاء المحققين كالمصنفِ والسَّيِّدِ والقُطبِ الرَّازي في رسالتِهِ المؤلَّفة في تحقيقِ التَّصورِ والتَّصديقِ، والعلامة الشيرازي في درَّةِ النَّاحِ وشرح حكمةِ الإشراق، واختار الجلالُ الدَّوَّانيُّ في حاشية المتنِ التَّعميم فقال : هو مطلقُ الصُّورةِ الحاضرة عند المدرك ؛ سواء كانت عين ماهيته؛ وهو في التَّصوُّرِ بالكُنْهِ أو غيرها ؛ وهو في غيره، وسواء كانت تلكَ الصُّورةُ غيرَ الصُّورةِ الخارجيَّة؛ وهو في العِلْم الحصوليّ أو عينها وهو العِلْمُ الحضوري، وسواء كانت في ذاتِ المدركِ كما في علم النَّفْسِ بالكليَّاتِ، أو في آلاتها؛ كما في عليها بالمحسوسات، وسواء كانت عين المدركِ كما في عِلْم الباري تَعَالى شأنُهُ بذاتِهِ أو غيره كما في علمِهِ بِسلسلة الممكناتِ، وقد يخصُّ هَهُنا بالعلم الحصوليّ أو الحادثِ مُعلِّلاً بأنَّ الانقسام إلى البديهية والكسبيَّةِ إنَّما يجري فيهما، ولا حاجة إليه ؛ فإنَّ الانقسام يجري في المطلق، وإن لم يجرِ في كل نوع منه على أنَّهُ تخصيص اللَّفْظِ مِن غير ضرورة داعية إليه، مع أنَّ التَّعميم أنسبُ بقواعد الفنّ ا.هـ. وأشار بقولِهِ : فإِنَّ الانقسام ... إلخ؛ لدفع ما عساه يقالُ : إِنَّ التَّعميم لهذهِ الأفرادِ ينافيهِ التَّقسيم، وحَاصِلُ الجوابِ أَنَّهُ يجوز أن يكون المقسمُ مُطلقاً، وجريان الأقسام فيهِ لا يستلزم جريانها في كل نوع منه ؛ إذْ لا يلزمُ مِنَ انقسام المطلقِ انقسامُ أنواعِهِ كُلّها ، وإلا ؛ لزمَ في كلِّ تقسيم انقسامُ الشَّيء إلى نفْسِهِ وإلى غَيْرِهِ، والحقُّ مَا ذهب إليه الجماعةُ مِنَ التَّخصيص.
الدسوقي
واعلَمْ أنَّ العِلْمَ يُطلقُ على القواعد والضوابط، وعلى الملكة الحاصلة من مزاولة القواعدِ ويُطلقُ على الإدراك، وهو حقيقة في الثالث؛ لأنَّ العِلْمَ مصدر، وإطلاقه على الأوَّلَيْن مَجاز، ولا يصح إرادة واحدٍ منهما هُنَا ؛ لأنَّ العِلْمَ المنقسم للأقسام الآتية إنَّما هو العِلْمُ بمعنى الإدراك.
العطار
ذهَبَ إليه الجماعةُ مِنَ التَّخصيص، وقولُ الجلالِ : إِنَّ التَّعميم أنسبُ بقواعدِ الفنّ؛ يقالُ عليهِ : إِنَّ التَّعميم يرتكب بقدر الحاجة هذا، والفرق بين العِلْم الحصولي والحضوري أن يُقالَ : العِلْمُ بالأشياء يكون على وجهين؛ أحدهما بحصولِ صورها في نَفْسِ العالم أو في آلاتِها ويُسمَّى حصوليا ، والآخَرُ بِحضورها أنفسها عند ؛ العالم ؛ ويُسمَّى حضوريًّا، كَعِلمِنًا بذاتِنَا وبالصِّفاتِ القائمة بها؛ إذْ ليسَ فِيهِ ارتسام. بل هناك حضور المعلوم بحقيقتِهِ لَا بِمِثَالِهِ عندَ العَالِمِ، وهذا أقوى من الحصولي؛ ضرورةَ أنَّ انكِشَافَ شَيْءٍ عن آخَرَ لأجل حضوره عنده أقوَى مِنَ انكِشَافِهِ عندَهُ لأجل حضورِ مثالِهِ ،وصورتِهِ ومِمَّا ينبغي أن يُنيَّة عليهِ هَهُنا أَنَّهُم اختلفُوا في أنَّ العِلْمَ مِن مقولة الكيفِ أو الانفعال أو الإضافة ؛ وربَّما وقعَ التَّصريح في كلام من لا تحقيق عندَهُ بأَنَّهُ مِن مَقولة الفعل وَهُوَ وَهُمْ، قال أبو الفَتْح: ومنشأ هذا الاختلافِ أنَّه ليس حاصلاً قبل حصولِ الصُّورةِ في الذهن بداهة واتّفاقاً، وحاصل عنده بداهة واتّفاقاً، والحاصل معه أمورٌ ثلاثةُ الصُّورةُ الحاصِلَةُ، وقبول الذهن لها ؛ مِنَ المبدأ الفياض، وإضافة مخصوصةٌ بينَ العَالِمِ والمعلُوم ؛ فذهبَ بعضُهُم إلى أنَّ العِلْمَ هو الأوَّلُ؛ فيكون من مقولة الكيف، وبعضُهم إلى أَنَّهُ الثَّاني؛ فيكونُ مِن مقولة الانفعال، وبعضُهُم إلى أنَّهُ الثَّالِثُ؛ فيكونُ مِن مَقولة الإضافة، وأمَّا أَنَّهُ نَفْسُ حصولِ الصُّورة في الذهنِ ؛ فَلَمْ يَقُلْ بِهِ أحدٌ مِنهُم ، كما لا يَحْفَى على مَن تَتَبَّعَ
Introduction of the author: Knowledge is apprehension absolutely. al-Dassuqi said: His saying: Knowledge, i.e., temporal, because it is divided into the mentioned divisions. His saying: And it is apprehension absolutely, i.e., without restricting it to being apprehension of a single term, or apprehension of the occurrence of the relation or its non-occurrence. So what is meant is absolute apprehension. He restricted it with absoluteness only to make its division into what follows correct. For if what was meant by it were specifically the apprehension that the relation occurs or does not occur, as some of the usuliyyun said, or apprehension of the single term, the division would be invalid, because it would be a division of a thing into itself and another. al-'Attar said: His saying: Knowledge, and it is apprehension absolutely, i.e., whether it is with conviction or not, based on the fact that the thing divided into conceptualization and assent is temporal acquired knowledge, not absolute knowledge encompassing presential and eternal. Because the division into axiomatic and acquired only occurs in acquired knowledge and temporal knowledge, not in presential knowledge and eternal knowledge, which is His knowledge, may He be exalted. Indeed, presential knowledge is axiomatic, and His knowledge, may He be exalted, is not described as axiomatic or acquired. This is what a group of excellent investigators chose, such as the author, al-Sayyid, and Qutb al-Din al-Razi in his treatise compiled on the verification of conceptualization and assent, and the scholar al-Shirazi in Durrat al-Nah and Sharh Hikmat al-Ishraq. And al-Jalal al-Dawwani chose in his gloss on the text generalization and said: It is any present form at the perceiver, whether it is the essence of its quiddity—which is in conceptualization by essence—or other than it—which is in other than that—and whether that form is other than the external form—which is in acquired knowledge—or identical to it—which is presential knowledge—and whether it is in the essence of the perceiver, as in the soul's knowledge of universals, or in its instruments, as in our knowledge of sensibles, and whether it is identical to the perceiver, as in the knowledge of Allah, exalted be His status, of His essence, or other than it, as in His knowledge of the chain of contingents. And it may be specified here as acquired or temporal knowledge, adducing that the division into axiomatic and acquired only occurs in them. There is no need for it, because division occurs in the absolute even if it does not occur in every type of it, on the grounds that it is specification of the word without necessity calling for it, while generalization is more suitable to the rules of the art. End of his speech. And he indicated by his saying: For division... etc., to repel what might be said: that generalization of these individuals is inconsistent with the division. The upshot of the answer is that it is permissible for the thing divided to be absolute, and the running of the divisions in it does not necessitate their running in every type of it, since from the division of the absolute, the division of all its types does not follow. Otherwise, in every division there would be a division of a thing into itself and another. And the truth is what the group of specification went to. al-Dassuqi said: And know that 'ilm is applied to rules and principles, and to the faculty resulting from practicing the rules, and it is applied to apprehension. It is literal in the third, because 'ilm is a verbal noun, and its application to the first two is metaphorical. It is not valid to intend one of them here, because 'ilm that is divided into the following divisions is only 'ilm in the sense of apprehension. al-'Attar said: The group of specification went to it. And al-Jalal's statement that generalization is more suitable to the rules of the art is objected to by saying that generalization is undertaken to the extent of need. And the difference between acquired and presential knowledge is that knowledge of things is of two types: one by the obtaining of their forms in the soul of the knower or in its instruments, called acquired; the other by the presence of the things themselves to the knower, called presential, like our knowledge of our own essence and the attributes subsisting in it, for there is no impression there. Rather, there is a presence of the known thing in its true reality, not by its image, to the knower. And this is stronger than acquired knowledge, necessarily, because the disclosure of a thing to another due to its presence to it is stronger than its disclosure to it due to the presence of its image and form. And among what should be noted here is that they differed on whether knowledge is from the category of quality, or passion, or relation. And sometimes it is explicitly stated in the speech of someone without verification that it is from the category of action, which is a delusion. Abu al-Fath said: The origin of this difference is that it does not obtain before the obtaining of the form in the mind, axiomatically and by consensus, and it obtains with it, axiomatically and by consensus. What obtains with it are three matters: the obtained form, the acceptance of the mind for it from the bestowing principle, and a specific relation between the knower and the known. Some held that knowledge is the first, so it is from the category of quality; some held it is the second, so it is from the category of passion; and some held it is the third, so it is from the category of relation. As for it being the very obtaining of the form in the mind, none of them said it, as is not hidden from one who investigates.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's definition of 'ilm (knowledge) as 'absolute apprehension.' It begins by clarifying that 'ilm here refers to temporal (hadith) knowledge, because it is divided into tasawwur and tasdiq. The commentary emphasizes that the definition is unrestricted (mutlaq) to allow this division; if it were restricted to only singular apprehension or relational apprehension, the division would be invalid (dividing a thing into itself and another). The commentator then engages in a scholarly debate about whether 'ilm should be restricted to acquired (husuli) knowledge or whether it includes presential (huduri) and eternal (qadim) knowledge. One group restricts it, because division into axiomatic and acquired only applies to acquired/temporal knowledge. Al-Dawwani argues for generalization, defining 'ilm as any form present to the perceiver, regardless of type. The commentary presents a counter-argument that division of the absolute does not require division in every species, and concludes that the truth is with the restrictors. Next, al-Dassuqi notes that 'ilm is used in three senses: rules, faculty, and apprehension; here it means apprehension. Finally, al-'Attar explains the difference between acquired and presential knowledge: acquired is by mental representation, presential is by direct presence (like self-knowledge). Presential is stronger. The passage ends with a discussion of the ontological category of 'ilm: whether it is quality (kayf), passion (infi'al), or relation (idafa). Abu al-Fath is cited explaining that three things accompany the form: the form itself, the mind's acceptance, and a relation. Scholars differ on which is 'ilm.

الإدراك (al-idrāk)

الحضوري (al-ḥuḍūrī)

Checkpoint
Which of the following best represents the position of the group that specifies 'ilm in this passage?
A) 'Ilm includes presential and eternal knowledge.
B) 'Ilm is restricted to acquired temporal knowledge.
C) 'Ilm is any form present to the perceiver.
D) 'Ilm is the same as the soul's self-awareness.

Key Takeaway
The predominant view in this commentary is that 'ilm in logic is restricted to acquired temporal knowledge, which alone divides into axiomatic and acquired.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
advanced
8 min
The Ontological Category of Knowledge: Quality, Passion, or Relation?
Discussion on the ontological category of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three positions on the ontological category of knowledge and the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
Knowledge is not a single category; scholars debate whether it is a quality, a passion, or a relation.

The passage concludes with a discussion of the ontological status of knowledge. When the form is present in the mind, three things occur: the form itself, the mind's acceptance, and a relation between knower and known. Scholars differ on which of these is knowledge. This lesson breaks down the debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three components that accompany the mental form
Abu al-Fath identifies three things: the form itself (al-ṣūra al-ḥāṣila), the mind's acceptance of it (qabūl al-dhihn li-hā), and a specific relation (iḍāfa makhṣūṣa) between knower and known.
2
Map each component to an Aristotelian category
The form is a quality (kayf), the acceptance is a passion (infiʿāl), and the relation is an addition (iḍāfa).
These correspond to categories in the ten categories.
3
Understand why scholars differ
Some hold that knowledge is the form (quality), some say it is the acceptance (passion), some say it is the relation. No one says it is the mere obtaining of the form (the act of obtaining).
4
Appreciate the implication
This debate shows that knowledge is a complex phenomenon, and different philosophical commitments lead to different ontological classifications.

(قَوْلُهُ : وَهُوَ الْإِدْرَاكُ مُطْلَقَاً) أي: من غير تقييد له بكونه إدراك مفرد، أو إدراك وقوع الـ النسبة أو لا وقوعها، فالمراد مُطلقُ الإدراك، وإنَّما قيَّدَهُ بِالإطلاق؛ ليصح تقسيمُهُ لِمَا يأتي; إذْ لو كان المراد به خصوص إدراك أن النسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعةٍ كَما قاله بعض الأصولتين، أو إدراك المفرد؛ كان التقسيم باطلاً؛ لأنه تقسيم الشَّيء لِنَفْسِهِ ولغيره .
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ: العِلْمُ وَهُوَ : الْإِدْرَاكُ مُطْلَقَاً) أي: سواءٌ كان على وجه الإذعان أو لا، بناءً على أنَّ المنقَسِمَ إلى التَّصوُّرِ والتَّصديقِ؛ هو العِلْمُ الحادث الحصولي، لا مُطلَقُ العِلْمِ الشَّاملِ للحضوري والقديم؛ لأنَّ الانقسام إلى البديهي والكسبي إنَّما يجري في العِلْم الحصوليّ والعِلْم الحادِثِ ؛ دونَ العِلْم الحضوري والعِلْم القديم، وَهُوَ عِلْمُهُ تَعالى، فإنَّ العِلْمَ الحضوري بديهي ، وعِلْمُهُ تَعَالَى لا يُوصَفُ بِبَداهِةٍ وَلَا كَسب، وهذا ما اختاره جماعةٌ مِنَ الفُضلاء المحققين كالمصنفِ والسَّيِّدِ والقُطبِ الرَّازي في رسالتِهِ المؤلَّفة في تحقيقِ التَّصورِ والتَّصديقِ، والعلامة الشيرازي في درَّةِ النَّاحِ وشرح حكمةِ الإشراق، واختار الجلالُ الدَّوَّانيُّ في حاشية المتنِ التَّعميم فقال : هو مطلقُ الصُّورةِ الحاضرة عند المدرك ؛ سواء كانت عين ماهيته؛ وهو في التَّصوُّرِ بالكُنْهِ أو غيرها ؛ وهو في غيره، وسواء كانت تلكَ الصُّورةُ غيرَ الصُّورةِ الخارجيَّة؛ وهو في العِلْم الحصوليّ أو عينها وهو العِلْمُ الحضوري، وسواء كانت في ذاتِ المدركِ كما في علم النَّفْسِ بالكليَّاتِ، أو في آلاتها؛ كما في عليها بالمحسوسات، وسواء كانت عين المدركِ كما في عِلْم الباري تَعَالى شأنُهُ بذاتِهِ أو غيره كما في علمِهِ بِسلسلة الممكناتِ، وقد يخصُّ هَهُنا بالعلم الحصوليّ أو الحادثِ مُعلِّلاً بأنَّ الانقسام إلى البديهية والكسبيَّةِ إنَّما يجري فيهما، ولا حاجة إليه ؛ فإنَّ الانقسام يجري في المطلق، وإن لم يجرِ في كل نوع منه على أنَّهُ تخصيص اللَّفْظِ مِن غير ضرورة داعية إليه، مع أنَّ التَّعميم أنسبُ بقواعد الفنّ ا.هـ. وأشار بقولِهِ : فإِنَّ الانقسام ... إلخ؛ لدفع ما عساه يقالُ : إِنَّ التَّعميم لهذهِ الأفرادِ ينافيهِ التَّقسيم، وحَاصِلُ الجوابِ أَنَّهُ يجوز أن يكون المقسمُ مُطلقاً، وجريان الأقسام فيهِ لا يستلزم جريانها في كل نوع منه ؛ إذْ لا يلزمُ مِنَ انقسام المطلقِ انقسامُ أنواعِهِ كُلّها ، وإلا ؛ لزمَ في كلِّ تقسيم انقسامُ الشَّيء إلى نفْسِهِ وإلى غَيْرِهِ، والحقُّ مَا ذهب إليه الجماعةُ مِنَ التَّخصيص.
الدسوقي
واعلَمْ أنَّ العِلْمَ يُطلقُ على القواعد والضوابط، وعلى الملكة الحاصلة من مزاولة القواعدِ ويُطلقُ على الإدراك، وهو حقيقة في الثالث؛ لأنَّ العِلْمَ مصدر، وإطلاقه على الأوَّلَيْن مَجاز، ولا يصح إرادة واحدٍ منهما هُنَا ؛ لأنَّ العِلْمَ المنقسم للأقسام الآتية إنَّما هو العِلْمُ بمعنى الإدراك.
العطار
ذهَبَ إليه الجماعةُ مِنَ التَّخصيص، وقولُ الجلالِ : إِنَّ التَّعميم أنسبُ بقواعدِ الفنّ؛ يقالُ عليهِ : إِنَّ التَّعميم يرتكب بقدر الحاجة هذا، والفرق بين العِلْم الحصولي والحضوري أن يُقالَ : العِلْمُ بالأشياء يكون على وجهين؛ أحدهما بحصولِ صورها في نَفْسِ العالم أو في آلاتِها ويُسمَّى حصوليا ، والآخَرُ بِحضورها أنفسها عند ؛ العالم ؛ ويُسمَّى حضوريًّا، كَعِلمِنًا بذاتِنَا وبالصِّفاتِ القائمة بها؛ إذْ ليسَ فِيهِ ارتسام. بل هناك حضور المعلوم بحقيقتِهِ لَا بِمِثَالِهِ عندَ العَالِمِ، وهذا أقوى من الحصولي؛ ضرورةَ أنَّ انكِشَافَ شَيْءٍ عن آخَرَ لأجل حضوره عنده أقوَى مِنَ انكِشَافِهِ عندَهُ لأجل حضورِ مثالِهِ ،وصورتِهِ ومِمَّا ينبغي أن يُنيَّة عليهِ هَهُنا أَنَّهُم اختلفُوا في أنَّ العِلْمَ مِن مقولة الكيفِ أو الانفعال أو الإضافة ؛ وربَّما وقعَ التَّصريح في كلام من لا تحقيق عندَهُ بأَنَّهُ مِن مَقولة الفعل وَهُوَ وَهُمْ، قال أبو الفَتْح: ومنشأ هذا الاختلافِ أنَّه ليس حاصلاً قبل حصولِ الصُّورةِ في الذهن بداهة واتّفاقاً، وحاصل عنده بداهة واتّفاقاً، والحاصل معه أمورٌ ثلاثةُ الصُّورةُ الحاصِلَةُ، وقبول الذهن لها ؛ مِنَ المبدأ الفياض، وإضافة مخصوصةٌ بينَ العَالِمِ والمعلُوم ؛ فذهبَ بعضُهُم إلى أنَّ العِلْمَ هو الأوَّلُ؛ فيكون من مقولة الكيف، وبعضُهم إلى أَنَّهُ الثَّاني؛ فيكونُ مِن مقولة الانفعال، وبعضُهُم إلى أنَّهُ الثَّالِثُ؛ فيكونُ مِن مَقولة الإضافة، وأمَّا أَنَّهُ نَفْسُ حصولِ الصُّورة في الذهنِ ؛ فَلَمْ يَقُلْ بِهِ أحدٌ مِنهُم ، كما لا يَحْفَى على مَن تَتَبَّعَ
Introduction of the author: Knowledge is apprehension absolutely. al-Dassuqi said: His saying: Knowledge, i.e., temporal, because it is divided into the mentioned divisions. His saying: And it is apprehension absolutely, i.e., without restricting it to being apprehension of a single term, or apprehension of the occurrence of the relation or its non-occurrence. So what is meant is absolute apprehension. He restricted it with absoluteness only to make its division into what follows correct. For if what was meant by it were specifically the apprehension that the relation occurs or does not occur, as some of the usuliyyun said, or apprehension of the single term, the division would be invalid, because it would be a division of a thing into itself and another. al-'Attar said: His saying: Knowledge, and it is apprehension absolutely, i.e., whether it is with conviction or not, based on the fact that the thing divided into conceptualization and assent is temporal acquired knowledge, not absolute knowledge encompassing presential and eternal. Because the division into axiomatic and acquired only occurs in acquired knowledge and temporal knowledge, not in presential knowledge and eternal knowledge, which is His knowledge, may He be exalted. Indeed, presential knowledge is axiomatic, and His knowledge, may He be exalted, is not described as axiomatic or acquired. This is what a group of excellent investigators chose, such as the author, al-Sayyid, and Qutb al-Din al-Razi in his treatise compiled on the verification of conceptualization and assent, and the scholar al-Shirazi in Durrat al-Nah and Sharh Hikmat al-Ishraq. And al-Jalal al-Dawwani chose in his gloss on the text generalization and said: It is any present form at the perceiver, whether it is the essence of its quiddity—which is in conceptualization by essence—or other than it—which is in other than that—and whether that form is other than the external form—which is in acquired knowledge—or identical to it—which is presential knowledge—and whether it is in the essence of the perceiver, as in the soul's knowledge of universals, or in its instruments, as in our knowledge of sensibles, and whether it is identical to the perceiver, as in the knowledge of Allah, exalted be His status, of His essence, or other than it, as in His knowledge of the chain of contingents. And it may be specified here as acquired or temporal knowledge, adducing that the division into axiomatic and acquired only occurs in them. There is no need for it, because division occurs in the absolute even if it does not occur in every type of it, on the grounds that it is specification of the word without necessity calling for it, while generalization is more suitable to the rules of the art. End of his speech. And he indicated by his saying: For division... etc., to repel what might be said: that generalization of these individuals is inconsistent with the division. The upshot of the answer is that it is permissible for the thing divided to be absolute, and the running of the divisions in it does not necessitate their running in every type of it, since from the division of the absolute, the division of all its types does not follow. Otherwise, in every division there would be a division of a thing into itself and another. And the truth is what the group of specification went to. al-Dassuqi said: And know that 'ilm is applied to rules and principles, and to the faculty resulting from practicing the rules, and it is applied to apprehension. It is literal in the third, because 'ilm is a verbal noun, and its application to the first two is metaphorical. It is not valid to intend one of them here, because 'ilm that is divided into the following divisions is only 'ilm in the sense of apprehension. al-'Attar said: The group of specification went to it. And al-Jalal's statement that generalization is more suitable to the rules of the art is objected to by saying that generalization is undertaken to the extent of need. And the difference between acquired and presential knowledge is that knowledge of things is of two types: one by the obtaining of their forms in the soul of the knower or in its instruments, called acquired; the other by the presence of the things themselves to the knower, called presential, like our knowledge of our own essence and the attributes subsisting in it, for there is no impression there. Rather, there is a presence of the known thing in its true reality, not by its image, to the knower. And this is stronger than acquired knowledge, necessarily, because the disclosure of a thing to another due to its presence to it is stronger than its disclosure to it due to the presence of its image and form. And among what should be noted here is that they differed on whether knowledge is from the category of quality, or passion, or relation. And sometimes it is explicitly stated in the speech of someone without verification that it is from the category of action, which is a delusion. Abu al-Fath said: The origin of this difference is that it does not obtain before the obtaining of the form in the mind, axiomatically and by consensus, and it obtains with it, axiomatically and by consensus. What obtains with it are three matters: the obtained form, the acceptance of the mind for it from the bestowing principle, and a specific relation between the knower and the known. Some held that knowledge is the first, so it is from the category of quality; some held it is the second, so it is from the category of passion; and some held it is the third, so it is from the category of relation. As for it being the very obtaining of the form in the mind, none of them said it, as is not hidden from one who investigates.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's definition of 'ilm (knowledge) as 'absolute apprehension.' It begins by clarifying that 'ilm here refers to temporal (hadith) knowledge, because it is divided into tasawwur and tasdiq. The commentary emphasizes that the definition is unrestricted (mutlaq) to allow this division; if it were restricted to only singular apprehension or relational apprehension, the division would be invalid (dividing a thing into itself and another). The commentator then engages in a scholarly debate about whether 'ilm should be restricted to acquired (husuli) knowledge or whether it includes presential (huduri) and eternal (qadim) knowledge. One group restricts it, because division into axiomatic and acquired only applies to acquired/temporal knowledge. Al-Dawwani argues for generalization, defining 'ilm as any form present to the perceiver, regardless of type. The commentary presents a counter-argument that division of the absolute does not require division in every species, and concludes that the truth is with the restrictors. Next, al-Dassuqi notes that 'ilm is used in three senses: rules, faculty, and apprehension; here it means apprehension. Finally, al-'Attar explains the difference between acquired and presential knowledge: acquired is by mental representation, presential is by direct presence (like self-knowledge). Presential is stronger. The passage ends with a discussion of the ontological category of 'ilm: whether it is quality (kayf), passion (infi'al), or relation (idafa). Abu al-Fath is cited explaining that three things accompany the form: the form itself, the mind's acceptance, and a relation. Scholars differ on which is 'ilm.

Key Terms
العلم (al-ʿilm)
الإدراك (al-idrāk)
التصور (al-taṣawwur)
التصديق (al-taṣdīq)
الحصولي (al-ḥuṣūlī)
الحضوري (al-ḥuḍūrī)
القديم (al-qadīm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu al-Fath, which of the following is NOT one of the three things that accompany the obtaining of the mental form?
A) The form itself.
B) The mind's acceptance.
C) The relation between knower and known.
D) The act of obtaining the form.

Key Takeaway
The ontological category of knowledge is debated among scholars, with positions inclining toward quality, passion, or relation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If someone defines knowledge as 'the mind's acceptance of the form from the active intellect,' which ontological category would that correspond to according to the passage? Explain your reasoning.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
beginner
5 min
The Two Doors of Knowledge: Husuli and Huduri
Al-'Attar explains the distinction between knowledge by representation and knowledge by presence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between husuli and huduri knowledge and identify the defining characteristic of each.

Core Idea
Knowledge is either through representation or direct presence; the latter is more powerful.

Al-'Attar provides a clear definitional distinction between two fundamental types of knowledge. Understanding this distinction is crucial for later discussions in Islamic epistemology, especially regarding self-knowledge and divine knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Look for the two 'وجوه' (aspects) mentioned in the passage. What are they called? One is 'حصولي' (husuli) and the other is 'حضوري' (huduri).
2
Understand the mechanism
For husuli, what 'occurs' (يحصل)? It is the images (صور) of things in the soul or its instruments. For huduri, what is 'present' (يحضر)? It is the things themselves (أنفسها) to the knower.
3
Locate the example
Find the example of huduri knowledge given. It is our knowledge of our own essence (ذات) and the attributes subsisting in it. There is no representation (ارتسام) here.
This example is important because it shows a direct, unmediated awareness.
4
Grasp the comparative strength
Why does al-'Attar say huduri is stronger (أقوى)? Because the disclosure (انكشاف) of a thing due to its own presence is more complete than disclosure through a likeness or image.
The reasoning is that presence is a more intimate and direct mode of knowledge.
5
Summarize in your own words
Rephrase the distinction without using the same Arabic terms. For example: 'One type of knowledge works by having a copy of the object in the mind; the other type is when the object itself is directly present to the knower.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفرق بين العِلْم الحصولي والحضوري أن يُقالَ : العِلْمُ بالأشياء يكون على وجهين؛ أحدهما بحصولِ صورها في نَفْسِ العالم أو في آلاتِها ويُسمَّى حصوليا ، والآخَرُ بِحضورها أنفسها عند العالم ؛ ويُسمَّى حضوريًّا، كَعِلمِنًا بذاتِنَا وبالصِّفاتِ القائمة بها؛ إذْ ليسَ فِيهِ ارتسام. بل هناك حضور المعلوم بحقيقتِهِ لَا بِمِثَالِهِ عندَ العَالِمِ، وهذا أقوى من الحصولي؛ ضرورةَ أنَّ انكِشَافَ شَيْءٍ عن آخَرَ لأجل حضوره عنده أقوَى مِنَ انكِشَافِهِ عندَهُ لأجل حضورِ مثالِهِ ،وصورتِهِ
And the difference between conceptual (husuli) and intuitive (huduri) knowledge is that it is said: knowledge of things is of two types: one is by the occurrence (husul) of their images in the soul of the knower or in its instruments, and it is called husuli; and the other is by the presence (hudur) of the things themselves to the knower, and it is called huduri, like our knowledge of our own essence and of the attributes subsisting in it — for there is no representation (irtisam) in it. Rather, there is the presence of the known thing in its reality, not by its likeness, to the knower. And this is stronger than husuli, necessarily because the disclosure of a thing to another due to its presence to it is stronger than its disclosure due to the presence of its likeness and image.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a definitional explanation by al-'Attar of the two types of knowledge: al-'ilm al-husuli (conceptual knowledge) and al-'ilm al-huduri (intuitive knowledge). He defines husuli knowledge as knowledge attained through the occurrence (husul) of images or forms of things in the soul or its faculties (like the senses). In contrast, huduri knowledge is when the thing itself is present to the knower without any intermediary representation. The example given is our knowledge of our own self (dhat) and its attributes, which is direct and not through an image. Al-'Attar then states that huduri knowledge is stronger (aqwa) because the disclosure (inkishaf) of something due to its own presence is more complete than disclosure through a likeness or image. This guards against the misunderstanding that all knowledge is representational.

Key Terms
العلم الحصولي
العلم الحضوري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of knowledge is exemplified by our knowledge of our own self?
A) Conceptual knowledge (husuli)
B) Intuitive knowledge (huduri)
C) Both equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The fundamental division of knowledge into representational (husuli) and presential (huduri) is a key epistemological distinction in Islamic thought.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether the following is husuli or huduri knowledge: 'I know that the Kaaba is in Mecca because I have seen a picture of it.' Explain your reasoning.
?
Give an example from your own experience of huduri knowledge that is not mediated by an image.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

The Logicians' Definition of Tasdiq and the Theologians' Dispute
Al-Dasuqi defines tasdiq and contrasts logician and theologian views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify what counts as tasdiq for logicians and contrast it with the theologians' definition.

Core Idea
Tasdiq for logicians includes certainty, opinion, ignorance, and taqlid—only doubt and illusion are excluded.

In this passage, al-Dasuqi unpacks the definition of tasdiq (assent) from the matn. He explains that for logicians, any perception of a proposition with certainty or opinion qualifies as tasdiq, even if that perception is wrong or blindly followed. He then contrasts this with the theologians, who restrict tasdiq to certain knowledge based on proof and define it as an inner speech of affirmation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the scope of logic versus theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms in the definition
What does 'idh'an' and 'nisba' mean according to al-Dasuqi? Recognize that 'idh'an' is perception with juzm or zann, and 'nisba' is the proposition or relation.
2
List the kinds of perception that count as tasdiq for logicians
Yaqin (certainty corresponding to reality), jahl murakkab (certainty not corresponding), zann (preponderant opinion), and taqlid (certainty that can be shaken).
All involve juzm or zann.
3
Identify what is excluded from tasdiq for logicians
Wahm (illusion) and shakk (doubt) are excluded because they lack juzm and zann.
4
Compare with the theologians' definition
Theologians define 'ilm as i'tiqad jazim mutabiq li-al-waqi' an dalil. They consider only yaqin as knowledge; zann, jahl, taqlid, shakk, wahm are not 'ilm. Their tasdiq is a psychological speech (kalam nafsani): 'I have believed and affirmed'.
5
Understand the implications of the difference
The logicians' tasdiq is epistemic (any judgment), while the theologians' is performative. This affects how each discipline defines its subject matter.

مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتن (إِنْ كَانَ إِذْعَاناً للنِّسْبَةِ) الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : إِنْ كَانَ إِذْعَانَا لِلنِّسْبَةِ) أي : إدراكاً على وجه الجزم أو الظَّنِّ؛ أي: إنْ كانَ إدراكاً؛ لوقوعِهَا أوْ لَا ،وقوعِها واللَّامُ في قوله : للنّسبة؛ زائدةٌ لِلتَّقوية؛ أي: إن كان إذعان نسبة؛ أي إدراكاً لها من حيث إنَّها واقعة أو ليست بواقعة؛ سواء كانَ ذلك الإدراك راجحاً وهو الظَّنُّ، أو جازماً غير مطابق للواقع وهو الجهل، أو مُطابقاً للواقع وَلَا يقبلُ التَّغيُّرَ وهو اليقين، أو يقبلُ التَّغير بتشكيكِ مشكك، وهو التَّقليد، فكلَّ مِنَ الظَّنِّ والجهل المركَبِ واليقين والتّقليد؛ تصديق عند المناطقة؛ لإنَّهُ إدراكُ وقوع النِّسبةِ أوْ لَا وَقوعِهَا على وجه الجزم أو الظَّنِّ، وهو شامل لما ذكر، وأمَّا إدراك وقوعِهَا أوْ لَا وقوعِها على وجهِ الوهم أو الشَّكِّ؛ فَلَا يُسمَّى تصديقاً ؛ لأنَّهُ لا جزمَ وَلَا ظَنَّ عندَ الشَّاكُ والمتوهم ، وأمَّا المتكلمونَ؛ فَلَا يجعلون الظَّنَّ، والجهل، والتَّقليد ، والشَّلَّ، والوهم مِنَ العِلْمِ، بل هِيَ مُقابلةٌ له؛ لأنَّ العِلْمَ عندَهُم الاعتقاد الجازم المطابق للواقع عن دليل، والعِلْمَ عندهم غيرُ المعلوم، فالتَّصديقُ عندَهم مُقابل لِلتَّصديقِ عَندَ المناطقة؛ لأنَّ التصديق عندَ المناطقةِ مِنْ قبيل العِلْم والمعرفة، وعند المتكلمين كلام نفساني يرجعُ لقول نفْسِ المصدِّقِ : آمنْتُ وَصدَّقْتُ ؛ فَلِهذا يعرّفونَهُ بأَنَّهُ حديثُ النَّفْسِ التَّابِعُ لِلمعرفة .
Introduction of the author: 'If it is an assent to the proposition.' Al-Dasuqi: His statement: 'If it is an assent to the proposition' meaning: a perception with certainty or opinion; i.e., if it is a perception of its occurrence or non-occurrence, and the lam in his statement 'to the proposition' is extra for emphasis; i.e., if it is an assent to a proposition, i.e., a perception of it in terms of it being actual or not actual; whether that perception is preponderant, which is opinion, or certain but not corresponding to reality, which is ignorance, or corresponding to reality and not admitting change, which is certainty, or admitting change by the skepticism of a skeptic, which is taqlid. So all of opinion, compound ignorance, certainty, and taqlid are tasdiq according to the logicians, because it is a perception of the occurrence or non-occurrence of the proposition with certainty or opinion, and it includes what was mentioned. As for perceiving the occurrence or non-occurrence of the proposition in the manner of illusion (wahm) or doubt (shakk), it is not called tasdiq, because there is no certainty or opinion for the doubter and the deluded. As for the theologians, they do not consider opinion, ignorance, taqlid, doubt, and illusion as knowledge, but rather they are opposed to it, because knowledge according to them is firm belief corresponding to reality based on proof, and knowledge according to them is other than the known. Thus, tasdiq according to them is opposite to tasdiq according to the logicians; because tasdiq according to the logicians is of the type of knowledge and cognition, while according to the theologians it is a psychological speech that goes back to the statement of the soul of the assenter: 'I believe and I affirm.' Therefore, they define it as 'the speech of the self that follows cognition.'
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a commentary by al-Dasuqi on the matn statement defining tasdiq (assent). The matn says: 'If it is an assent to the proposition.' Al-Dasuqi begins by explaining that 'assent' (idh'an) means a perception with either certainty (jazzm) or opinion (zann). The lam in 'lil-nisba' (to the proposition) is for emphasis. He then breaks down the types of perception of the proposition (nisba): if the perception is preponderant but not certain, it is zann; if it is certain but does not correspond to reality, it is jahl murakkab (compound ignorance); if certain and corresponds to reality, it is yaqin (certainty); if it admits change due to a skeptic's questioning, it is taqlid (blind acceptance). All of these are considered tasdiq by the logicians (al-mantiqiyyun) because they all involve a judgment of occurrence or non-occurrence with either certainty or opinion. On the other hand, perception of the proposition through wahm (illusion) or shakk (doubt) is not tasdiq because there is no certainty or opinion. Al-Dasuqi then contrasts the theologians (al-mutakallimun): they do not classify zann, jahl, taqlid, shakk, or wahm as knowledge ('ilm); for them, knowledge is firm belief (i'tiqad jazim) that corresponds to reality and is based on proof. Thus, their definition of tasdiq is the opposite of the logicians'. For the logicians, tasdiq is a type of knowledge and cognition; for the theologians, it is a psychological speech (kalam nafsani) that corresponds to the inner utterance 'I have believed and affirmed.' Therefore, they define it as 'the speech of the self (hadith al-nafs) that follows cognition.' This highlights a fundamental difference: the logicians' tasdiq is epistemic (perception of a proposition), while the theologians' is a performative or psychological act of affirmation.

Checkpoint
According to al-Dasuqi's explanation of the logicians' definition, which of the following is NOT considered a tasdiq?
A) Yaqin (certainty)
B) Zann (opinion)
C) Shakk (doubt)
D) Taqlid (blind acceptance)

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq in logic encompasses any judgment of a proposition with certainty or opinion, excluding doubt and illusion; the theologians restrict it to certain knowledge based on proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify the following as tasdiq or not according to the logicians: a) A Muslim's firm belief that the Quran is the word of God (yaqin). b) A person's 70% belief that a certain hadith is authentic based on a weak chain (zann). c) A child's blind acceptance of what their parents say about Allah (taqlid). d) A scholar's hesitation about the correct ruling on a new issue after considering conflicting evidence (shakk).
?
Explain why the theologians would classify case (a) as tasdiq but not cases (b)-(d), referring to their definition.

The Judgmental Proposition: Definition and Components
Al-Dasuqi defines the judgmental proposition and its acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the judgmental proposition (al-nisba al-hukmiyya) and distinguish between affirmation (īqā') and negation (intizā') as the two acts of judgment.

Core Idea
The judgmental proposition is the relational content serving as the locus of judgment.

In this lesson, we explore the core of logical judgment: the proposition (nisba) that is the subject of a judgment (hukm). The passage defines this 'judgmental proposition' and explains the two fundamental acts of judgment: affirmation and negation. Understanding this distinction is essential for analyzing any logical statement in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term 'judgmental proposition'
Find the phrase 'al-nisba al-hukmiyya' in the Arabic. It is defined as the relation between subject and predicate, e.g., the attribution of predicate to subject.
The term is specific to logic; it is not any relation but the one that forms the content of a declarative statement.
2
Extract the definition
The proposition is 'judgmental' because it is attached to the judgment. It serves as the locus (ma'ruz) of affirmation and negation.
3
Distinguish īqā' and intizā'
Īqā' is the act of affirming that the proposition is actual (occurring), i.e., placing the predicate onto the subject. Intizā' is the act of perceiving the non-occurrence, i.e., lifting the predicate.
These are the two modes of judgment; every declarative statement involves one of these acts.
4
Apply to a fiqh example
Consider the statement 'Zakat is obligatory.' The judgmental proposition is 'Zakat is obligatory.' The act of judgment is īqā' (affirmation). If we say 'Zakat is not obligatory,' it is intizā' (negation).

الحكميَّة؛ (فَتَصْدِيقٌ). الدسوقي المجموعة المنطقية. (قَوْلُهُ : لِلنِّسْبَةِ الْحُكْمِيَّةِ) كثبوتِ الخبر للمبتدأ؛ أي: إدراكاً؛ لكون النسبة واقعةً أولاً، والحكمية : نسبة للحكم ؛ لكونها متعلّقة، فهي موردُ الإيجاب والسَّلْبِ المعبر عنهما بالإيقاع ؛ والانتزاع؛ وهو إدراك عدم الوقوع. و إدراك الوقوع، وبعبارة أخرى : قوله : لِلنِّسبة الحكمية؛ أي: المنسوبة للحكم لتعلقِهِ بها ؛ لأنَّ الحُكْمَ إدراك أنَّ النِّسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعةٍ، وَلَا تَتَّصفُ النِّسَبةُ حقيقةٌ بِكُونِهَا العطار معروضُهُ مِن هذه المقولة أو من مقولةٍ أُخرى، وبهذا التحقيق ينحل كثيرٌ من الإشكالات، كالإشكال بأنَّ الأشياء حَاصِلةٌ في الذهن بأنفسها، فيجب أن يكون العِلْمُ بالجوهر أو بالكم كَما، وبالكَيف كَيْفاً ؛ وهكذا، لا أنْ يكونَ مِن مقولة الكيف مُطلَقاً، ولا حاجة إلى ما ارتكبه المحشّي - يعني : الدَّوَّاني - في حواشي شرح التَّجريدِ ؛ مِن أنْ عدَّهُ مِن مقولة الكيف على سبيل المسامحة وتشبيه الأمور الذهنية بالأمور العينيَّةِ .ا.هـ. فظهر من هذا كُلِّهِ أنَّ الكَلامَ كُلَّهُ مبني على القولِ بالوجودِ الذهني، وقد قالَ بِهِ جميع الفلاسفة وبعضُ المتكلمين، وأنَّ الحَاصِل في الذهن هو الأشياء أنفسها، أمَّا على ما عليه جمهور المتكلمينَ مِنْ إنكار الوجود الذهني؛ فإِنَّ العِلْمَ عندَهُم إضافة مخصوصةٌ بين العالم والمعلوم، أو هو صفةٌ حقيقية ذات إضافة، وعلى من قالَ بالشَّبح والمثالِ مِنَ الحكماء؛ فَلَا إشكال في كَونِهِ مِن مقولة الكيف عندهم، قالَ الفَاضِلُ الكلنبوي في حواشي الدَّوَّاني على المتن : ليس معنى إنكار المتكلمين الوجودَ الذهني أنَّه لا يحصل صورةٌ عند العقل إذا تصوَّرْنَا شيئاً أو صدقنا بهِ؛ لأنَّ حصولها عنده في الواقع بديهي لا ينكره إلا المكابِرُ، وكيفَ يُنكرونَهُ والعِلْمُ الحادِثُ مَخلوقٌ عندَهُم؟! والخلق إنَّما يتعلَّق بأعيان الموجوداتِ، بل هو بمعنى أنَّ ذلك الحصول ليسَ نحواً آخَرَ مِن وجودِ الماهية المعلومة بأن يكونَ لِمَاهِيَّةٍ واحدةٍ كالشَّمس مثلاً وُجُودانِ؛ أحدُهُما خارجي، والآخَرَ ذهنيّ ؛ كما يقولُ بِهِ مثبتُوهُ ، فَهُم لا ينكرون الوجود عن صور الأشياء وأمثالها وأشباحها؛ لأنَّ تلك الأمثال والأشباحَ مَوجودات خارجيَّةٌ وكيفيات نفسانية عندَهُم، وهي المخلوقة عندَهُم ، وإنَّما ينكرون الوجود الذهني عن
The judgmental [proposition]; (thus tasdiq). Al-Dasuqi: The logical collection. (His statement: 'For the judgmental proposition') like the attribution of the predicate to the subject; i.e., a perception that the proposition is actual or not, and 'judgmental' means a proposition related to judgment because it is attached, so it is the locus of affirmation and negation, expressed by 'affirmation' (īqā') and 'withdrawal' (intizā'); the latter is perceiving non-occurrence, and the former perceiving occurrence. In other words: His statement: 'For the judgmental proposition' means the one ascribed to judgment because of its attachment to it, because judgment is the perception that the proposition is actual or not actual, and the proposition is not actually described as being of this category or another. Al-‘Attar: Its object is from this category or another, and by this investigation many problems are solved, such as the problem that things are present in the mind themselves, so knowledge of substance or quantity should be quantity, and of quality should be quality, and so on, not that it is absolutely from the category of quality. There is no need for what the commentator (meaning al-Dawwani) undertook in his glosses on the commentary of al-Tajrid, that he counted it as from the category of quality by way of leniency and comparing mental matters to external matters. So it appears from all this that the entire discussion is based on the assertion of mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni). All the philosophers and some theologians have asserted it, and what obtains in the mind is the things themselves. As for the position of the majority of theologians who deny mental existence, then knowledge according to them is a specific relation between the knower and the known, or it is a real attribute with relation. And for those among the philosophers who speak of 'shadow' (shabah) and 'image' (mithāl), there is no problem in it being from the category of quality according to them. Al-Kalanbawi said in his glosses on al-Dawwani's commentary on the text: 'The denial of mental existence by the theologians does not mean that no form occurs in the mind when we conceive something or assent to it, because its occurrence is intuitively obvious, and only the obstinate would deny it. How could they deny it while knowledge that comes to be is created according to them? And creation only pertains to the essences of existing things. Rather, it means that this obtaining is not another mode of existence of the known essence, such that one essence like the sun has two existences: one external and one mental, as its affirmers claim. So they do not deny existence with respect to the forms, likenesses, and images of things, because those likenesses and images are external existents and psychological qualities according to them, and they are what is created according to them. They only deny mental existence from...'
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a composite commentary. Al-Dasuqi explains the phrase 'lil-nisbati al-hukmiyyah' (for the judgmental proposition), meaning the proposition that is the object of a judgment (hukm) — specifically the relation between subject and predicate (like the attribution of predicate to subject). The proposition is 'judgmental' because it is attached to the judgment, serving as the locus of affirmation (īqā') and negation (intizā'). Al-‘Attar then enters a discussion about the category (maqula) of knowledge. He notes that, given mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni), things themselves are present in the mind. Therefore, knowledge of a substance would itself be substance, knowledge of quantity would be quantity, and knowledge of quality would be quality. This would imply that all knowledge is not simply in the category of quality, as some might assume. Al-‘Attar criticizes al-Dawwani for trying to fit knowledge into the category of quality through leniency (musamaha). He resolves the issue by stating that the whole discussion is based on the acceptance or rejection of mental existence. Philosophers and some theologians affirm mental existence, so for them the mental forms are the things themselves; hence knowledge is not restricted to quality. But the majority of theologians deny mental existence; for them, knowledge is a relation (idafa) or a real attribute with relation. For philosophers who speak of 'shabah' (shadow) and 'mithal' (image), knowledge is a quality. Al-Kalanbawi's gloss clarifies that the theologians' denial is not of the presence of forms in the mind (which is undeniable) but of the claim that those forms constitute a second mode of existence for the essence. For them, the mental similitudes are external existents (psychological qualities) and are created, so they do not assert a separate mental existence.

Key Terms

الإيقاع
الانتزاع

Key Takeaway

Resolving the Category of Knowledge: Al-'Attar's Critique
Al-'Attar resolves the category problem of knowledge and critiques al-Dawwani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct al-'Attar's resolution of the problem of whether knowledge belongs to the category of quality and evaluate his critique of al-Dawwani.

Core Idea
Knowledge is not simply a quality because, given mental existence, the mind contains things themselves in their own categories.

A key problem in Islamic logic and epistemology is: if things exist in the mind as themselves, then knowledge of a substance should be substance, not quality. Al-'Attar resolves this by pointing out that the entire discussion depends on one's view of mental existence, and he criticizes al-Dawwani's attempt to forcibly place knowledge into the category of quality. This lesson unpacks that resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Read al-'Attar's statement: if things are present in the mind as themselves, then knowledge of a substance would be substance, knowledge of quantity would be quantity, knowledge of quality would be quality. This contradicts the common view that knowledge is in the category of quality.
This problem arises only for those who affirm mental existence.
2
Find al-Dawwani's attempted solution
Al-Dawwani, in his glosses on al-Tajrid, counted knowledge as being from the category of quality 'by way of leniency' (musamaha), comparing mental matters to external ones.
3
Understand al-'Attar's resolution
Al-'Attar says the whole discussion is based on affirming or denying mental existence. For those who affirm it, knowledge is not necessarily quality; the mental form is the thing itself in its category. For those who deny it (the theologians), knowledge is a relation, not a quality. There is no need for al-Dawwani's leniency.
Thus, the problem dissolves once we recognize the different metaphysical commitments.
4
Evaluate the critique
Al-'Attar's critique is logically sound: if mental existence is true, then knowledge mirrors the object's category. If it is false, knowledge is a relation. Al-Dawwani's forced classification is unnecessary.

الحكميَّة؛ (فَتَصْدِيقٌ). الدسوقي المجموعة المنطقية. (قَوْلُهُ : لِلنِّسْبَةِ الْحُكْمِيَّةِ) كثبوتِ الخبر للمبتدأ؛ أي: إدراكاً؛ لكون النسبة واقعةً أولاً، والحكمية : نسبة للحكم ؛ لكونها متعلّقة، فهي موردُ الإيجاب والسَّلْبِ المعبر عنهما بالإيقاع ؛ والانتزاع؛ وهو إدراك عدم الوقوع. و إدراك الوقوع، وبعبارة أخرى : قوله : لِلنِّسبة الحكمية؛ أي: المنسوبة للحكم لتعلقِهِ بها ؛ لأنَّ الحُكْمَ إدراك أنَّ النِّسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعةٍ، وَلَا تَتَّصفُ النِّسَبةُ حقيقةٌ بِكُونِهَا العطار معروضُهُ مِن هذه المقولة أو من مقولةٍ أُخرى، وبهذا التحقيق ينحل كثيرٌ من الإشكالات، كالإشكال بأنَّ الأشياء حَاصِلةٌ في الذهن بأنفسها، فيجب أن يكون العِلْمُ بالجوهر أو بالكم كَما، وبالكَيف كَيْفاً ؛ وهكذا، لا أنْ يكونَ مِن مقولة الكيف مُطلَقاً، ولا حاجة إلى ما ارتكبه المحشّي - يعني : الدَّوَّاني - في حواشي شرح التَّجريدِ ؛ مِن أنْ عدَّهُ مِن مقولة الكيف على سبيل المسامحة وتشبيه الأمور الذهنية بالأمور العينيَّةِ .ا.هـ. فظهر من هذا كُلِّهِ أنَّ الكَلامَ كُلَّهُ مبني على القولِ بالوجودِ الذهني، وقد قالَ بِهِ جميع الفلاسفة وبعضُ المتكلمين، وأنَّ الحَاصِل في الذهن هو الأشياء أنفسها، أمَّا على ما عليه جمهور المتكلمينَ مِنْ إنكار الوجود الذهني؛ فإِنَّ العِلْمَ عندَهُم إضافة مخصوصةٌ بين العالم والمعلوم، أو هو صفةٌ حقيقية ذات إضافة، وعلى من قالَ بالشَّبح والمثالِ مِنَ الحكماء؛ فَلَا إشكال في كَونِهِ مِن مقولة الكيف عندهم، قالَ الفَاضِلُ الكلنبوي في حواشي الدَّوَّاني على المتن : ليس معنى إنكار المتكلمين الوجودَ الذهني أنَّه لا يحصل صورةٌ عند العقل إذا تصوَّرْنَا شيئاً أو صدقنا بهِ؛ لأنَّ حصولها عنده في الواقع بديهي لا ينكره إلا المكابِرُ، وكيفَ يُنكرونَهُ والعِلْمُ الحادِثُ مَخلوقٌ عندَهُم؟! والخلق إنَّما يتعلَّق بأعيان الموجوداتِ، بل هو بمعنى أنَّ ذلك الحصول ليسَ نحواً آخَرَ مِن وجودِ الماهية المعلومة بأن يكونَ لِمَاهِيَّةٍ واحدةٍ كالشَّمس مثلاً وُجُودانِ؛ أحدُهُما خارجي، والآخَرَ ذهنيّ ؛ كما يقولُ بِهِ مثبتُوهُ ، فَهُم لا ينكرون الوجود عن صور الأشياء وأمثالها وأشباحها؛ لأنَّ تلك الأمثال والأشباحَ مَوجودات خارجيَّةٌ وكيفيات نفسانية عندَهُم، وهي المخلوقة عندَهُم ، وإنَّما ينكرون الوجود الذهني عن
The judgmental [proposition]; (thus tasdiq). Al-Dasuqi: The logical collection. (His statement: 'For the judgmental proposition') like the attribution of the predicate to the subject; i.e., a perception that the proposition is actual or not, and 'judgmental' means a proposition related to judgment because it is attached, so it is the locus of affirmation and negation, expressed by 'affirmation' (īqā') and 'withdrawal' (intizā'); the latter is perceiving non-occurrence, and the former perceiving occurrence. In other words: His statement: 'For the judgmental proposition' means the one ascribed to judgment because of its attachment to it, because judgment is the perception that the proposition is actual or not actual, and the proposition is not actually described as being of this category or another. Al-‘Attar: Its object is from this category or another, and by this investigation many problems are solved, such as the problem that things are present in the mind themselves, so knowledge of substance or quantity should be quantity, and of quality should be quality, and so on, not that it is absolutely from the category of quality. There is no need for what the commentator (meaning al-Dawwani) undertook in his glosses on the commentary of al-Tajrid, that he counted it as from the category of quality by way of leniency and comparing mental matters to external matters. So it appears from all this that the entire discussion is based on the assertion of mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni). All the philosophers and some theologians have asserted it, and what obtains in the mind is the things themselves. As for the position of the majority of theologians who deny mental existence, then knowledge according to them is a specific relation between the knower and the known, or it is a real attribute with relation. And for those among the philosophers who speak of 'shadow' (shabah) and 'image' (mithāl), there is no problem in it being from the category of quality according to them. Al-Kalanbawi said in his glosses on al-Dawwani's commentary on the text: 'The denial of mental existence by the theologians does not mean that no form occurs in the mind when we conceive something or assent to it, because its occurrence is intuitively obvious, and only the obstinate would deny it. How could they deny it while knowledge that comes to be is created according to them? And creation only pertains to the essences of existing things. Rather, it means that this obtaining is not another mode of existence of the known essence, such that one essence like the sun has two existences: one external and one mental, as its affirmers claim. So they do not deny existence with respect to the forms, likenesses, and images of things, because those likenesses and images are external existents and psychological qualities according to them, and they are what is created according to them. They only deny mental existence from...'
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a composite commentary. Al-Dasuqi explains the phrase 'lil-nisbati al-hukmiyyah' (for the judgmental proposition), meaning the proposition that is the object of a judgment (hukm) — specifically the relation between subject and predicate (like the attribution of predicate to subject). The proposition is 'judgmental' because it is attached to the judgment, serving as the locus of affirmation (īqā') and negation (intizā'). Al-‘Attar then enters a discussion about the category (maqula) of knowledge. He notes that, given mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni), things themselves are present in the mind. Therefore, knowledge of a substance would itself be substance, knowledge of quantity would be quantity, and knowledge of quality would be quality. This would imply that all knowledge is not simply in the category of quality, as some might assume. Al-‘Attar criticizes al-Dawwani for trying to fit knowledge into the category of quality through leniency (musamaha). He resolves the issue by stating that the whole discussion is based on the acceptance or rejection of mental existence. Philosophers and some theologians affirm mental existence, so for them the mental forms are the things themselves; hence knowledge is not restricted to quality. But the majority of theologians deny mental existence; for them, knowledge is a relation (idafa) or a real attribute with relation. For philosophers who speak of 'shabah' (shadow) and 'mithal' (image), knowledge is a quality. Al-Kalanbawi's gloss clarifies that the theologians' denial is not of the presence of forms in the mind (which is undeniable) but of the claim that those forms constitute a second mode of existence for the essence. For them, the mental similitudes are external existents (psychological qualities) and are created, so they do not assert a separate mental existence.

Key Terms
الوجود الذهني
الإشكال
المسامحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-'Attar, why is al-Dawwani's classification of knowledge as quality unnecessary?
A) Because knowledge is not a quality but a substance
B) Because the problem is based on affirming or denying mental existence, and each position leads to a different categorization
C) Because al-Dawwani's classification was correct but he provided no evidence
D) Because the entire discussion is meaningless

Key Takeaway
The category of knowledge is not fixed; it depends on whether one affirms mental existence or sees knowledge as a relation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ghazali (a theologian) defines knowledge as a relation (idafa). Using al-'Attar's framework, explain how this aligns with the denial of mental existence.
?
If a philosopher affirms mental existence, what category would knowledge of a quality (like 'whiteness') belong to according to al-'Attar's reasoning? Justify.
