Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
6 min
Clarifying the Theologians' Denial of Mental Existence
Al-Kalanbawi clarifies the theologians' denial of mental existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the theologians' position on mental existence and distinguish it from a denial of mental representation.

Core Idea
Theologians deny that mental images are a second existence of the essence, not that they occur in the mind.

A common misunderstanding is that the theologians (mutakallimun) who deny mental existence believe that no mental forms occur. Al-Kalanbawi's gloss clarifies: they affirm the occurrence of forms but deny that these forms are a separate mode of existence of the thing itself. This lesson unpacks that crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the common misunderstanding
Many assume that denying mental existence means denying that we have mental images. Al-Kalanbawi says this is false; it is intuitively obvious that forms occur in the mind when we think or assent.
2
Read al-Kalanbawi's positive claim
The theologians' denial means that the mental form is not another mode of existence (wujud) of the essence. For example, the sun in the mind is not a second sun existing mentally; it is a likeness (shabah) or image (mithal) that is itself an external existent (a psychological quality).
They consider these mental forms as created things, which are external existents in the category of quality.
3
Contrast with philosophers' view
Philosophers affirm mental existence, meaning the same essence has two existences: external and mental. Theologians reject this duplication; for them, there is only one existence, and knowledge is a relation or attribute.
4
Apply to an example
When you conceive of a horse, the Ash'ari theologian says a form of the horse occurs in your mind, but that form is a created psychological quality, not the horse itself existing mentally. The philosopher says the horse's essence exists mentally.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

Three Theories of Mental Existence in Islamic Epistemology
Author discusses mental existence and defends knowledge as quality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three positions on what exists in the mind during knowledge and evaluate the theologians' fire argument against mental existence.

Core Idea
Theologians deny essences in the mind, not mental forms.

This passage clarifies a subtle debate: do external objects themselves enter the mind when we know them? The author distinguishes three views: the philosophers' mental existence (essences themselves), the theologians' relational theory (knowledge as relation), and the intermediate phantom/likeness theory. He then defends the classification of knowledge under quality against an objection. Understanding these distinctions is key to later discussions in metaphysics and epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Locate in the Arabic the three views: 1) Philosophers and some theologians affirm mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni) – the essences themselves are in the mind. 2) The majority of theologians deny this, holding knowledge as a relation or a real attribute with relation. 3) Some philosophers adopt the phantom/likeness theory (al-shabah wa al-mithal) – a mental representation, not the essence itself.
The phantom/likeness theory is intermediate: it affirms mental forms but denies essences.
2
Understand the theologians' denial
According to al-Kalanbawi, the theologians do not deny that a form or image occurs in the mind – that is obvious. They deny that this form is another mode of existence of the same essence that has external existence. So for them, the mental form is a created accident, not the thing itself.
The theologians' fire argument proves that fire itself (external essence) is not in the mind, but does not refute the existence of a phantom of fire.
3
Reconstruct the fire argument logically
The argument is: If fire itself were in the mind, then minds would burn (antecedent to consequent). But minds do not burn (denial of consequent). Therefore, fire itself is not in the mind (denial of antecedent). This is a valid modus tollens conditional syllogism.
The argument only targets the claim that the essence itself enters the mind, not phantoms.
4
Analyze the objection about knowledge as quality
The objection: Quality is defined as not depending on conceiving another, but acquired knowledge depends on prior concepts. The answer: The dependence in the definition means the quality cannot be conceived without itself, not that it cannot depend on external things. Acquired knowledge can be intuitively known, so it fits.
This shows how careful definition is needed in logical classifications.

Source Text

فَظَهَرَ مِنْ هَذَا كُلِّهِ أَنَّ الْكَلَامَ كُلَّهُ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى الْقَوْلِ بِالْوُجُودِ الذِّهْنِيِ , وَقَدْ قَالَ بِهِ جَمِيعُ الْفَلَاسِفَةِ وَبَعْضُ الْمُتَكَلِّمِينَ , وَأَنَّ الْحَاصِلَ فِي الذِّهْنِ هُوَ الْأَشْيَاءُ أَنْفُسُهَا , أَمَّا عَلَى مَا عَلَيْهِ جُمْهُورُ الْمُتَكَلِّمِينَ مِنْ إِنْكَارِ الْوُجُودِ الذِّهْنِيِ ; فَإِنَّ الْعِلْمَ عِنْدَهُمْ إِضَافَةٌ مَخْصُوصَةٌ بَيْنَ الْعَالِمِ وَالْمَعْلُومِ , أَوْ هُوَ صِفَةٌ حَقِيقِيَّةٌ ذَاتُ إِضَافَةٍ , وَعَلَى مَنْ قَالَ بِالشَّبَحِ وَالْمِثَالِ مِنَ الْحُكَمَاءِ ; فَلَا إِشْكَالَ فِي كَوْنِهِ مِنْ مَقُولَةِ الْكَيْفِ عِنْدَهُمْ , قَالَ الْفَاضِلُ الْكَلَنْبَوِيُ فِي حَوَاشِي الدَّوَّانِيِ عَلَى الْمَتْنِ : لَيْسَ مَعْنَى إِنْكَارِ الْمُتَكَلِّمِينَ الْوُجُودَ الذِّهْنِيَ أَنَّهُ لَا يُحْصُلُ صُورَةٌ عِنْدُ الْعَقْلِ إِذَا تَصَوَّرْنَا شَيْئاً أَوْ صَدَّقْنَا بِهِ ; لِأَنَّ حُصُولَهَا عِنْدَهُ فِي الْوَاقِعِ بَدِيهِيٌّ لَا يُنْكِرُهُ إِلَّا الْمُكَابِرُ , وَكَيْفَ يُنْكِرُونَهُ وَالْعِلْمُ الْحَادِثُ مَخْلُوقٌ عِنْدَهُمْ؟! وَالْخَلْقُ إِنَّمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِأَعْيَانِ الْمَوْجُودَاتِ , بَلْ هُوَ بِمَعْنَى أَنَّ ذَلِكَ الْحُصُولَ لَيْسَ نَحْواً آخَرَ مِنْ وُجُودِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ الْمَعْلُومَةِ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ لِمَاهِيَّةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ كَالشَّمْسِ مَثَلاً وُجُودَانِ ; أَحَدُهُمَا خَارِجِيٌ , وَالْآخَرَ ذِهْنِيٌ ; كَمَا يَقُولُ بِهِ مُثْبِتُوهُ , فَهُمْ لَا يُنْكِرُونَ الْوُجُودَ عَنْ صُورِ الْأَشْيَاءِ وَأَمْثَالِهَا وَأَشْبَاحِهَا ; لِأَنَّ تِلْكَ الْأَمْثَالَ وَالْأَشْبَاحَ مَوجُودَاتٌ خَارِجِيَّةٌ وَكَيْفِيَّاتٌ نَفْسَانِيَّةٌ عِنْدَهُمْ , وَهِيَ الْمَخْلُوقَةُ عِنْدَهُمْ , وَإِنَّمَا يُنْكِرُونَ الْوُجُودَ الذِّهْنِيَ عَنْ نَفْسِ تِلْكَ الْأَشْيَاءِ , وَذَلِكَ بِشَهَادَةِ أَدِلَّتِهِمْ ; حَيْثُ قَالُوا: لَوْ حَصُلَ النَّارُ فِي الْأَذْهَانِ ; لَاحْتَرَقَتْ أَذْهَانُنَا بِتَصَوُّرِنَا لَهَا , وَاللَّازِمُ بَاطِلٌ , فَإِنَّهُ كَمَا تَرَى , إِنَّمَا يَنْفِي الْوُجُودَ عَنْ نَفْسِ النَّارِ لَا عَنْ شَبَحِهَا وَمِثَالِهَا , فَالْحَقُّ أَنَّ جُمْهُورَ الْمُتَكَلِّمِينَ إِنَّمَا يُنْكِرُونَ مَا ذَهَبَ إِلَيْهِ مُحَقِّقُو الْفَلَاسِفَةِ ; مِنْ أَنَّ الْحَاصِلَ فِي الْأَذْهَانِ أَنْفُسُ مَاهِيَّاتِ الْأَشْيَاءِ , وَلَمْ يُنكِرُوا مَا ذَهَبَ إِلَيْهِ أَهْلُ الْأَشْبَاحِ ; كَمَا صَرَّحَ بِهِ بَعْضُ الْأَفَاضِلِ فِي حَاشِيَةِ الْخَيَالِيِ , وَبَقِيَ أَنَّ الْمَحَشِّيَ نَقَلَ عَنِ الشَّيْخِ الْغَنِيمِيِّ اسْتِشْكَالَ جَعْلِ الْعِلْمِ مِنْ مَقُولَةِ الْكَيْفِ مَعَ قَوْلِهِمْ إِنَّ الْكَيْفَ عَرَضٌ لَا يَقْبَلُ الْقِسْمَةَ لِذَاتِهِ , وَلَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى تَصَوُّرِ غَيْرِهِ بِأَنَّه لَا يَصْدُقُ عَلَى الْعُلُومِ الْكَسْبِيَّةِ ; لِأَنَّ تَصَوُّرَهَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى تَصَوُّرِ غَيْرِهَا . ا.ه . وَأَقُولُ : الْإِشْكَالُ مَشْهُورٌ قَدِيماً , وَأَجَابُوا عَنْهُ , قَالَ الْعَلَّامَةُ عَبْدُ الْحَكِيمِ فِي حَاشِيَةِ الْمُطَوَّلِ : إِنَّ مَعْنَى التَّوَقُّفِ الْمَأْخُوذِ فِي تَعْرِيفِ الْكَيْفِ ; أَنَّهُ لَا يُمْكِنُ التَّصَوُّرُ بِدُونِهِ أَصْلاً , قَالُوا : فَلَا يَرِدُ الْكَيْفِيَّةُ الْمُرَكَّبَةُ ; لِأَنَّ تَصَوُّرَهَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى تَصَوُّرِ أَجْزَائِهَا ; لَا عَلَى أَمْرٍ خَارِجٍ , وَكَذَا الْكَيْفِيَّةُ الْمُكْتَسَبَةُ بِالْحَدِّ أَوِ الرَّسْمِ ; إِذْ لَا تَوَقُّفَ فِيهَا بِمَعْنَى عَدَمِ إِمْكَانِ التَّصَوُّرِ بِدُونِهَا ; لِإِمْكَانِ حُصُولِهَا بِالْبَدَاهَةِ . ا.ه . وَقَدْ أَطَلْنَا الْكَلَامَ فِي هَذَا الْمَقَامِ ; حِرْصاً عَلَى تِلْكَ الْفَوَائِدِ الَّتِي قَلَّ أَنَّ تُوجَدُ هَكَذَا فِي كِتَابٍ , فَاحْرِصْ عَلَيْهَا إِنْ كُنْتَ مِنْ أَذْكِيَاءِ الطُّلَّابِ . ثُمَّ إِنِّي بَعْدَ حِينٍ مِنَ الرَّمَانِ رَأَيْتُ لِلْعَلَّامَةِ مِيرْ زَاهِدٍ الْهِنْدِيِّ حَاشِيَةً عَلَّقَهَا عَلَى رِسَالَةِ الْعَلَّامَةِ الرَّازِيِّ فِي التَّصَوُّرِ وَالتَّصْدِيقِ ; ذَكَرَ فِيهَا كَلَاماً يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهَذَا الْمَقَامِ فِي غَايَةِ التَّحْقِيقِ ; فَأَحْبَبْتُ ذِكْرَهُ هَهُنَا , وَإِنْ أَدَّى إِلَى مَزِيدِ تَطْوِيلٍ ; لِعِلْمِي أَنَّهُ نَادِرُ الْوُجُودِ , وَقَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ : اعْلَمْ أَنَّ هَهُنَا إِشْكَالاً مَشْهُوراً أَوْرَدَهُ الشَّيْخُ فِي «إِلَهِيّاتِ الشِّفَاءِ», وَأَجَابَ عَنْهُ حَيْثُ قَالَ: لِقَائِلِ أَنْ يَقُولَ
So it became clear from all of this that the entire discussion is based on the affirmation of mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni), and all philosophers and some theologians have affirmed it, and that what obtains in the mind is the things themselves. As for the position of the majority of theologians who deny mental existence, for them knowledge is a specific relation between the knower and the known, or it is a real attribute having relation. And for those among the philosophers who affirm the phantom and likeness, there is no difficulty in knowledge being from the category of quality according to them. Al-Fadil al-Kalanbawi said in his glosses on al-Dawani's commentary on the text: 'The meaning of the theologians' denial of mental existence is not that no form obtains in the mind when we conceive something or assent to it; because its obtaining there is actually obvious and no one denies it except a stubborn person. How could they deny it while contingent knowledge is created according to them? And creation pertains only to the essences of existents. Rather, it means that that obtaining is not another mode of existence of the known essence such that a single essence like the sun would have two existences, one external and one mental, as its affirmers claim. So they do not deny existence from the forms of things and their likenesses and phantoms, because those likenesses and phantoms are external existents and psychological qualities according to them, and they are what are created by them. They only deny mental existence from the things themselves. This is witnessed by their arguments, where they said: If fire itself obtained in minds, our minds would be burned by our conception of it, and the consequent is false. This argument, as you see, negates existence from the fire itself, not from its phantom and likeness. So the truth is that the majority of theologians only deny what the investigating philosophers held—that what obtains in minds is the very essences of things—and they did not deny what the proponents of phantoms held, as some excellent scholars stated in the gloss of al-Khiyali. There remains the objection that the glossator transmitted from al-Shaykh al-Ghanimi regarding the classification of knowledge under the category of quality despite their saying that quality is an accident that does not admit division in itself and does not depend on the conception of another, in that it does not apply to acquired knowledges because their conception depends on the conception of something else. End quote. I say: This objection is well-known from ancient times, and they have answered it. Al-Allama Abd al-Hakim said in his gloss on al-Mutawwal: 'The meaning of the dependence (tawaqquf) taken in the definition of quality is that it is absolutely impossible to conceive without it. They said: So it does not apply to the composite quality, because its conception depends on the conception of its parts, not on an external matter. Similarly for the quality acquired by definition or description, since there is no dependence in it in the sense of the impossibility of conception without it, because it can be obtained by intuition.' End quote. I have lengthened the discussion in this place out of eagerness for those benefits that are rarely found in a book, so be eager for them if you are among the intelligent students. Then, after some time, I saw for al-Allama Mir Zahid al-Hindi a gloss he wrote on al-Allama al-Razi's treatise on tasawwur and tasdiq, in which he mentioned a discussion related to this place that is extremely thorough, so I wanted to mention it here, even if it leads to further lengthening, because I know it is rare to find. He said, may God have mercy on him: 'Know that there is a well-known objection that the Shaykh raised in the Ilahiyyat of al-Shifa', and he answered it where he said: For a speaker might say...'
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a critical-epistemological discussion about mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni) and its implications for the classification of knowledge as a quality (kayf). The commentator begins by clarifying that the entire preceding discussion is built on the assumption of mental existence, which is affirmed by all philosophers and some theologians. For the majority of theologians who deny mental existence, knowledge is either a specific relation (idafa) or a real attribute with relation. For those philosophers who adopt the 'phantom and likeness' theory, knowledge is unproblematically a quality. The commentator then quotes al-Kalanbawi to clarify what the theologians' denial of mental existence actually means: they do not deny that a form occurs in the mind when we conceive or assent—that is obvious—rather they deny that this form is another mode of existence of the same essence that exists externally. The theologians' famous argument against mental existence (the fire example) only shows that the fire itself is not in the mind, but does not rule out a phantom or likeness. Thus the majority of theologians only reject the philosophers' claim that the very essences of things exist in the mind, not the theory of phantoms. The passage then presents an objection regarding knowledge being classified as a quality: quality is defined as something that does not depend on the conception of another, but acquired knowledge depends on prior concepts. The commentator provides the answer from Abd al-Hakim: the dependence in the definition means that the quality cannot be conceived without itself; it is not about dependence on external things. Composite qualities and acquired qualities can be conceived without themselves (they can be known by intuition or by their parts), so the objection does not apply. Finally, the commentator introduces a rare quote from Mir Zahid al-Hindi on a related objection from Avicenna's Ilahiyyat, but the passage cuts off before the quote is complete.

According to al-Kalanbawi's explanation, why do the theologians' arguments against mental existence (e.g., the fire example) not refute the 'phantom and likeness' theory?
A) Because the argument only negates the existence of the fire itself, not its phantom.
B) Because the argument is based on a mistaken premise.
C) Because the theologians accept mental existence for simple concepts.
D) Because the fire example is not a valid logical argument.

Key Takeaway
The theologians' denial of mental existence is a specific denial that essences themselves enter the mind, not the denial of any mental form; this distinction is crucial for understanding Islamic epistemology and the classification of knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the theologians' fire argument and reconstruct it as a conditional syllogism (modus tollens). Then explain why, according to al-Kalanbawi, this argument does not refute the phantom/likeness theory.
?
Compare the three positions on mental existence in a table: Philosophers (mental existence of essences), Phantom theorists (mental phantoms but not essences), Theologians (knowledge as relation/attribute). For each, state what exists in the mind and whether knowledge is a quality, using the passage as evidence.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
8 min
Mental Existence and the Definition of Knowledge
Author addresses objections to mental existence and definition of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish mental image from physical essence and evaluate the objection that knowledge as a quality conflicts with acquired sciences.

Core Idea
In the mind, only the image of fire exists, not fire itself—so the mind does not burn.

This passage tackles two classic objections: one against mental existence (the fire argument) and another against defining knowledge as a quality. The author clarifies that the objector confuses the image with the essence, and then resolves a subtle issue about acquired knowledge depending on other concepts. Understanding these responses is essential for anyone working in Islamic theology or logic, as they defend core epistemological commitments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the fire objection
The objector argues: if fire existed in our minds, our minds would burn. This is meant to be a reductio ad absurdum of mental existence.
Identify the premise that mental existence of fire implies physical effects of fire.
2
Locate the response
The text replies that the objection only negates the existence of the fire itself (its physical essence) in the mind, not its image (shabah) and likeness (mithal). The mind contains only the form, not the fiery substance.
The key distinction is between the thing's essence and its mental representation.
3
Examine the second problem
The second objection: knowledge is said to be a quality, which is defined as an accident that does not depend on conceiving something else. But acquired sciences (al-ʿulūm al-kasbiyya) depend on prior concepts—so how can they be simple qualities?
This threatens the classification of knowledge under the category of quality.
4
Extract the solution
The answer from ʿAbd al-Ḥakīm clarifies that the dependence in the definition of quality is absolute impossibility of conception without it. Acquired sciences can be attained intuitively (bi-l-bidāha), so their dependence on parts or definitions is not of that absolute type.
Thus, acquired sciences still qualify as simple qualities because they do not require an external concept for their conception in an absolute sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العطار نفس؛ تلك الأشياء، وذلكَ بِشهادة أدلَّتِهم؛ حيث قالُوا: لو حصلَ النَّارُ في الأذهان؛ لاحترقت أذهاننا بتصورِنَا لها، واللَّازِمُ باطل، فإنَّهُ كما ترى، إنَّما ينفي الوجود عن نفس النَّارِ لا عَن شَبَحِهَا ومِثَالِها، فالحقُّ أنَّ جمهور المتكلمينَ إِنَّما ينكرونَ ما ذهبَ إليهِ مُحقِّقُو الفلاسفة؛ مِن أنَّ الحاصِلَ في الأذهان أنفُسُ ماهيَّاتِ الأشياء، ولم يُنكِرُوا ما ذهب إليه أهل الأشباح؛ كما صرَّحَ بِهِ بعضُ الأفاضل في حاشية الخيالي، وبقي أنَّ المحشّي نقل عن الشَّيخ الغنيمي استشكال جعل العلمِ مِن مقولة الكيف مع قولهم إنَّ الكيف عرضُ لا يقبلُ القِسمةَ لِذاتِهِ، ولا يتوقَّفُ عَلى تَصوُّرِ غيرِهِ بأَنَّهُ لا يصدقُ على العلوم الكسبيَّةِ؛ لأنَّ تصورها يتوقَّفُ على تصورِ غيرِها .ا.هـ. وأقولُ : الإشكالُ مَشهورٌ قديماً، وأجابوا عنه، قال العلامة عبد الحكيم في حاشية المطوَّلِ: إنَّ معنى التَّوقُفِ المأخوذ في تعريف الكيف؛ أنَّه لا يُمكنُ التَّصَوُّرُ بدونِهِ أصلاً، قالوا: فلا يردُّ الكيفيَّةُ المركَّبةُ؛ لأنَّ تصوُّرها يتوقَّفُ على تصور أجزائها؛ لا على أمر خارج، وكَذَا الكيفية المكتسبة بالحد أو الرسم؛ إذ لا توقُفَ فيها بمعنى عدم إمكانِ التَّصَوُّرِ بدونِها؛ لإمكان حصولها بالبداهة .ا.هـ.
Al-Attar: ... those things, as testified by their proofs, when they said: If fire were obtained in minds, our minds would burn due to our conceiving it. The consequent is false. For it, as you see, only negates existence from the fire itself, not from its image and likeness. The truth is that the majority of theologians only deny what the verifying philosophers held, that what is obtained in minds are the very essences of things. They do not deny what the proponents of images held, as some distinguished scholars explicitly stated in the marginal commentary on al-Khayali. And it remains that the commentator [al-Muhashshi] reported from Shaykh al-Ghunaimi a problem concerning making knowledge a category of quality, along with their statement that quality is an accident that does not admit division in itself, and does not depend on the conception of another, [arguing] that it does not apply to acquired sciences because their conception depends on the conception of other things. [End quote]. I say: This problem is well-known from antiquity, and they answered it. Al-Allama Abd al-Hakim said in the marginal commentary on al-Mutawwal: The meaning of dependence taken in the definition of quality is that conception is absolutely impossible without it. They said: So composite quality is not objected to because its conception depends on the conception of its parts, not on an external matter. Likewise, quality acquired by definition or description, for there is no dependence in it in the sense of impossibility of conception without it, because it can be obtained intuitively. [End quote].
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a critical discussion of two objections related to mental existence and the definition of knowledge. The first objection is a classical one: if fire existed in the mind, our minds would burn. The answer is that the objector mistakenly thinks that the very essence of fire is in the mind, whereas what is present is only the image (shabah) and likeness (mithal) of fire. Thus, the philosophers' claim that the forms of things are in the mind does not mean the physical fire itself is present. The commentator then notes that the majority of theologians only deny the extreme view of some philosophers that the essences themselves are in the mind, but they accept that images are in the mind. Next, a second problem is raised from a marginal commentary: if knowledge is a quality, and quality is defined as an accident that does not depend on the conception of another, then acquired sciences are problematic because their conception depends on other things. The answer, from Abd al-Hakim's commentary on al-Mutawwal, clarifies that the dependence intended in the definition of quality is absolute impossibility of conception without it. Acquired sciences depend on their parts or on a definition, but this dependence is not of that absolute type, because they can be attained intuitively. Hence, they still qualify as simple qualities.

Key Terms
الحصول في الأذهان
شبح
الكيف
العلوم الكسبية

Checkpoint
The objection that if fire were in the mind, our minds would burn is answered by:
A) The mind is not affected by mental images.
B) The fire in the mind is not the same as external fire.
C) The objector only denies the existence of the fire itself, not its image.
D) The philosophers do not claim that fire itself is in the mind.

Key Takeaway
Mental existence pertains to the image of a thing, not its physical essence; and acquired knowledge, though dependent on other concepts, can still be a simple quality because that dependence is not absolute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Reproduce the fire objection in your own words, then write the response from the passage, clearly distinguishing between the mental image and the physical essence.
?
Task 2: Consider the definition of knowledge in usul al-fiqh: 'knowledge is the mental image with certainty.' How does the passage's distinction between mental existence of an image and the thing itself apply to this definition? Does the definition refer to the image or the essence?

Definition of Tasdiq as Pure Judgment
Author defines tasdiq as hukm only, simplifying it to a single act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definition of tasdiq as judgment only, according to the philosophers, and distinguish it from composite definitions that include conception.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is nothing but judgment – a simple act, not composite.

This lesson focuses on a foundational definition in Islamic logic: what is tasdiq (assent)? The author, following the philosophers (al-hukama'), defines tasdiq as purely judgment (hukm) – a simple mental act. This definition contrasts with other views that treat tasdiq as composite, involving both conception (tasawwur) and judgment. Understanding this simplification is key to grasping the nature of belief and knowledge in the Islamic intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find the definiendum: the term that is being defined. In the Arabic, it is التصديق (al-tasdiq). Notice that the author also mentions 'taslim' and 'qabul' as alternative names for the same act.
2
Extract the core component of the definition
The definition states that tasdiq is 'al-hukm faqaṭ' – judgment only. What is judgment? The author earlier described it as 'idrāk ʿalā al-wajh al-madhkūr' (perception in the mentioned manner), which implies perception with commitment to truth.
Judgment here is the mental act of affirming or denying a proposition.
3
Contrast with the alternative composite definition
Later logicians often define tasdiq as tasawwur (conception) + hukm, making it composite. This passage explicitly rejects that by saying 'only' (faqaṭ). Compare: in the composite view, first you conceive the meaning, then you judge; here the judgment itself is the entire act.
This distinction is important for understanding debates about the nature of iman (faith).
4
Note the doctrinal attribution
The definition is attributed to 'the philosophers' (al-hukama'). This indicates that the view is associated with the falāsifa tradition (e.g., Avicenna, al-Farabi). Recognize that this is one school among many in Islamic logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسم التسليم والقبول. والإدراك على الوجه المذكور يسمى حكماً. فالتصديق على تعريفه: هو الحكم فقط كما هو مذهب الحكماء، فيكون بسيطاً.
The name of submission and acceptance. And perception in the mentioned manner is called judgment. So assent according to its definition: it is judgment only, as is the doctrine of the philosophers, so it is simple.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage defines assent (tasdiq) according to the philosophers (hukama'). It begins by stating that the terms 'submission' (taslim) and 'acceptance' (qabul) are names for the same mental act. Perception in the way that involves commitment—i.e., with judgment—is called 'judgment' (hukm). Building on that, the author says that assent (tasdiq), by definition, is merely judgment (hukm) and nothing more. This aligns specifically with the view of the philosophers (al-hukama'), who consider assent to be a simple act of the mind, not composite. This contrasts with other schools that might add additional elements to the definition. For example, in fiqh, assenting that 'wine is haram' is simply the mental judgment of prohibition; it does not require a separate act of conception beyond the judgment itself, according to this view.

Key Terms
التصديق (al-tasdiq): Assent: the mental act of judging a proposition to be true or false, identified here solely with hukm, without additional components. [Note: Later logicians often define tasdiq as 'tasawwur + hukm', making it composite, contrary to this passage.]
الحكم (al-hukm): Judgment: the perception that a relation (nisba) holds or does not hold, which is the core of tasdiq. [Note: In this context, hukm is synonymous with tasdiq; in later texts, hukm may be distinguished as a broader category.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers in this passage, tasdiq is defined as:
A) Conception plus judgment
B) Judgment only
C) Submission only
D) Perception without judgment

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq, for the philosophers, is solely the mental act of judgment, making it a simple rather than composite act.

Three Prerequisites for Judgment (Hukm)
Author lists three necessary conceptualizations for a judgment to occur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three conceptual prerequisites for any judgment (hukm) and explain how they relate to the definition of tasdiq.

Core Idea
Every judgment requires three mental acts: knowing the subject, the predicate, and the relation between them.

In this passage, the author explains that for a judgment (hukm) to exist, three conceptualizations must precede it. These are not parts of the judgment itself but prerequisites. Understanding these is essential for analyzing propositions (qadaya) in logic and later in Islamic sciences like usul al-fiqh. The author also justifies the definition of hukm as the perception of a relation holding or not holding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conceptualizations
List them from the Arabic: تصور المحكوم عليه, تصور النسبة الحكمية, تصور المحكوم به.
2
Understand each term
المحكوم عليه = subject (what is being judged about); المحكوم به = predicate (what is affirmed/denied); النسبة الحكمية = the relational judgment (the connection between subject and predicate).
3
Recognize that these are prerequisites, not components
The judgment (hukm) is the perception that the relation holds or does not hold. For example, in 'the world is created,' the judgment is the mental act of affirming the relation between 'world' and 'created'.
4
Connect to tasdiq (assent)
Tasdiq is defined as judgment (hukm). So the three conceptualizations are necessary for any act of assent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكن يُشترط في وجوده ثلاثة تصورات: 1. تصور المحكوم عليه. 2. وتصور النسبة الحكمية. 3. وتصور المحكوم به. وإنما قلنا: الإدراك على الوجه المذكور هو الحكم؛ لأن الحكم على ما ذكر القوم هو: إدراك أن النسبة واقعة، أو ليست بواقعة.
But for its existence, three conceptualizations are required: 1. Conception of the subject of judgment. 2. Conception of the relational judgment. 3. Conception of the object of judgment. And we only said: perception in the mentioned manner is judgment; because judgment, as the people (scholars) mentioned, is: perception that the relation is occurring, or not occurring.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the prerequisites for a judgment (hukm) to exist. The author states that three conceptualizations (tasawwurat) must precede the act of judging. First, one must conceive the subject of the judgment (al-mahkum 'alayhi). Second, one must conceive the relational judgment itself (al-nisba al-hukmiyya), which is the connection between subject and predicate. Third, one must conceive the object of judgment (al-mahkum bihi), i.e., the predicate. Then the author justifies why they defined perception in a specific way as 'judgment': because the standard definition of hukm among scholars is that it is the perception that a relation either holds (waqi'a) or does not hold (laysat bi-waqi'a). Thus, the act of judging inherently involves these three components, but the judgment itself is the perception of the occurrence or non-occurrence of the relation. For example, to judge that 'the world is created,' one must first conceive 'the world' (subject), then the relational notion of predication (nisba), and then 'created' (predicate). The judgment itself is the mental act of affirming that relation.

Key Terms
المحكوم عليه
النسبة الحكمية
المحكوم به
الحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Subject, predicate, and judgment
B) Subject, relational judgment, and predicate
C) Subject, object, and conclusion
D) Assent, conception, and judgment

Key Takeaway
The three conceptualizations (subject, relation, predicate) are prerequisites for any judgment, and judgment itself is the perception of the relation's occurrence or non-occurrence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Al-Sayyid's Objection to the Division of Knowledge
Author reports al-Sayyid's objection that the common division is unsound.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct al-Sayyid's objection to the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq and explain why it challenges the standard presentation.

Core Idea
The common division of knowledge was contested on grounds of authority and logical soundness.

The passage presents al-Sayyid al-Jurjani's critique of the division of knowledge into conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). This division is often taken as foundational in Islamic logic. However, as we learn here, some scholars found it unsound. Understanding this critique deepens our appreciation of the debates within the discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of the objection
What exactly is being criticized? Al-Sayyid objects to the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq. Recognize that this division was commonly taught in logic texts.
This division is a standard starting point in many works of Islamic logic.
2
Extract the grounds of the objection
On what basis does al-Sayyid reject the division? He says it does not agree with the philosophers (al-hukama') nor the Imam, and is not sound in itself, leading to absurd consequences (muhadhir).
The reference to 'Imam' likely means Fakhr al-Din al-Razi or al-Ghazali.
3
Note the methodological critique
The passage criticizes the commentator (al-muhashshi) for inadequate transmission of the original text and the objection, and for falsely claiming that the division was well-known among later scholars.
This shows the importance of accurate transmission in scholarly critique.
4
Assess the implications
If this division is unsound, what does that mean for the study of logic? It challenges a foundational framework and shows that even basic concepts were debated.
This highlights the dynamic nature of Islamic intellectual tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاعترضها السيد بأنه تقسيم لا يوافق مذهب الحكماء ولا الإمام، بل لا يكون صحيحاً في نفسه، وبين ذلك بلزوم محاذير نقل المحشي بعضها؛ فقد أخل بنقل كلام الأصل وبالاعتراض عليه، وادعى أنه قول اشتهر عند المتأخرين مع أنه لم يقل به أحد منهم، وحكموا بفساده.
Al-Sayyid objected to it (the division) that it is a division that does not agree with the doctrine of the philosophers nor of the Imam, rather it is not sound in itself, and he demonstrated that by (the necessity) of absurdities, some of which the commentator transmitted; for he (the commentator) was deficient in transmitting the statement of the original text and the objection against it, and he claimed that it is a saying that became famous among the later scholars, whereas none of them said it, and they judged it to be corrupt.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage reports a critique by al-Sayyid (al-Sharif al-Jurjani) against the common division of knowledge into conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). The critique is that this division does not conform to the doctrine of the philosophers (al-hukama') nor of the Imam (likely al-Razi or al-Ghazali), and is not even intrinsically sound. Al-Sayyid demonstrates this by pointing out absurd consequences (muhadhir). The text then criticises the commentator (al-muhashshi) for inadequately transmitting both the original text's statement and the objection itself. The commentator allegedly claimed that this division became well-known among later scholars, yet none of them actually held it, and they judged it to be corrupt. This critical passage highlights that the common presentation of knowledge as either mere conception or conception-with-judgment is considered problematic and not endorsed by earlier authorities.

Key Terms

الإمام
محاذير

Key Takeaway

Perception with Taslim is Judgment
Author proves that perceiving the relation under taslim equals perceiving its actuality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the immediate inference that equates perceiving a relation with taslim to judging its actuality.

Core Idea
Taslim is not just belief; it is the very act of judging reality.

The matn author establishes a foundational identity: perceiving a propositional relation under the mode of taslim is precisely what constitutes judgment. This might seem trivial, but it prevents defining judgment tautologically. Let's unpack the logical move.

Guided Path
1
Identify the relations
The passage mentions two types: affirmative (positive) and negative relations. Note that each corresponds to a propositional content.
2
Define 'taslim' mode
Taslim is a mode of perception characterized by acquiescence and certainty, distinguished from mere conceptualization (tasawwur). Ask: what does it add?
3
See the immediate inference
The text asserts that if you perceive an affirmative relation with taslim, you have perceived it as actual. Similarly for negative. This is an immediate inference: taslim-perception directly entails judgment of actuality or non-actuality.
The inference is valid by definition of taslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا شك أن من أدرك النسبة الإيجابية على وجه يطلق عليه اسم التسليم فقد أدرك أنها واقعة وكذا من أدرك النسبة السلبية على الوجه المذكور فقد أدرك أنها ليست بواقعة.
And there is no doubt that whoever perceives the affirmative relation in a manner called taslim has indeed perceived that it is actual, and similarly whoever perceives the negative relation in the mentioned manner has indeed perceived that it is not actual.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a direct statement from the original text (matn) establishing the identity between perceiving a propositional relation with 'taslim' (acquiescence) and the act of judgment. The author argues that if a person perceives an affirmative relation (al-nisba al-ijabiyya) in the mode of taslim—which implies acceptance and certainty—then that person has necessarily perceived that the relation corresponds to reality (waqi'a). Likewise, if a person perceives a negative relation in that same mode, they have perceived that the relation does not correspond to reality. This is an immediate inference: the mode of perception (taslim) directly entails the content of judgment (actuality or non-actuality). The argument supports the earlier definition that judgment is precisely this kind of perception.

Key Terms
التسليم (al-taslim): A mode of perception characterized by acquiescence and certainty, distinguished from mere conceptualization [Note: In later works, taslim is often used interchangeably with tasdiq (assent), but here it specifies the manner of perception.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The relation is probably true
B) The relation is actual
C) The relation is merely imagined
D) The relation is false

Key Takeaway
Perception of a relation in the mode of taslim is not merely conceptual; it is identical to affirming or denying its reality.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
10 min
Judgment as Elementary Assent: Resolving Infinite Regress
Defines judgment and resolves infinite regress by elementary cognition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why defining judgment as 'perceiving that the relation is actual' leads to infinite regress and how the concept of elementary cognition (idh'an) resolves it.

Core Idea
Judgment is the elementary assent itself, not a second-order perception.

The text defines judgment as perceiving an affirmative or negative relation in a way that amounts to taslim (assent). But this definition seems to trigger an infinite regress: if judgment is perceiving that a relation is actual, then that perception itself is a new judgment requiring another perception, ad infinitum. The commentator resolves this by distinguishing between the elementary cognition (ijmālī) called idh'an and its detailed expression. Understanding this distinction is crucial for a sound epistemology in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of judgment in the matn
The matn states that whoever perceives the affirmative or negative relation in a way called 'taslim' has perceived that the relation is actual or not actual. This perception is the judgment (hukm). Note that 'taslim' denotes certainty.
The commentator explains that 'taslim' is a kind of idh'an (assent).
2
Locate the infinite regress objection
The commentator raises a problem: if judgment is defined as 'perceiving that the relation is actual', then that very perception is a new judgment (since it perceives a relation between the relation and actuality). This would require a further perception, leading to an infinite chain of judgments, which is impossible.
The objection is based on the definition of judgment as a perception of a relation's actuality.
3
Understand the resolution: elementary cognition
The answer is that the initial perception after knowing the two terms (subject and predicate) is an elementary (ijmālī) thing called idh'an. This elementary cognition is the judgment itself. When expressed in detail, it appears as a separate tasdiq, but the judgment is that elementary thing, as witnessed by conscience.
The resolution avoids infinite regress by denying that the judgment itself requires a second-order perception.
4
Apply the resolution to the commentator's suggestion on wording
The commentator notes that the relation is only described as affirmative or negative after attachment of affirmation/negation, so it would be better to use 'khabariyya' (predictive) to avoid confusion. This reflects the same concern: the judgment is not about the relation's property but a direct cognition.
This linguistic refinement prevents the mistaken inference of a second judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتن ولا شكّ أنَّ : مَنْ أدركَ النّسبة الإيجابيَّة على وجه يُطلَقُ عليه اسم التسليم ؛ فقد أدرك أنَّها واقعة وكذا مَنْ أدركَ النِّسبة السلبية على الوجه المذكور ؛ فقد أدرك أنَّها ليست بواقعة. (قَوْلُهُ : الْإِيْجَابِيَّةَ) وهي ثبوتُ الخبر للمبتدأ، والإيجابية نسبة للإيجاب من نسبة المتعلقِ بالفتح للمتعلق بالكسر ، وقد علمت المراد بالإيجاب . (قَوْلُهُ : فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ أَنَّهَا وَاقِعَةٌ) أي : وإذا كان كذلكَ ؛ فيكونُ إدراكُ النِّسبةِ على الوجهِ المذكور هو إدراك أنَّها واقعة أو غيرُ واقعةٍ وإدراك أنَّها واقعةٌ هو الحكم، فيكونُ إدراك النسبةِ على الوجه المذكور هو الحكم وهو المدَّعَى ، وكذا يُقالُ فيما بعد. (قَوْلُهُ : النِّسْبَةَ السَّلْبِيَّةَ هي : انتفاء القيام عن زيدٍ في : زيدٌ ليسَ بِقائم، والسَّلبيَّةُ نسبة لِلسَّلْبِ من حيثُ إنَّها مُتعلّقه، فهو من نسبة المتعلق بالفتح للمتعلّق بالكسرِ، وقد علمتَ المراد بالسَّلْب فيما مرَّ ، وَلَا تَتَصفُ النِّسبةُ بكونها إيجابيَّةً أو سلبيَّةً إِلَّا بعد تعلّقِ الإيجاب أو السَّلْبِ بها ، لا قبلَ ذلكَ كَما هو ظاهرُهُ، فَلَوْ حذفَ كُلًّا مِنَ الإيجابية والسَّلبيَّةِ وعبَّر بدلَهُما بالخبريَّةِ ؛ كانَ أَوْلَى. (قَوْلُهُ : وَلَمَّا كَانَ ... إلخ) جواب عن مخالفة المصنفِ القوم في التعبيرِ؛ حيثُ عبر هو بالإذعان، وهُمْ عبّرُوا بإدراكِ أنَّ النِّسبةَ واقعةُ أو ليسَتْ بواقعة. (قَوْلُهُ : مَا ذَكَرَهُ الْقَوْمُ أي : في تعريف الحكم من أَنَّهُ إدراكُ أَنَّ النِّسبة واقعةٌ، ) أو ليست بواقعة. والحُكْمُ الَّذي هو في بيانِهِ، فَهَهُنا تصديقٌ وحُكْمْ آخَرُ ، وهو أن تدركَ النَّفْسُ أَنَّ النِّسبة بين تلك النسبةِ وبين واقعةٍ؛ واقعةٌ، فيلزم هناك تصديق وحُكم ثالث، وهكذا؛ فيتوقَّفُ حصولُ حُكْم واحدٍ على أحكام غير متناهية، وهو باطل قطعاً، ومحصِّلُ الجوابِ أَنَّ المدرك بعد إدراكِ الطَّرفين أمرُ إجمالي يُقَالُ لَهُ : الإذعانُ إِذا عُبّر عنه بالتفصيل ؛ يظهرُ فيهِ تَصديقٌ آخَرُ ، والحُكْمُ هو ذلك المجملُ كما يشهدُ بِهِ الوجدان . (قَوْلُهُ: وَلَمَّا كَانَ مُحَصَّلُ مَا ذَكَرَهُ الْقَوْمُ ... إلخ) شروع في توجيه تقسيم. (قَوْلُهُ : رَاجِعَاً إِلَى الْإِذْعَانِ أي: لأنَّهُ كما سبق إدراك أنَّ النِّسبةَ واقعة أو ليسَتْ بواقعة على سبيل الجزم أو الظَّنِّ، فقوله: راجعاً إلى الإذعان؛ أي: بطريقِ اللُّزومِ. (قَوْلُهُ : عَبَّرَ عَنْهُ أي : عن محصّل ما ذكره القوم؛ أي: عن ملزومه.
The introduction of the author: And there is no doubt that whoever perceives the affirmative relation in a way that is called 'taslim' (submission/assent) has perceived that it is actual, and likewise whoever perceives the negative relation in the mentioned way has perceived that it is not actual. (His statement: 'the affirmative') It is the subsistence of the predicate for the subject, and 'affirmative' is a relation to 'affirmation' from the relation of the object (with fatha) to the subject (with kasra), and you have known the intended meaning of 'affirmation'. (His statement: 'so he has perceived that it is actual') That is: if it is so, then the perception of the relation in the mentioned way is the perception that it is actual or not actual, and the perception that it is actual is the judgment, so the perception of the relation in the mentioned way is the judgment, and that is the claim, and similarly one says in what follows. (His statement: 'the negative relation') It is the negation of standing of Zayd in 'Zayd is not standing', and 'negative' is a relation to 'negation' in that it is related to it, so it is from the relation of the object (with fatha) to the subject (with kasra), and you have known the intended meaning of 'negation' previously. And the relation is not described as affirmative or negative except after the attachment of affirmation or negation to it, not before that, as is apparent. So if he had omitted both 'affirmative' and 'negative' and expressed instead with 'predictive' (khabariyya), it would have been better. (His statement: 'And since the sum of what the people said... etc.') It is an answer to the author's opposition to the people in expression, because he expressed with 'idh'an' (assent), while they expressed with 'perceiving that the relation is actual or not actual'. (His statement: 'what the people said') That is, in their definition of judgment as perception that the relation is actual, or not actual. And the judgment that is in his explanation: here there is another tasdiq and judgment, which is that the soul perceives that the relation between that relation and actuality is actual, so there follows a third tasdiq and judgment, and so on, so the obtaining of a single judgment would depend on infinite judgments, which is absolutely false. And the summary of the answer is that the percept after perceiving the two extremes is an elementary (ijmali) thing called 'idh'an'; if expressed in detail, another tasdiq appears in it, and the judgment is that elementary thing, as witnessed by conscience. (His statement: 'And since the sum of what the people said... etc.') Beginning of directing the division. (His statement: 'referring back to idh'an') That is, because it is, as previously, a perception that the relation is actual or not actual with certainty or opinion, so his statement 'referring back to idh'an' is by way of implication. (His statement: 'he expressed it') That is, about the sum of what the people said, i.e., about its necessary consequence.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage begins with the author's definition of judgment. The matn states that whoever perceives an affirmative relation in the manner of taslim (assent) has perceived that it is actual, and similarly for negative relations. The commentator al-Dasuqi then explains the terms: 'affirmative relation' means the subsistence of the predicate for the subject, and the perception of the relation as actual is itself the judgment. He also argues that it would be better to use 'khabariyya' (predictive) instead of specifying affirmative/negative, because the relation only becomes affirmative/negative after attachment of affirmation/negation. Then al-Attar raises a problem: if judgment is perceiving a relation as actual, then that perception itself is a new judgment (that the relation is actual), which would require another perception, leading to infinite regress. The answer is that the perception after knowing the two terms is an elementary (ijmali) thing called idh'an; when expanded, it appears as a separate tasdiq, but the original judgment is that elementary cognition. Finally, al-Dasuqi explains that the author's use of 'idh'an' is by way of necessary implication (luzum) of the logicians' expression.

الحكم
التسليم
النسبة الإيجابية
النسبة السلبية

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

Why Tasdiq Must Be Defined as Idh'an
Defense of the author's definition of tasdiq as idh'an against the famous expression.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between assenting (tasdiq) and non-assenting perceptions (takhyil, shakk, wahm) and justify why the definition of tasdiq must exclude the latter.

Core Idea
Not every perception of a proposition's truth is assent; imagination, doubt, and presumption are not tasdiq.

In logic, tasdiq is judgment with assent. But some definitions inadvertently include perceptions that lack full commitment. The commentator defends the author's definition of tasdiq as idh'an (assent) over the famous expression, showing how it avoids including imaginative perception (takhyil), doubt (shakk), and presumption (wahm). This refinement is essential for precise reasoning in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing definitions
The famous expression defines tasdiq as 'perception that the relation is actual or not actual'. The author defines it as 'idh'an (assent) of the relation'. Locate these in the Arabic passage.
The author's definition comes from the division of perceptions.
2
Understand the three non-assenting perceptions
Takhyil is imagination of occurrence without hesitation or assent; shakk is doubt (both sides equal); wahm is presumption (one side weighted). These are perceptions of the proposition's truth value but without full commitment.
Abu al-Fath clarifies the meanings in the commentary.
3
Analyze the objection: the famous expression includes non-assenting perceptions
Al-Dawwani argues that the famous expression is too broad because one can 'perceive that the relation is actual' while imagining or doubting. That would incorrectly count as tasdiq.
The objection is that the definition fails to exclude takhyil, shakk, and wahm.
4
Evaluate the defense and counter-defense
A defender might say that 'perception that the relation is actual' implies assent. But Mir Zahid notes that the phrase 'occurrence or non-occurrence' (used in some variants) is ambiguous and does not guarantee idh'an. The author's explicit use of 'idh'an' avoids this.
The commentary discusses the weakness of the defense.
5
Conclude why the author's definition is superior
The author's definition is both brief and precise, capturing only assenting judgments. It serves as a reliable tool for distinguishing genuine belief from other cognitive states in Islamic logic.
The commentator favors the author's definition.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المصنف، واستحسان تعريف التصديق المستفاد من ذلك التقسيم بأنه إذعان للنسبة على صنيع القوم، ولم يعدل بين عبارة المصنف والأصل لما علمت من فسادها؛ فنزلت منزلة العدم، وحاصل ما ذكره من توجيه الاستحسان أمران؛ الأول: الاختصار، والثاني: التفرقة بين الإدراكين المتعلقين بالنسبة، فإنه يتعلق بهما علمان؛ أحدهما تصوري، والآخر تصديقي كما سيظهر، ووجه العلامة الدواني كلام المصنف بسلامة تعريف التصديق المستفاد منه عن عدم المنع بخلاف تعريف قال: عدل القوم عن العبارة المشهورة، وهي إدراك أن النسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعة؛ لأنه يدخل فيها التخييل، فإنه إدراك لوقوع النسبة أو لا وقوعها، وكذا الشك والوهم؛ ضرورة أن المدرك في جانب الوهم هو الوقوع أو اللاوقوع، إلا أن تلك الإدراكات ليست على وجه الإذعان والتسليم، بل على سبيل التخييل والتجويز ا.هـ. قال أبو الفتح: أراد بالتخييل؛ تصور الوقوع أو اللا وقوع من غير تردد ولا تجويز، والشك تصورهما على وجه التردد، والوهم تجويز أحدهما ظن الآخر، ويمكن دفع المناقشة عن العبارة المشهورة بأن المتبادر من إدراك أن النسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعة؛ إدراكها على وجه الإذعان كما يشعر به عنوان أن النسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعة بخلاف قولهم: وقوع النسبة أو لا وقوعها ا.هـ. وقد أشار مير زاهد لضعف هذا الجواب بقوله: وربما يظن أن التحييل والشك والوهم إدراك لوقوع النسبة أو لا وقوعها؛ لا لأن النسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعة، ولعل منشأ هذا الظن أخذ معنى الإذعان في الثاني دون الأول ا.هـ. فهذه مرجحات ثلاثة؛ اثنان للشارح وواحد للدواني، وهناك مرجحان آخران ذكراهما
The author, and his approval of the definition of tasdiq obtained from that division, that it is idh'an of the relation according to the practice of the people, and he did not equate between the author's expression and the original because you know its corruption; thus it descended to the level of non-existence. The summary of what he mentioned in directing the approval are two matters: the first: brevity, and the second: distinguishing between the two perceptions related to the relation, for two sciences relate to them: one is conceptual (tasawwuri) and the other is assenting (tasdiqi) as will appear. And al-Allama al-Dawwani interpreted the author's words as having the soundness of the definition of tasdiq derived from it from the lack of prevention, contrary to the definition he said: 'The people deviated from the famous expression, which is "perception that the relation is actual or not actual", because it includes takhyil (imaginative perception), for it is a perception of the occurrence of the relation or its non-occurrence, and likewise doubt and presumption; of necessity, the percept in the realm of presumption is occurrence or non-occurrence, except that those perceptions are not in the mode of idh'an and taslim, but rather in the mode of takhyil and tajwiz (imagination and permissibility).' end quote. Abu al-Fath said: 'By takhyil he meant conceptualization of occurrence or non-occurrence without hesitation or permission, and doubt is conceptualization of both in a hesitant manner, and presumption is permissibility of one of them with opinion of the other.' And it is possible to refute the objection against the famous expression by [saying] that the immediate understanding from 'perception that the relation is actual or not actual' is perceiving it in the mode of idh'an, as is suggested by the title 'that the relation is actual or not actual' contrary to their saying 'occurrence of the relation or its non-occurrence' end quote. And Mir Zahid alluded to the weakness of this answer by saying: 'Perhaps one might think that takhyil, doubt, and presumption are perception of the occurrence of the relation or its non-occurrence, not because the relation is actual or not actual, and perhaps the origin of this opinion is taking the meaning of idh'an in the second but not the first' end quote. So these are three preponderating factors: two by the commentator and one by al-Dawwani, and there are two other preponderating factors that they mentioned...
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary defending the author's definition of tasdiq as idh'an. The commentator begins by stating that the author approved the definition of tasdiq as 'idh'an of the relation' based on the division (of perceptions). The author did not equate his expression with the logicians' famous expression because the latter is flawed. Two reasons support this: brevity and distinguishing between conceptual and assenting knowledge. Al-Dawwani explains that the famous expression includes takhyil, shakk, and wahm, which are not in the mode of idh'an. Abu al-Fath clarifies these terms. A possible defense of the famous expression is given, but Mir Zahid points out its weakness. Thus, the author's definition is preferred.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

Distinguishing Tasawwur and Tasdiq by Essence, Not Object
Commentary explains the essential distinction between tasawwur and tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why tasdiq is essentially different from tasawwur, using the testimony of intuition (wijdan) and the concomitants of truth and falsehood.

Core Idea
Tasdiq and tasawwur are distinguished by essence, not by what they are about.

In this passage, al-Dawwani and Mir Abu al-Fath clarify a pivotal insight: tasdiq (assent) is not just a perception of a different object than tasawwur (conceptualization). Rather, both can perceive the same relation (nisba), but tasdiq adds a distinct mode—assent (idh'an)—which makes it essentially different. This deepens your understanding of how Islamic logicians define knowledge and sets the stage for later debates on the structure of propositions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing views on the distinction
The passage reports two camps: some say tasdiq and tasawwur differ by object (tasdiq perceives the occurrence/non-occurrence of a relation; tasawwur perceives only the terms or the relation itself). Others say both can perceive the same object, so the difference must be essential.
The second view is endorsed by the verifiers (muhaqqiqun).
2
Extract the verifiers' argument for essential distinction
The verifiers appeal to intuition (wijdan): direct introspection shows that one can conceive a proposition (e.g., 'The world is eternal') without assenting to it. The same object (the relation of eternity to the world) is present in both, but only tasdiq involves judgment (idh'an). The concomitants (lawazim) like truth-value further mark tasdiq as distinct.
Truth and falsehood apply only to tasdiq, not tasawwur.
3
Understand the author's choice of 'idh'an'
The author (of the matn) used 'idh'an' (assent) instead of the longer phrase 'knowledge that the relation holds or does not hold' to avoid implying that tasdiq includes imaginary or poetic statements that lack truth-value. This choice signals commitment to the essential distinction view.
Imagination (takhayyul) and poetry (shi'r) involve conceptualization but not assent.
4
Link to the debate on the parts of the proposition
Al-Attar explains that the same essential distinction underlies the dispute about the number of parts in a proposition. Later scholars posited two relations (the affirmative relation and its occurrence) yielding four parts; earlier scholars held one relation (union/non-union) with three parts. The verifiers side with the earlier view, consistent with the essential distinction: the single relation is the object, and tasdiq is the act of assenting to it.
This shows how the epistemological point has implications for propositional ontology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الدَّوَّانيُّ أيضاً: وفي هذا؛ أي: قولِ المصنّف العلم إنْ كانَ إذعاناً للنَّسبة ... إلخ؛ إشارة إلى تحقيق الأمر في المقام، وهو أنَّ التصديق نوع آخَرُ من الإدراكِ ؛ مُغَايرُ للتَّصورِ مُغايرةً ذاتيّةُ لا باعتبارِ المتعلِّقِ كما يشهدُ بِهِ الرُّجوع إلى الوجدانِ، وأنَّ التَصرُّرَ يتعلَّقُ أيضاً بِمَا يتعلَّقُ بِهِ التَّصديقُ، أعني أنَّ النِّسبةَ واقعةٌ أو ليست بواقعة ولا حجر فيه فيتعلَّق بكلِّ شيء. قال مير أبو الفتح: اختلفُوا في أَنَّ التَّصديق يمتاز عن التَّصورِ باعتبار المتعلّق أو لا، فَمِنهُم مَن قال : إنَّ التَّصرُّرَ لا يتعلَّق بما يتعلَّقُ بِهِ التَّصديقُ مِن وقوع النِّسبة أو لا وقوعها، بل إنَّما يتعلق بغيره من النسبة وأطرافها ، فالتصديق عندَهُم إدراك متعلّق بوقوعِ النِّسبة أو لا وقوعِهَا مُطلقاً، والتصوُّرُ إدراك متعلّق بغير ذلك، فيكون بينهما امتياز باعتبارِ المتعلّق أيضاً، ومِنهُم مَن قال: لا حجر في التَّصورِ بل يتعلق بما يتعلق به التصديقُ وغيرُهُ مِنَ الأشياء، فلا امتياز بينَهما إلا بحسب الذَّاتِ واللُّوازمِ كاحتمالِ الصدق والكذب دونَ المتعلَّق، وهذا هو الحقُّ عند المحققين بشهادةِ الوجدانِ الصَّادقِ، ولهذا ؛ عدلَ المصنِّفُ عَنِ العبارة المشهورة لإيهامها دخول التخييل والشَّلِّ والوهم فيها ؛ بناءً على ذلك المذهب الحقِّ. ثم قال العطار: يعني قولُ المصنفِ : العِلْمُ إِنْ كانَ إذعاناً . . . إلخ؛ إشارة إلى . . . أنَّهُ ليسَ بين طرفي القضية نسبتانِ؛ إحداهما : النِّسبةُ الحكميَّةُ الثبوتية، والأُخرى: وقوع تلكَ النِّسبة أو لا وقوعها كما ذهب إليه المتأخّرونَ، فتكونُ أجزاء القضيَّةِ عندَهُم أربعة بل بين طرفيها نسبةٌ واحدةٌ ؛ هِيَ اتحاد المحمول بالموضوع، أو عدم اتحادِهِ بِهِ مثلاً، كما هو اختيار المتقدِّمينَ؛ فتكونُ أجزاء القضيَّةِ عندَهُم ثلاثة، وهو الحقُّ عند المحققينَ بِشهادةِ الوجدان أيضاً.
Al-Dawwani also said: And in this—i.e., the author's statement 'knowledge, if it is assent to the relation... etc.'—is an indication of the verification of the matter in this context, and it is that assent (tasdiq) is another type of perception, essentially different from conceptualization (tasawwur), not by consideration of the object, as attested by recourse to true intuition, and that conceptualization also pertains to what assent pertains to, namely that the relation holds or does not hold, without restriction, so it pertains to everything. Mir Abu al-Fath said: They differed on whether assent is distinguished from conceptualization by consideration of the object or not. Some said that conceptualization does not pertain to what assent pertains to, namely the occurrence or non-occurrence of the relation, but rather pertains to other than that, such as the relation and its terms. So for them assent is a perception pertaining to the occurrence or non-occurrence of the relation absolutely, and conceptualization is a perception pertaining to other than that, so there is a distinction between them by object as well. And some said: There is no restriction on conceptualization; rather it pertains to what assent pertains to and other things, so there is no distinction between them except by essence and concomitants, such as the possibility of truth and falsehood, not by object. And this is the truth according to the verifiers, by the testimony of true intuition. For this reason, the author departed from the famous expression because it suggests the inclusion of imagination, poetry, and illusion in it, based on that true doctrine. Then al-Attar said: He means the author's statement 'Knowledge, if it is assent... etc.' is an indication that there are not two relations between the two terms of the proposition: one the affirmative judgmental relation, and the other the occurrence or non-occurrence of that relation, as the later scholars held, making the parts of the proposition four. Rather, between its two terms there is a single relation, which is the union of the predicate with the subject, or its non-union, for example, as is the choice of the earlier scholars, making the parts of the proposition three. And this is the truth according to the verifiers, also by the testimony of intuition.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the author's definition of knowledge as either conceptualization (tasawwur) or assent (tasdiq). The commentator al-Dawwani begins by affirming that the author's phrasing indicates a deeper point: that tasdiq is a type of perception essentially distinct from tasawwur, not merely different by its object. Both tasdiq and tasawwur can have the same object—namely, a judgment that a relation holds or does not hold. The difference is that tasdiq involves a particular mode of perception (assent), while tasawwur does not. Mir Abu al-Fath then reports the historical disagreement: some scholars held that tasdiq and tasawwur are distinguished by their objects—tasdiq is always about the occurrence or non-occurrence of a relation, while tasawwur is about other things like the terms of the relation. Others, including the 'verifiers' (muhaqqiqun), held that there is no restriction; tasawwur can also consider the very same object—the occurrence or non-occurrence of the relation—but without the element of judgment. Thus, the distinction is one of essence and inherent properties (lazim), such as the capacity for truth and falsehood, which belongs only to tasdiq. The author of the matn deliberately chose the word 'idh'an' (assent) over the more common phrase 'knowledge that the relation holds or does not hold' to avoid implying that imaginative or poetic statements (which lack truth-value) would be included. This choice signals the author's commitment to the view that tasdiq is essentially different. Finally, al-Attar explains that this same point underlies the dispute about the number of parts in a proposition. The later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) posited two relations: the affirmative relation linking subject and predicate, and the judgment that this relation holds or not—making the proposition have four parts. The earlier scholars (mutaqaddimun) held there is only one relation—the union or non-union of predicate with subject—making three parts. The verifiers side with the earlier view, again appealing to intuition. This discussion reinforces that tasdiq is not just another perception of a second relation, but a distinct epistemological act upon a single relation.

Key Terms
التصديق
التصور
النسبة
الإذعان
الوجدان

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq is a distinct perception of a relation with assent, while tasawwur can grasp the same relation without assent; they differ in essence, not object.

Distinguishing Conception from Assent: The Doubtful Proposition as Proof
Commentators explain the difference between conception of a relation and assent using the doubtful proposition as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why perception of a relation (idrak al-nisbah) and assent (idh'an al-nisbah) are essentially distinct, using the doubtful proposition as a proof.

Core Idea
Conception of a relation is not yet knowledge; assent requires judging its truth or falsehood.

In Islamic logic, a key epistemological distinction is made between merely conceiving a propositional relation (idrak al-nisbah) and assenting to it (idh'an al-nisbah). This lesson unpacks that distinction through the commentators' analysis of a doubtful proposition, where the relation is perceived but not judged. Understanding this difference is crucial for grasping the nature of knowledge and certainty in the Islamic intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cognitive acts
Locate the terms 'idrak al-nisbah' (perception of the relation) and 'idh'an al-nisbah' (assent to the relation) in the passage. Note that the former is a type of conception (tasawwur) and the latter a type of assent (tasdiq).
Pay attention to how commentators define each.
2
Understand the logical entailment
Extract the statement: 'every assent is a perception, but not every perception is an assent.' This means that assent necessarily includes perception, but the reverse is not true.
This is a key logical relation that grounds the essential distinctness.
3
Apply the doubtful proposition example
Consider the example of a doubtful proposition (al-jumla al-mashkuka). A person who doubts whether a relation holds definitely perceives the terms and the relation, but does not assent to either side. This shows that perception can exist without assent.
The example demonstrates the distinction in practice.
4
Compare essential vs. by-object distinctness
Note the commentators' point that the distinctness between perception and assent is essential (dhati), not merely by consideration of the object. This means they differ in their very nature, not just in what they are about.
This emphasizes the fundamental nature of the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المنطقية
وبين إذعانِ النِّسبة؛ الَّذي هو مِن قبيل التصديقِ. بأوضحِ وجه وأَوْجَزِ . فإِنَّ إدراكَ النّسبةِ على وجه يُطلَقُ عليه اسم التسليم، وإدراكَ النِّسبة فقط لا على هذا الوجه؛
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : إِذْعَانِ النِّسْبَةِ أي: إدراكِ أنَّها واقعةٌ أو ليسَتْ بواقعة. (قَوْلُهُ: بِأَوْضَحِ وَجْهِ) يتعلَّقُ بالفرقِ، وقوله: (وأوجزه)؛ أي: أخصره، ومصدوقُ ذلك الوجه الأوضح ؛ أنَّ إدراك النسبة تصور، وإذعانَها تصديق، وقولُهُ: (بأوضح وجه . . . إلخ)؛ أي: وأيضاً يلزمُ مِن إذعانِ النّسبة إدراكهَا وَلَا عكس؛ لأنَّ مُتعلِّقَ الإذعان كونُها واقعةً أو ليست بواقعةٍ، وهو أخصُّ مِن متعلّق إدراكِ النِّسبة، وهو ثبوت المحمول للموضوع؛ أي : تَعلَّقُهُ به · والحاصلُ : أَنَّ كُلَّ إذعان إدراك ، وليسَ كُلُّ إدراك إذعاناً ، تأمل.
(قَوْلُهُ : فَإِنَّ إِدْرَاكَ ... إلخ) أي : إِنَّما عبر المصنِّفُ بالإذعانِ؛ إثباتاً لِلفَرْقِ؛ لأنَّ إدراك النِّسبةِ ... إلخ، فهو علَّةٌ لِلمعلَّل مع علَّتِهِ ، أو إنَّما أثبت الفَرْقَ بينَهُما ؛ لأنَّ ... إلخ، فيكونُ علَّةٌ لِلعلَّة، فتدبَّرُ .
(قَوْلُهُ : لَا عَلَى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ) تفسير لقوله : (فقط).
العطار
المجملة، يعني قولُ المصنفِ : العِلْمُ إِنْ كانَ إذعاناً . . . إلخ؛ إشارة إلى . . . أنَّهُ ليسَ بين طرفي القضية نسبتانِ؛ إحداهما : النِّسبةُ الحكميَّةُ الثبوتية، والأُخرى: وقوع تلكَ النِّسبة أو لا وقوعها كما ذهب إليه المتأخّرونَ، فتكونُ أجزاء القضيَّةِ عندَهُم ،أربعة بل بين طرفيها نسبةٌ واحدةٌ ؛ هِيَ اتحاد المحمول بالموضوع، أو عدم اتحادِهِ بِهِ مثلاً، كما هو اختيار المتقدِّمينَ؛ فتكونُ أجزاء القضيَّةِ عندَهُم ثلاثة، وهو الحقُّ عند المحققينَ بِشهادةِ الوجدان أيضاً .ا.هـ. فَهذان مرجّحان، أيضاً يُضمَّانِ لِلخمسةِ السَّابقة، فتمَّتِ العدَّةُ سبعة .

مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتن
مُتغايرانِ سيَّما في الجملة الخبريَّةِ المشكَوكَةِ، فإنَّ المغايرةَ هنا بَلَغَتْ مبلغ الوضوح؛ لوجودِ إدراكِ النسبة فيها دون إذعانِها؛ إذِ الشَّاكُ في النسبةِ مُتَرَدِّدُ بين وقوعِها أَوْ اللاوقوعها ، فقد حَصَلَ لهُ إدراك النّسبة قطعاً، لكن لم يحصل له إذعانُها .
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : سِيَّمَا ) أي : خصوصاً التَّغايرُ في الجملة الخبرية المشكوكة، فسيَّما كلمة يؤتى بها ؛ للتنبيه على أولوية ما بعده بالحكم. (قَوْلُهُ : الْمَشْكُوْكَةِ أي : المشكوك في نسبتها ؛ هل هي واقعة أم لا؟. (قَوْلُهُ : فَإِنَّ الْمُغَايَرَةَ) أي : بين إدراكِ النِّسبة وإذعانها، وهو علَّةٌ لِسيَّما . (قَوْلُهُ : هُنَا ) أي : في الجملةِ المذكورة، وقضيّته : أنَّ فيها إدراكاً وإذعاناً، وأنَّ التَّغاير بينهما فيها واضحٌ ؛ مع أنَّهُ ليس فيها إذعان كما قالَ الشَّارِحُ بعد، لكنَّ المراد أنَّ الإذعان لم يوجد فيها مع وجودِ الإدراك فيها، فقد بلغَ التَّغايرُ في الوضوح غايته. (قَوْلُهُ : بَلَغَتْ مَبْلَغَ) أي: غايةَ الوضوح، وقوله: (لوجودِ)، علَّةٌ لتلغت.
(قَوْلُهُ : فِيْهَا ) أي : في الجملة المذكورة. (قَوْلُهُ : لَمْ يَحْصَلْ لَهُ إِذْعَانُهَا أي: إدراك أنَّها واقعةً أو ليست بواقعةٍ على سبيل الجزم أو الظَّنِّ ؛ إذ الشَّاكُ لا جزمَ ولا ظنَّ عنده .
العطار
=
(قَوْلُهُ: مُتَغَايِرَانِ تغايراً ذاتيا ؛ لا باعتبار المتعلِّقِ، قالَ السَّيِّدُ في شرح المواقفِ : إِنَّكَ إذا تصوَّرْتَ نسبة أمرٍ إلى آخَرَ وشكَكْتَ فيها؛ فقد عَلِمْتَ ذَينكَ الأمرين والنِّسبة بينَهُما قطعاً، فَلَكَ في هذه الحالة نوعٌ مِنَ العِلْمِ، ثمَّ إذا زالَ عنكَ الشَّدُّ وحكمْتَ بأحدِ طرفَي النِّسبةِ ؛ فقد عَلِمْتَ تلكَ النِّسبةَ نوعاً آخرَ مِنَ العِلْمِ؛ ممتازاً عن الأوَّلِ بحقيقته .ا.هـ. بل في حاشية الدَّوَّاني على الشّرحِ الجديد للتجريد ؛ أنَّ التَّصورات ليست مُتماثلة ولا التصديقات، بل تصرُّرُ كُلَّ مَفهومٍ يُغَايِرُ تصور مفهوم آخَرَ بحسبِ النَّوعِ، وكذا التصديق بكلِّ نسبةٍ يُغَايرُ التصديق بأُخرى بالنوع.
Logic
And between the assent to the relation, which is of the type of assent (tasdiq), with the clearest and shortest way. For the perception of the relation in a way that is called submission (taslim), and perception of the relation only not in this way.
Al-Dasuqi: (His saying: assent to the relation) meaning: perceiving that it occurs or does not occur. (His saying: with the clearest way) relates to the difference, and his saying: (and the shortest) meaning: the most concise. The referent of that clearest way is that perception of the relation is conception (tasawwur), and its assent is assent (tasdiq). And his saying: with the clearest way etc. means: also, from assent to the relation necessarily follows its perception, but not vice versa; because the object of assent is its being occurring or not occurring, which is more specific than the object of perception of the relation, which is the affirmation of the predicate for the subject, i.e., its connection to it. And the conclusion: every assent is a perception, but not every perception is an assent. Reflect.
(His saying: For the perception... etc.) means: The author only used the expression 'assent' to establish the difference; because the perception of the relation... etc., so it is a cause for the effect together with its cause, or he only established the difference between them because... etc., so it is a cause for the cause. So ponder.
(His saying: not in this way) is an interpretation of his saying: (only).
Al-Attar: The summary, i.e., the author's statement: Knowledge, if it is assent... etc., indicates that there are not two relations between the two extremes of the proposition; one: the judgmental affirmative relation, and the other: the occurrence or non-occurrence of that relation, as the later scholars held, so the parts of the proposition according to them are four; rather, between its two extremes is one relation: it is the union of the predicate with the subject or its non-union, for example, as is the choice of the earlier scholars; so the parts of the proposition according to them are three, and that is the truth according to the verifiers, by the testimony of intuition as well. End quote. So these are two preferences, also added to the previous five, so the number becomes seven.

Introduction of the author (matn): They are distinct, especially in the declarative doubtful proposition, for the distinctness here reaches the utmost clarity; due to the existence of perception of the relation in it without its assent; for the doubter regarding the relation is hesitant between its occurrence or non-occurrence, so he has definitely obtained the perception of the relation, but has not obtained its assent.
Al-Dasuqi: (His saying: especially) meaning: particularly the distinctness in the doubtful declarative proposition. 'Especially' is a word used to draw attention to the priority of what follows in ruling. (His saying: the doubtful) meaning: the one doubted in its relation; whether it occurs or not. (His saying: for the distinctness) meaning: between perception of the relation and its assent, and it is the cause for 'especially'. (His saying: here) meaning: in the mentioned proposition, and its implication is that there is perception and assent in it, and the distinctness between them is clear in it; although there is no assent in it as the commentator later said, but the intention is that assent is not found in it along with the existence of perception in it, so distinctness has reached its utmost in clarity. (His saying: reached the utmost) meaning: the extreme of clarity, and his saying: (due to the existence) is the cause for 'reached'. (His saying: in it) meaning: in the mentioned proposition. (His saying: he has not obtained its assent) meaning: perceiving that it occurs or does not occur with certainty or probability; for the doubter has neither certainty nor probability.
Al-Attar: (His saying: they are distinct) with an essential distinctness, not by consideration of the object. Al-Sayyid said in Sharh al-Mawaqif: When you conceive a relation of something to another and you doubt it, you have known those two things and the relation between them definitely, so you have in this state a kind of knowledge. Then when the doubt leaves you and you judge by one of the two sides of the relation, you have known that relation with another kind of knowledge, distinct from the first by its reality. End quote. Moreover, in the Hashiya of al-Dawwani on al-Sharh al-Jadid li al-Tajrid: that conceptions are not identical, nor are assents; rather, the conception of each concept is different in type from the conception of another concept, and likewise the assent to each relation is different in type from the assent to another.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological commentary on the distinction between perceiving a relation (idraki al-nisbah) and assenting to it (idh'an al-nisbah), which corresponds to the classical distinction between conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). The commentators clarify that the author's phrase 'assent to the relation' means perceiving that the relation either occurs or does not occur. The clearest way to distinguish them is that perception of a relation is conception, while assent to it is assent proper. They note a logical entailment: every assent necessarily includes perception, but not every perception rises to the level of assent. The example of a doubtful proposition (al-jumla al-mashkuka) is used to prove this: a person who doubts whether a relation holds definitely perceives the terms and the relation between them, but does not assent to either side. Thus, perception and assent are essentially distinct, not merely by consideration of the object. The passage also engages with a meta-debate about whether a proposition contains one relation (as the earlier scholars held) or two (as the later scholars held), concluding that the correct view is one relation, supporting the three-part proposition (subject, predicate, relation). This distinction is foundational for understanding the nature of knowledge and certainty in Islamic logic.

Checkpoint
In the doubtful proposition 'Will Zayd pray?', a person perceives the relation between Zayd and prayer but does not assent. What does this example demonstrate?
A) Perception and assent are identical.
B) Assent always requires perception but not vice versa.
C) Doubt is a type of assent.
D) The proposition has two separate relations.

Key Takeaway
Perception of a relation is necessary but not sufficient for assent; the doubtful proposition proves their essential distinctness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the doubtful proposition: 'Is the world eternal or created?' A person perceives the relation but does not assent. Write a short explanation of how this illustrates the essential distinctness between conception and assent, using the concepts of idrak al-nisbah and idh'an al-nisbah.
?
In Usul al-Fiqh, a mujtahid may conceive a ruling from a general text (e.g., 'All intoxicants are forbidden') without assenting to its applicability to a specific case (e.g., a new drug). Explain why this is possible using the logical entailment that every assent includes perception but not vice versa.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
5 min
Distinguishing Perception of Relation from Assent
Commentary explains difference between perceiving a proposition's relation and assenting, using doubtful sentence as clearest example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between idrak al-nisba and idh'an in any proposition, using the doubter's case as the clearest example.

Core Idea
Perception of a proposition's relation is distinct from assenting to it; doubt proves the difference.

In logic, it's crucial to separate understanding a statement from affirming or denying it. This lesson uses the case of doubt to show that one can perceive a proposition's relational content without assenting to it. The commentators elaborate on this essential distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two mental acts
Recognize that idrak al-nisba is mere understanding of the proposition (subject-predicate relation) without judgment, while idh'an is the affirmation or denial of that relation.
These are both types of knowledge but differ essentially.
2
Apply to the doubtful case
Consider the proposition 'Is zakat obligatory on all types of wealth?' The doubter understands the relation but does not affirm or deny it. This shows perception without assent.
The passage explicitly uses this example to highlight the difference.
3
Explain why the difference is essential
The commentators emphasize that the distinction is not merely by relation to objects but by essence (dhati). Al-Sayyid al-Sharif in Sharh al-Mawaqif illustrates: the same relation, when doubted, gives one type of knowledge; when judged, another type, distinct in essence.
Al-Dawwani adds that conceptualizations and assents differ by type, not just by content.
