مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتن
مُتغايرانِ سيَّما في الجملة الخبريَّةِ المشكَوكَةِ، فإنَّ المغايرةَ هنا بَلَغَتْ مبلغ الوضوح؛ لوجودِ إدراكِ النسبة فيها دون إذعانِها؛ إذِ الشَّاكُ في النسبةِ مُتَرَدِّدُ بين وقوعِها أَوْ اللاوقوعها ، فقد حَصَلَ لهُ إدراك النّسبة قطعاً، لكن لم يحصل له إذعانُها .
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : سِيَّمَا ) أي : خصوصاً التَّغايرُ في الجملة الخبرية المشكوكة، فسيَّما كلمة يؤتى بها ؛ للتنبيه على أولوية ما بعده بالحكم. (قَوْلُهُ : الْمَشْكُوْكَةِ أي : المشكوك في نسبتها ؛ هل هي واقعةٌ أم لا؟. (قَوْلُهُ : فَإِنَّ الْمُغَايَرَةَ) أي : بين إدراكِ النِّسبة وإذعانها، وهو علَّةٌ لِسيَّما . (قَوْلُهُ : هُنَا ) أي : في الجملةِ المذكورة، وقضيّته : أنَّ فيها إدراكاً وإذعاناً، وأنَّ التَّغاير بينهما فيها واضحٌ ؛ مع أنَّهُ ليس فيها إذعان كما قالَ الشَّارِحُ بعد، لكنَّ المراد أنَّ الإذعان لم يوجد فيها مع وجودِ الإدراك فيها، فقد بلغَ التَّغايرُ في الوضوح غايته. (قَوْلُهُ : بَلَغَتْ مَبْلَغَ) أي: غايةَ الوضوح، وقوله: (لوجودِ)، علَّةٌ لتلغت.
(قَوْلُهُ : فِيْهَا ) أي : في الجملة المذكورة. (قَوْلُهُ : لَمْ يَحْصَلْ لَهُ إِذْعَانُهَا أي: إدراك أنَّها واقعةً أو ليست بواقعةٍ على سبيل الجزم أو الظَّنِّ ؛ إذ الشَّاكُ لا جزمَ ولا ظنَّ عنده .
العطار
=
(قَوْلُهُ: مُتَغَايِرَانِ تغايراً ذاتيا ؛ لا باعتبار المتعلِّقِ، قالَ السَّيِّدُ في شرح المواقفِ : إِنَّكَ إذا تصوَّرْتَ نسبة أمرٍ إلى آخَرَ وشكَكْتَ فيها؛ فقد عَلِمْتَ ذَينكَ الأمرين والنِّسبة بينَهُما قطعاً، فَلَكَ في هذه الحالة نوعٌ مِنَ العِلْمِ، ثمَّ إذا زالَ عنكَ الشَّدُّ وحكمْتَ بأحدِ طرفَي النِّسبةِ ؛ فقد عَلِمْتَ تلكَ النِّسبةَ نوعاً آخرَ مِنَ العِلْمِ؛ ممتازاً عن الأوَّلِ بحقيقته .ا.هـ. بل في حاشية الدَّوَّاني على الشّرحِ الجديد للتجريد ؛ أنَّ التَّصورات ليست مُتماثلة ولا التصديقات، بل تصرُّرُ كُلَّ مَفهومٍ يُغَايِرُ تصور مفهوم آخَرَ بحسبِ النَّوعِ، وكذا التصديق بكلِّ نسبةٍ يُغَايرُ التصديق بأُخرى بالنوع.
وعند متأخّرِي المنطقِيِّينَ : إِنَّ التصديق مُركَّبٌ .
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : عِنْدَ مُتَأَخِّرِي ... إلخ) الحقِّ : أنَّ التصديق بسيط، وذلك لأنَّهُ مُستفادٌ مِنَ الحجة، والمستفاد منها إنَّما هو إدراك أنَّ النِّسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعةٍ، وأمَّا تصور المحكوم عليهِ وَبِهِ والنّسبة ؛ فإنَّما هوَ مُستفادٌ مِنَ القولِ الشَّارحِ : وأنَّ التَّحقيق أنَّ الحُكْمَ إدراك كما قالَهُ الشَّيخُ ياسين
وَقولُهُ : (عند متأخّري ... إلخ) معطوف على معنى ما تقدَّم ؛ أي: إِنَّ مَا تقدَّم من أنَّ التصديق هو الحكم فقط عند الحكماء وعند . . . إلخ، وَلَا فائدة للخلافِ ، إِلَّا أَنَّهُ على
الأوَّلِ إذا اختل شرطٌ ؛ فإنَّه يُسمَّى بالتصديق (۱) ، غاية الأمرِ أَنَّهُ يُقال له : تصديق فاسد . وعلى الثَّاني إذا اختلَّ شيءٌ مِنَ الشُّطورِ ؛ فلا يُقالُ له: تصديق أصلاً نظير الصَّلاةِ بغير وضوء، فإنَّه يُقال لها : صلاةٌ ; غاية الأمر أنَّها فاسدة، وإذا اختل ركن منها ; فَلَا يُقالُ: إِنَّ هناك صلاةٌ وُجِدَت هكذا ذكر بعض شيوخ شيخنا، وهو سيّدي مُحمَّد الصَّغير، وبعبارة(٢) قوله: (وعند متأخري ... إلخ)؛ أي: الإمام الرّازي ومَنْ تَبعَهُ ، والفرقُ بين المذهبين من وجوه :
أحدُها : أنَّ التَّصديق بسيط عند الحكماء ، ومركّب عند المتأخّرين .
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : وَعِنْدَ مُتَأَخِّرِي الْمَنْطِقِيِّينَ ومِنهُمُ الإمامُ الرَّازِيُّ، قالَ السَّيِّدُ : ومذهبُ الحكماء هو الحقُّ؛ لأنَّ تقسيم العِلْمِ إلى هَذَينِ القِسمَينِ إِنَّما هو لامتياز كل منهما عنِ الآخَرِ بطريق يتحصَّلُ بِهِ، ثمَّ إِنَّ الإدراك المسمَّى بالحكم ينفرد بطريق خاص يُوصل إليه وهو الحجَّةُ المنقسمة إلى أقسامِهَا ، وما عدا هذا الإدراك له طريق واحد يُوصِلُ إليه، وهو القولُ الشَّارحُ ; فتَصوُّرُ المحكوم عليه وتصور المحكوم به، وتصور النسبةِ الحكميَّة; يشارك سائر التَّصوراتِ في الاستحصال بالقول الشارح، فلا فائدةً
يسمى
(۱) (قَوْلُهُ : بالتصديق يرد عليه ما يأتي من أنها شروط وجود لا صحة فلا يتأتى وجود الحكم، بدونها، وحينئذ قياسه على الصلاة قياس مع الفارق .ا.هـ. الشَّرنوبي . (۲) (قَوْلُهُ : وبعبارة أخرى ... إلخ) كذا بالنسخة التي بأيدينا ولعلَّ فيها سقط كلمة ويعني» وبها يتضح المراد. ا.هـ. الشرنوبي.
Introduction of the author: They are different, especially in the doubtful declarative sentence, for the difference here reaches utmost clarity due to the existence of perception of the relation without assent to it; since the doubter about the relation is hesitating between its occurrence or non-occurrence, so he has definitely obtained perception of the relation, but has not obtained assent to it. al-Dusuqi: His statement: 'especially' means particularly the difference in the doubtful declarative sentence, so 'especially' is a word brought for alerting to the priority of what comes after in the ruling. His statement: 'the doubtful' means doubtful about its relation; is it occurring or not? His statement: 'for the difference' means between perception of the relation and assent to it, and it is the cause for 'especially'. His statement: 'here' means in the mentioned sentence, and its implication: that in it there is perception and assent, and that the difference between them is clear, even though there is no assent in it as the commentator said later, but the meaning is that assent does not exist in it while perception exists in it, so the difference reached its utmost clarity. His statement: 'reached the level of' means the utmost of clarity, and his statement: 'due to the existence' is the cause for 'reached'. His statement: 'in it' means in the mentioned sentence. His statement: 'he has not obtained assent to it' means perception that it is occurring or not occurring with certainty or opinion; for the doubter has no certainty nor opinion. al-'Attar: His statement: 'differing essentially', not by consideration of the relatum; al-Sayyid said in Sharh al-Mawaqif: When you perceive a relation of something to another and doubt it, you have definitely known those two things and the relation between them, so you have in this state a type of knowledge. Then when the doubt leaves you and you judge with one of the two sides of the relation, you have known that relation another type of knowledge, distinct from the first by its essence. End quote. Rather in the Hashiya of al-Dawwani on the new commentary on al-Tajrid, that concepts are not identical nor are assents, but rather the conceptualization of every concept differs from the conceptualization of another concept in type, and likewise the assent to every relation differs from the assent to another in type. And according to the later logicians: Assent is composite. al-Dusuqi: His statement: 'according to the later... etc.' The truth: that assent is simple, because it is derived from proof, and what is derived from proof is only the perception that the relation is occurring or not occurring. As for the conceptualization of the subject and predicate and the relation, it is derived from the explicative statement. And the verification is that judgment is perception as Shaykh Yasin said. And his statement: 'according to the later... etc.' is conjoined to the meaning of what preceded, i.e., what preceded that assent is only judgment according to the philosophers and according to... etc., and there is no benefit to the disagreement except that according to the first, if a condition is violated, it is called 'assent', at most it is said to be a flawed assent. And according to the second, if something of the conditions is violated, it is not called 'assent' at all, analogous to prayer without ablution, for it is called prayer, at most it is flawed; and if a pillar is missing, it is not said that there is a prayer that existed. Thus mentioned some of the teachers of our teacher, and he is my master Muhammad al-Saghir. And in other words, his statement: 'according to the later... etc.' means Imam al-Razi and those who followed him. And the difference between the two schools is in aspects: One of them: that assent is simple according to the philosophers, and composite according to the later ones. al-'Attar: His statement: 'and according to the later logicians', and among them is Imam al-Razi; al-Sayyid said: The school of the philosophers is the truth, because the division of knowledge into these two divisions is only for distinguishing each from the other by a method by which it is obtained. Then the perception called judgment is unique with a specific method that leads to it, which is proof divided into its types. And other than this perception has one method that leads to it, which is the explicative statement. So the conceptualization of the subject, the conceptualization of the predicate, and the conceptualization of the judgmental relation participate with other conceptualizations in being obtained by the explicative statement, so there is no benefit. (1) (His statement: 'by assent' there is an objection from what follows that they are conditions of existence not validity, so the existence of judgment does not occur without them, and in that case its analogy to prayer is an analogy with a difference. End quote from al-Sharnubi. (2) (His statement: 'and in other words... etc.') Thus in the copy we have, and perhaps there is a missing word 'meaning' and by it the meaning becomes clear. End quote from al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion about the distinction between mere perception of a proposition's relational content (idrak al-nisba) and full assent (idh'an) to it, and debates whether assent (tasdiq) is simple or composite. The text begins with the matn's statement: 'They are different, especially in the doubtful declarative sentence.' The commentator Dusuqi explains that 'especially' (siyyma) highlights the case of a doubtful proposition as the clearest example of the difference, because in doubt one certainly perceives the relation (e.g., 'Zayd is in the house?' one understands the proposition but does not affirm it). The difference is thus maximal: perception exists without assent. The commentator 'Attar adds that this is an essential difference (dhati), not merely by relation to objects. He quotes al-Sayyid al-Sharif from Sharh al-Mawaqif: when you conceive a relation and doubt it, you have one type of knowledge (mere conception); when you then judge one side, you have another type of knowledge (assent), distinct in essence. Additionally, al-Dawwani's hashia on al-Tajrid holds that concepts differ by type, and likewise assents to different relations differ by type. Then the text notes a disagreement: the later logicians (muta'akhkhirun, e.g., al-Razi) consider assent composite, while the earlier philosophers (hukama') consider it simple. Dusuqi argues for simplicity: assent is derived from proof (hujja), which only gives the perception of the relation's occurrence or non-occurrence; the conceptualization of subject, predicate, and relation comes from definition (qawl sharh). He likens the disagreement to prayer: if a condition (e.g., wudu) is missing, the prayer is still called prayer but flawed; if a pillar (rukn) is missing, it is not called prayer at all. According to the first view (conditions are for validity), flawed tasdiq is still tasdiq; according to the second (conditions are for existence), it is not. 'Attar confirms that al-Sayyid and the truth are with the philosophers: because knowledge is divided into concept and assent by the distinct methods of obtaining them—judgment uniquely via proof, other concepts via definition. The footnote by al-Sharnubi notes a possible flaw in the prayer analogy. Overall, the passage clarifies the nature of tasdiq and the criteria for its validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a doubtful proposition about whether a particular act is obligatory, the doubter has which of the following?
A) Both perception of the relation and assent to it.
B) Neither perception nor assent.
C) Perception of the relation but not assent.
D) Assent but not perception.

Key Takeaway
The undeniable difference between perception of a relation and assent is most evident in doubt, where perception exists without assent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the proposition 'The world is temporally originated.' Explain the difference between perceiving its relation and assenting to it. Then, give an example from Islamic theology where a doubter would have perception without assent.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
advanced
7 min
Is Assent Simple or Composite? The Debate on Tasdiq
Commentary discusses the debate on whether tasdiq is simple or composite and its implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the simple and composite views of tasdiq and apply their consequences regarding flawed judgments.

Core Idea
The nature of assent (tasdiq) as simple or composite changes whether a flawed judgment still counts as assent.

The later logicians (muta'akhkhirun) held that tasdiq is composite, including the conceptualization of subject, predicate, and relation, plus the judgment. The earlier philosophers considered it simple—just the judgment itself. This disagreement has practical consequences: does a defective argument yield any kind of tasdiq? This lesson unpacks that debate using the analogy of prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Philosophers (hukama') say tasdiq is simple: the act of judgment alone. Later logicians (e.g., al-Razi) say it is composite: includes conceptualization of subject, predicate, relation, plus judgment.
The difference is whether the conceptual parts are conditions for existence or for validity.
2
Identify the sources of each view
The philosophers' view is attributed to early thinkers like Ibn Sina; the later view to Imam al-Razi and his followers.
Al-'Attar says al-Sayyid al-Sharif considers the philosophers' view correct.
3
Explain the consequence using the prayer analogy
If tasdiq is composite (like prayer with pillars), missing a condition means it still exists but is flawed; missing a pillar means it does not exist. If simple, missing any condition means no tasdiq.
The analogy: prayer without wudu is still prayer but flawed; without a rukn, it is not prayer.
4
Evaluate which view the commentators prefer
Al-Dusuqi calls the simple view 'al-haqq' (the truth). Al-'Attar quotes al-Sayyid that the philosophers' view is correct because the division of knowledge into concept and assent is based on distinct methods of acquisition.
The footnote by al-Sharnubi notes a potential flaw in the analogy, but doesn't overturn the preference.

(قَوْلُهُ : بَلَغَتْ مَبْلَغَ) أي: غايةَ الوضوح، وقوله: (لوجودِ)، علَّةٌ لتلغت.
(قَوْلُهُ : فِيْهَا ) أي : في الجملة المذكورة. (قَوْلُهُ : لَمْ يَحْصَلْ لَهُ إِذْعَانُهَا أي: إدراك أنَّها واقعةً أو ليست بواقعةٍ على سبيل الجزم أو الظَّنِّ ؛ إذ الشَّاكُ لا جزمَ ولا ظنَّ عنده .

(قَوْلُهُ: مُتَغَايِرَانِ تغايراً ذاتيا ؛ لا باعتبار المتعلِّقِ، قالَ السَّيِّدُ في شرح المواقفِ : إِنَّكَ إذا تصوَّرْتَ نسبة أمرٍ إلى آخَرَ وشكَكْتَ فيها؛ فقد عَلِمْتَ ذَينكَ الأمرين والنِّسبة بينَهُما قطعاً، فَلَكَ في هذه الحالة نوعٌ مِنَ العِلْمِ، ثمَّ إذا زالَ عنكَ الشَّدُّ وحكمْتَ بأحدِ طرفَي النِّسبةِ ؛ فقد عَلِمْتَ تلكَ النِّسبةَ نوعاً آخرَ مِنَ العِلْمِ؛ ممتازاً عن الأوَّلِ بحقيقته .ا.هـ. بل في حاشية الدَّوَّاني على الشّرحِ الجديد للتجريد ؛ أنَّ التَّصورات ليست مُتماثلة ولا التصديقات، بل تصرُّرُ كُلَّ مَفهومٍ يُغَايِرُ تصور مفهوم آخَرَ بحسبِ النَّوعِ، وكذا التصديق بكلِّ نسبةٍ يُغَايرُ التصديق بأُخرى بالنوع.

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion about the distinction between mere perception of a proposition's relational content (idrak al-nisba) and full assent (idh'an) to it, and debates whether assent (tasdiq) is simple or composite. The text begins with the matn's statement: 'They are different, especially in the doubtful declarative sentence.' The commentator Dusuqi explains that 'especially' (siyyma) highlights the case of a doubtful proposition as the clearest example of the difference, because in doubt one certainly perceives the relation (e.g., 'Zayd is in the house?' one understands the proposition but does not affirm it). The difference is thus maximal: perception exists without assent. The commentator 'Attar adds that this is an essential difference (dhati), not merely by relation to objects. He quotes al-Sayyid al-Sharif from Sharh al-Mawaqif: when you conceive a relation and doubt it, you have one type of knowledge (mere conception); when you then judge one side, you have another type of knowledge (assent), distinct in essence. Additionally, al-Dawwani's hashia on al-Tajrid holds that concepts differ by type, and likewise assents to different relations differ by type. Then the text notes a disagreement: the later logicians (muta'akhkhirun, e.g., al-Razi) consider assent composite, while the earlier philosophers (hukama') consider it simple. Dusuqi argues for simplicity: assent is derived from proof (hujja), which only gives the perception of the relation's occurrence or non-occurrence; the conceptualization of subject, predicate, and relation comes from definition (qawl sharh). He likens the disagreement to prayer: if a condition (e.g., wudu) is missing, the prayer is still called prayer but flawed; if a pillar (rukn) is missing, it is not called prayer at all. According to the first view (conditions are for validity), flawed tasdiq is still tasdiq; according to the second (conditions are for existence), it is not. 'Attar confirms that al-Sayyid and the truth are with the philosophers: because knowledge is divided into concept and assent by the distinct methods of obtaining them—judgment uniquely via proof, other concepts via definition. The footnote by al-Sharnubi notes a possible flaw in the prayer analogy. Overall, the passage clarifies the nature of tasdiq and the criteria for its validity.

Key Terms
التصديق
بسيط
مركب
القول الشارح
الحجة

A) Composite, including conceptualization and judgment.
B) Simple, just the judgment itself.

Key Takeaway
The debate over the simplicity of tasdiq has real implications for whether faulty reasoning can still produce valid assent.

The Simple vs. Composite Nature of Assent (Tasdiq)
Dispute over the composition of assent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two positions (philosophers vs. later logicians) on the nature of tasdiq and explain the difference between a condition (shart) and a part (shatr) in this context.

Core Idea
Is assent the judgment alone or inclusive of its terms? The answer changes what counts as defective.

This passage introduces a fundamental dispute in Islamic logic: is tasdiq (assent) a simple act of judgment, or does it include the three concepts (subject, predicate, relation)? The early philosophers held the simple view, while later logicians like al-Razi argued for composition. Understanding this dispute is crucial for evaluating definitions and proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two schools
Locate the names: hukama' (philosophers) and muta'akhkhirun (later logicians). Note key figures such as al-Razi and the commentators.
Al-Dasuqi begins by stating the later logicians' position.
2
Extract the core claim
What does each school say about the simplicity or complexity of tasdiq? For philosophers, tasdiq is the judgment alone; for later logicians, it includes the three concepts.
The text explicitly says: 'assent is simple according to the philosophers and composite according to the later ones.'
3
Compare shart vs. shatr
How do the two schools differ on the status of the three concepts? Philosophers consider them conditions (shurut) external to tasdiq; later logicians consider them parts (ashjar) internal to it.
This distinction is the key point of difference.
4
Note the consequence for defective tasdiq
According to each school, if a condition or part is missing, is it still called tasdiq? For philosophers, it is tasdiq but defective; for later logicians, it is not tasdiq at all.
The prayer analogy in the text illustrates this.

السرير، مع
And according to the later logicians: indeed, assent is composite.
Al-Dasuqi: (His statement: 'According to the later... etc.') The truth is that assent is simple, and that is because it is derived from the argument, and what is derived from it is only the perception that the relation occurs or does not occur. As for the conception of the subject, predicate, and relation, it is derived from the explanatory statement. And the verification is that the judgment is a perception, as Shaykh Yasin said. And his statement: (According to the later... etc.) is conjoined to the meaning of what preceded, i.e., what preceded that assent is only judgment according to the philosophers and according to... etc., and there is no benefit to the disagreement except that on the first view, if a condition is violated, it is still called assent (1), at most it is said to be defective assent. On the second view, if any of the parts is violated, it is not called assent at all, analogous to prayer without ablution: it is called prayer, at most it is defective, but if a pillar is violated, it is not said that there is a prayer. Thus mentioned some of the teachers of our teacher, and he is my master Muhammad al-Saghir. And in another expression (2): his statement: (According to the later... etc.) i.e., Imam al-Razi and those who followed him. And the difference between the two schools is in several aspects: One of them: that assent is simple according to the philosophers, and composite according to the later ones.
Al-'Attar: (His statement: And according to the later logicians, and among them Imam al-Razi. Al-Sayyid said: The doctrine of the philosophers is the truth, because the division of knowledge into these two divisions is only for distinguishing each from the other by the path by which it is obtained. Then indeed, the perception called judgment is unique in having a special path that leads to it, which is the argument divided into its parts. What is other than this perception has a single path that leads to it, which is the explanatory statement. So the conception of the subject, the conception of the predicate, and the conception of the judgmental relation share with other conceptions in acquisition by the explanatory statement, so there is no benefit in joining them to the judgment and making the whole one division of knowledge called assent, because this whole does not have a special path. So whoever observes the purpose of the art, namely the explanation of the paths leading to knowledge, it will not be ambiguous to him that the necessary in its division is to observe the distinction in the paths, so the judgment is one of its two divisions called assent, but it is conditional in its existence upon multiple things from individuals of the other division. End. 'Abd al-Hakim said: And one may say that this perception, because it is related to the relation related to the two extremes in that it is an instrument for observing them, is like the form for the string that produces a single real thing. Just as what is obtained externally is that the act only attaches to the form, similarly what is obtained after the argument is the whole. And if acquisition is attached to the mentioned perception, just as its object, namely the predicative relation, is like the form for the proposition, by which the whole, namely the two extremes and the relation, becomes a single real thing distinct from each of the two extremes and the relation, while what is obtained after the two extremes is only the relation. So just as they made the two extremes and the relation parts of the known, similarly knowledge, and what is the reason for opposing knowledge to the known and making the mentioned things a condition in the first and a part in the second? And after your thorough understanding of what we said, it appears to you that the dispute about assent is verbal. So whoever looks at the fact that what is obtained after the argument is only the mentioned perception said: the bed, with

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary (hashiya) by al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar on a sharh of a logic text (likely Tahdhib). It addresses the epistemological dispute over the nature of tasdiq (assent): is it a simple perception of the judgment (hukm) or does it include the three concepts (subject, predicate, and relation)? The authors present two views: the early philosophers (hukama') hold that tasdiq is simple, merely the judgment, while the later logicians (muta'akhkhirun), led by Imam al-Razi, hold that it is composite, including the three concepts. Al-Dasuqi begins by stating that the truth is that tasdiq is simple, because it is obtained from the argument (hujja), which yields only the perception of the relation's occurrence or non-occurrence. The three concepts are obtained from the explanatory statement (qawl sharh), not from the argument. He then explains the practical consequence: if tasdiq is simple and a condition (shart) is missing, it is still called tasdiq but defective (fasid), analogous to prayer without ablution—still prayer but defective. If a component (rukn) is missing, it is not called prayer at all. On the composite view, if any part (shatr) is missing, it is not called tasdiq at all. Al-'Attar confirms that the philosophers' view is correct because the division of knowledge (ilm) into conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq) is based on the path of acquisition. Judgment has a unique path (the argument), while the concepts share a single path (the explanatory statement). Therefore, including the concepts in tasdiq would make it lack a special path, violating the division's purpose. Al-Dasuqi then lists three differences between the schools: (1) simplicity vs. composition; (2) the three concepts are conditions (shurut) external to the essence of tasdiq for the philosophers, but internal parts (ashjar) for the later logicians; (3) the judgment is the entire tasdiq for the philosophers, but only a part for the later logicians. Both agree that the three concepts are needed, but differ on the nature of that need. Finally, al-Dasuqi mentions a key consequence: for the later logicians, tasdiq can be a priori (badihi) only if all its parts are a priori; while for the philosophers, it suffices that the judgment itself is a priori, even if the concepts are theoretical (nadhari). Al-'Attar continues with a more intricate discussion suggesting that the dispute is verbal: what is obtained after the argument is the judgment, but the judgment necessarily involves the relation between extremes, so the whole is a single real entity. The passage ends abruptly but emphasizes the verbal nature of the conflict.

Checkpoint
According to the later logicians (muta'akhkhirun), if one of the three concepts (subject, predicate, relation) is missing from a judgment, is it still called tasdiq?
A) Yes, but it is defective.
B) No, it is not called tasdiq at all.
C) Yes, it is called tasdiq if the judgment itself is present.
D) It depends on whether the missing concept is a condition or a part.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over tasdiq's composition hinges on whether the three concepts are considered conditions (external) or parts (internal), with practical consequences for defective knowledge and a priori status.

?

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

Is the Dispute Merely Verbal? The Final Position
Assessment of the dispute as verbal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the claim that the dispute over tasdiq is verbal (lafzi) and explain the reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
The dispute about tasdiq may be only about words, not about reality.

After presenting the two views on tasdiq, the passage suggests that the disagreement may be merely verbal (lafzi). This lesson unpacks the argument that the philosophers' position is more consistent with the division of knowledge, and that the later logicians' composition view may be a matter of terminology. Understanding this helps avoid false dichotomies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim that the dispute is verbal
Find where the passage explicitly says 'the dispute about assent is verbal' (النزاع في التصديق لفظي). This is the thesis of this part.
The text states near the end: 'ظهر لك أن النزاع في التصديق لفظي'
2
Understand the reasoning based on the division of knowledge
The passage argues that the division of knowledge into conception and assent is based on the path of acquisition. The judgment has a unique path (the argument), so it alone constitutes the division of assent. The three concepts share a path with other conceptions, so including them would mix paths.
Al-'Attar quotes al-Sayyid: 'the perception called judgment is unique in having a special path...'
3
Consider the counterargument from unification
The passage also presents a view that the whole (subject, predicate, relation) is a single real entity because the relation unifies the extremes, analogous to a string's form producing one melody. This suggests composition is real.
This is from 'Abd al-Hakim's comment.
4
Assess the outcome: verbal dispute
Despite the appearance of a real disagreement, the author concludes it is verbal because both sides agree that the three concepts are needed; they only differ on whether to label them as conditions or parts. The essence of tasdiq remains the judgment.
The verbal nature means that the practical consequences remain, but the ontological claim is less important.

(قَوْلُهُ : وَعِنْدَ مُتَأَخِّرِي الْمَنْطِقِيِّينَ ومِنهُمُ الإمامُ الرَّازِيُّ، قالَ السَّيِّدُ : ومذهبُ الحكماء هو الحقُّ؛ لأنَّ تقسيم العِلْمِ إلى هَذَينِ القِسمَينِ إِنَّما هو لامتياز كل منهما عنِ الآخَرِ بطريق يتحصَّلُ بِهِ، ثمَّ إِنَّ الإدراك المسمَّى بالحكم ينفرد بطريق خاص يُوصل إليه وهو الحجَّةُ المنقسمة إلى أقسامِهَا ، وما عدا هذا الإدراك له طريق واحد يُوصِلُ إليه، وهو القولُ الشَّارحُ ؛ فتَصوُّرُ المحكوم عليه وتصور المحكوم به، وتصور النسبةِ الحكميَّة؛ يشارك سائر التَّصوراتِ في الاستحصال بالقول الشارح، فلا فائدةً

في ضَمِّهَا إلى الحكم وجعل المجموع قسماً واحداً مِنَ العِلْمِ مُسَمّى بالتصديقِ؛ لأنَّ هذا المجموع ليسَ لَهُ طريق خاص، فَمَن لاحظ مقصودَ الفَنِّ، أعني : بيانَ الطَّرِقِ الموصلة إلى العِلْم لم يلتبس عليهِ أنَّ الواجب في تقسيمه ملاحظة الامتياز في الطُّرقِ، فيكونُ الحُكْمُ أحد قسميه المسمى بالتصديقِ، لكنَّهُ مَشروط في وجودِهِ إلى أمورٍ متعدّدةٍ مِن أفرادِ القسم الآخرِ ا.هـ. ، قال عبد الحكيم : وَلِقَائِل أن يقول : إِنَّ ذلك الإدراك لكونه متعلقاً بالنسبة المتعلقة بالطَّرفين من حيثُ إِنَّهَا الةٌ لِمُلاحظتها بمنزلة الهيئة للشرير المحصلة للأمر الواحِدِ الحقيقي، فَكَمَا أَنَّ الحاصل في الخارج أنَّ الفعل لم يتعلَّق إلا بالهيئة؛ فكذلك الحاصل بعد الحجَّةِ هو المجموع، وإذا كان الاكتساب مُتعلّقاً بالإدراك المذكور، كما أنَّ مُتَعلِّقَهُ، أعني: النِّسبة الخبريَّةَ، بمنزلة الهيئة للقضيَّةِ، بِسببها صارَ الكُلُّ، أعني : الطَّرفَيْنِ والنِّسبة؛ أمراً واحداً حقيقيّاً مُغَايراً لِكُلِّ واحدٍ من الطَّرفين والنّسبة، مع أنَّ الحاصل بعد الطَّرفين ليس إلا النسبة، فَكَما جعلُوا الطَّرفين والنّسبة أجزاء مِنَ المعلوم؛ فكذلكَ العِلْم، وما وجهُ مُخالفةِ العِلْمِ بالمعلوم وجعل الأمور المذكورة شرطاً في الأوَّلِ وشَرطاً في الثَّاني، وأنتَ بعد إحاطتِكَ بما قُلْنَا ؛ ظهرَ لكَ أَنَّ النّزاعَ في التصديقِ لفظي، فَمَنْ نظر إلى أنَّ الحاصل بعد الحجّةِ ليس إلا الإدراك المذكورُ ؛ قالَ
السرير، مع
And according to the later logicians: indeed, assent is composite.
Al-Dasuqi: (His statement: 'According to the later... etc.') The truth is that assent is simple, and that is because it is derived from the argument, and what is derived from it is only the perception that the relation occurs or does not occur. As for the conception of the subject, predicate, and relation, it is derived from the explanatory statement. And the verification is that the judgment is a perception, as Shaykh Yasin said. And his statement: (According to the later... etc.) is conjoined to the meaning of what preceded, i.e., what preceded that assent is only judgment according to the philosophers and according to... etc., and there is no benefit to the disagreement except that on the first view, if a condition is violated, it is still called assent (1), at most it is said to be defective assent. On the second view, if any of the parts is violated, it is not called assent at all, analogous to prayer without ablution: it is called prayer, at most it is defective, but if a pillar is violated, it is not said that there is a prayer. Thus mentioned some of the teachers of our teacher, and he is my master Muhammad al-Saghir. And in another expression (2): his statement: (According to the later... etc.) i.e., Imam al-Razi and those who followed him. And the difference between the two schools is in several aspects: One of them: that assent is simple according to the philosophers, and composite according to the later ones.
Al-'Attar: (His statement: And according to the later logicians, and among them Imam al-Razi. Al-Sayyid said: The doctrine of the philosophers is the truth, because the division of knowledge into these two divisions is only for distinguishing each from the other by the path by which it is obtained. Then indeed, the perception called judgment is unique in having a special path that leads to it, which is the argument divided into its parts. What is other than this perception has a single path that leads to it, which is the explanatory statement. So the conception of the subject, the conception of the predicate, and the conception of the judgmental relation share with other conceptions in acquisition by the explanatory statement, so there is no benefit in joining them to the judgment and making the whole one division of knowledge called assent, because this whole does not have a special path. So whoever observes the purpose of the art, namely the explanation of the paths leading to knowledge, it will not be ambiguous to him that the necessary in its division is to observe the distinction in the paths, so the judgment is one of its two divisions called assent, but it is conditional in its existence upon multiple things from individuals of the other division. End. 'Abd al-Hakim said: And one may say that this perception, because it is related to the relation related to the two extremes in that it is an instrument for observing them, is like the form for the string that produces a single real thing. Just as what is obtained externally is that the act only attaches to the form, similarly what is obtained after the argument is the whole. And if acquisition is attached to the mentioned perception, just as its object, namely the predicative relation, is like the form for the proposition, by which the whole, namely the two extremes and the relation, becomes a single real thing distinct from each of the two extremes and the relation, while what is obtained after the two extremes is only the relation. So just as they made the two extremes and the relation parts of the known, similarly knowledge, and what is the reason for opposing knowledge to the known and making the mentioned things a condition in the first and a part in the second? And after your thorough understanding of what we said, it appears to you that the dispute about assent is verbal. So whoever looks at the fact that what is obtained after the argument is only the mentioned perception said: the bed, with
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary (hashiya) by al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar on a sharh of a logic text (likely Tahdhib). It addresses the epistemological dispute over the nature of tasdiq (assent): is it a simple perception of the judgment (hukm) or does it include the three concepts (subject, predicate, and relation)? The authors present two views: the early philosophers (hukama') hold that tasdiq is simple, merely the judgment, while the later logicians (muta'akhkhirun), led by Imam al-Razi, hold that it is composite, including the three concepts. Al-Dasuqi begins by stating that the truth is that tasdiq is simple, because it is obtained from the argument (hujja), which yields only the perception of the relation's occurrence or non-occurrence. The three concepts are obtained from the explanatory statement (qawl sharh), not from the argument. He then explains the practical consequence: if tasdiq is simple and a condition (shart) is missing, it is still called tasdiq but defective (fasid), analogous to prayer without ablution—still prayer but defective. If a component (rukn) is missing, it is not called prayer at all. On the composite view, if any part (shatr) is missing, it is not called tasdiq at all. Al-'Attar confirms that the philosophers' view is correct because the division of knowledge (ilm) into conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq) is based on the path of acquisition. Judgment has a unique path (the argument), while the concepts share a single path (the explanatory statement). Therefore, including the concepts in tasdiq would make it lack a special path, violating the division's purpose. Al-Dasuqi then lists three differences between the schools: (1) simplicity vs. composition; (2) the three concepts are conditions (shurut) external to the essence of tasdiq for the philosophers, but internal parts (ashjar) for the later logicians; (3) the judgment is the entire tasdiq for the philosophers, but only a part for the later logicians. Both agree that the three concepts are needed, but differ on the nature of that need. Finally, al-Dasuqi mentions a key consequence: for the later logicians, tasdiq can be a priori (badihi) only if all its parts are a priori; while for the philosophers, it suffices that the judgment itself is a priori, even if the concepts are theoretical (nadhari). Al-'Attar continues with a more intricate discussion suggesting that the dispute is verbal: what is obtained after the argument is the judgment, but the judgment necessarily involves the relation between extremes, so the whole is a single real entity. The passage ends abruptly but emphasizes the verbal nature of the conflict.

The Two Conceptions of Judgment (Hukm): Perception vs. Act
Author discusses whether hukm is an act or a perception and its implications for tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the ancient and later logicians' definitions of hukm and explain how each affects the composition of tasdiq.

Core Idea
Is judgment an act or a perception? Your answer changes how many components tasdiq has.

In this passage, the author refines a crucial epistemological distinction in Islamic logic: whether hukm (judgment) is a perception (idrak) or an act (fi'l). This determines the structure of tasdiq (assent), the core of knowledge. We will unpack the two positions and their implications for how tasdiq is composed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of hukm
Find in the Arabic where the author states 'judgment is either perception or act'. Note that perception is associated with the ancients (al-mutaqaddimun), act with the later logicians (al-muta'akhkhirun).
The author explicitly links each definition to a school.
2
Understand the consequence for tasdiq
According to the commentator's resumption: if hukm is an act, tasdiq = 3 perceptions + act; if perception, tasdiq = 4 perceptions. This shows how the nature of hukm affects the components of knowledge.
The later view reduces the number of perceptions but adds an act.
3
Trace the disagreement
The author clarifies that the disagreement is between ancients and later logicians, not only among later ones. Note the examples: 'corrupt tasdiq' vs. not called tasdiq at all when conditions are lacking.
This mirrors how prayer is classified when conditions or parts are missing.
4
Apply the distinction
Consider a simple proposition like 'The world is created'. Under each view, would it be considered knowledge? How many components? Write down the composition for each school.
This exercise solidifies the structural difference.

والحكم: إما إدراك، أو فِعْل. وذكر بعض الأشياخ فائدةً أُخرى وهي أنَّه على مذهب الحكماء يُقالُ لَهُ: تصديقٌ، وإن اختلَّ بعضُ الشُّروط، غاية الأمر أنَّهُ عند الاختلال يُقالُ له : تصديق فاسد، وعلى مذهب المتأخّرينَ؛ لَا يُقالُ له تَصديق إلَّا إذا وُجِدَت الشُّطور، فإن اختلَّ شيءٌ منها؛ فَلَا يُقالُ له تصديق. ... إذا علمت هذا؛ فقولُ الشَّارح: (الحكم إمَّا إدراك)؛ أي: وهو ما قاله المتقدّمونَ، وقولُهُ: (أو فعل)؛ أي: وهو قول المتأخرين؛ أي: لأنَّهم قالُوا : إِنَّ الحكم هو الإيقاع والانتزاع والإيجابُ والسَّلْبُ، وهذه أفعال، فليس الخلافُ في كون الحكم فعلاً أو إدراكاً بين المتأخرين فقط كما قد يتوهم من عبارة الشارح، بل الخلافُ فيما بينهم وبين المتقدمين. وأُجيب : بأنَّ قولَ الشَّارح : (والحكمُ . . . إلخ) استئناف، فكأَنَّه قال : ثمَّ إِنَّ قُلْنَا بقولِ المتأخّرينَ مِنْ أنَّ الحكم فِعْل؛ فالتَّصديقُ مُركَّب من ثلاثةِ تصورات وفعل، وإنْ قُلْنَا بقول المتقدِّمينَ مِنْ أَنَّهُ إدراكٌ؛ كانَ مُركَّباً من أربعة إدراكات.
And judgment: either it is a perception or an act. Some scholars mentioned another benefit: that according to the school of the philosophers, it is called tasdiq even if some conditions are lacking; at most, when lacking it is called corrupt tasdiq. According to the later [logicians], it is not called tasdiq unless the conditions are present; if something is lacking, it is not called tasdiq. ... If you know this, then the commentator's saying: 'Judgment is either perception' means it is what the ancients said, and his saying 'or act' means it is the saying of the later [logicians], because they said that judgment is positing, abstracting, affirming, and negating, and these are acts. So the disagreement is not about whether judgment is act or perception only among the later [logicians] as might be understood from the commentator's expression; rather, the disagreement is between them and the ancients. And it was answered: that the commentator's saying 'Judgment... etc.' is a resumption, as if he said: then if we adopt the saying of the later [logicians] that judgment is an act, then tasdiq is composed of three perceptions and an act; and if we adopt the saying of the ancients that it is perception, then it is composed of four perceptions.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage refines the understanding of the term 'hukm' (judgment) in logic. The author begins by stating that judgment is either a perception (idrak) or an act (fi'l). He then explains a benefit: according to the philosophers (al-hukama', i.e., the ancients), the term tasdiq (assent) can be applied even if some conditions are missing, in which case it is called 'corrupt tasdiq'. According to the later logicians (al-muta'akhkhirun), tasdiq is only called such when all conditions are met. This is analogous to prayer: if a condition like purity is missing, it is still called prayer but corrupt; whereas if a part is missing, it is not called prayer at all. The author then clarifies that the disagreement about whether judgment is an act or perception is not only among the later logicians, as might be assumed, but between them and the ancients. The later logicians hold that judgment is an act (e.g., positing, abstracting, affirming, negating). The response (Ajib) explains that the commentator's statement is a resumption: if we adopt the later view, tasdiq consists of three perceptions plus an act; if we adopt the ancients' view, it consists of four perceptions. This shows how the nature of hukm affects the composition of knowledge.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm): The mental act or perception that affirms or negates a proposition; the central element in tasdiq. [Note: In earlier texts, hukm is often seen as a perception; later logicians redefined it as an act.]
التصديق (al-tasdiq): Assent or belief in the truth of a proposition, composed of either three perceptions and an act (later view) or four perceptions (ancients' view). [Note: The definition of tasdiq shifts depending on whether hukm is considered an act or perception.]

B) Three perceptions and an act
C) Two perceptions and two acts
D) One perception and one act

Key Takeaway
The classification of judgment as perception or act changes the number of components in tasdiq from four to three plus an act.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

The Composition of Tasdiq: Four Concepts or Four Perceptions?
Author states conditional on hukm being idrak, then commentary on composition of tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the composition of tasdiq as a compound of four cognitions and distinguish between the broad and narrow uses of 'tasawwur' in Islamic logic.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is not a simple act; it is a compound of four cognitions, including judgment as one of its parts.

This lesson examines a foundational passage in Islamic logic about the structure of assent (tasdiq). The author presents a conditional: if judgment is a form of perception, then tasdiq must consist of four concepts. The commentary by al-Dasuqi clarifies the terminological issues and defends the author's choice. By understanding this composition, you will gain insight into how Muslim logicians conceived of the mind's knowledge processes.

Guided Path
1
Locate the conditional in the matn
Find the phrase 'فإن كان إدراكاً فالتصديق مركب من تصورات أربعة'. Identify the antecedent (if judgment is perception) and consequent (tasdiq is composed of four concepts).
2
Understand al-Dasuqi's preferred terminology
Al-Dasuqi suggests that the author should have said 'four perceptions' rather than 'four concepts' because 'tasawwur' normally excludes judgment. Why does this terminological precision matter?
It affects how we classify judgment within the framework of cognition.
3
Compare two views on tasdiq and hukm
One view equates tasdiq with hukm, making the three concepts mere conditions. The other view holds that tasdiq is composed of three concepts plus a distinct judgment. Trace how each view affects the classification of judgment.
4
See the logical necessity of hukm being a concept on the second view
If tasdiq has parts and judgment is a part, and if judgment is a perception, then it must be a concept (tasawwur) because it cannot be tasdiq (part ≠ whole) nor an intermediate (no such entity).
This shows the internal coherence of the author's position.
5
Connect to al-'Attar's definition of tasdiq as submission
Al-'Attar adds that tasdiq is submission (inqiyad) and acceptance (qabul), not an act. This reinforces that tasdiq is a cognitive state, not a voluntary action.
This confirms the non-act nature of tasdiq.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتنِ
فإنْ كانَ إدراكاً ; فالتَّصديقُ مُركَّبٌ مِنْ تَصوراتٍ أربعة :
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : مِنْ تَصَوُّرَاتٍ أَرْبَعَةٍ) أرادَ بالتَّصورِ مُطلق صورة الشيء الحاصلة في العقل فيشمل الحكم، ولكنْ كانَ الأَوْلَى أنْ يقول : من إدراكات أربعة; لأنَّ التَّصوَّرَ إذا أُطلق; لا ينصرفُ إلَّا لِمَقابل الحكم، بخلافِ الإدراكِ; فإنَّهُ يتناولُ الحكم ومُقابلَه مِنَ التَّصوراتِ الثَّلاثة ، كَذَا قِيلَ . وفيهِ : أَنَّ كونَ التَّصورِ إذا أُطلِقَ; إِنَّما ينصرفُ لِمقابل الحكم، إنَّما هو على قول الحكماء : إنَّ التَّصديق هو الحكم، وإنَّ التَّصوراتِ الثَّلاثة شروط لوجودِهِ، أما على القول بأنَّ التَّصديقَ مُركَّبُ مِنَ التَّصوراتِ الثَّلاثةِ والحكم، وقُلْنَا : إنَّ الحكم إدراك، فيتعيَّنَ أنْ يكونَ الحكم - وهو إدراك أنَّ النِّسبة واقعة أو ليست بواقعة - تصوُّراً، كما قالَ الشَّارحُ ; إذ لا يجوز أنْ يكونَ تصديقاً; لأنَّه جزؤه، ولا يجوز أن يكونَ واسطةٌ بينَ التَّصورِ والتَّصديق ; إذْ لا قائل بها .
العطار
به، ومعناه الانقيادِ والقبول، ولا ترجع إلى فِعْل أصلاً ; كما يشهدُ بِهِ الوجدانُ الصَّحيحُ ا.هـ.
Introduction of the author: If (judgment) is perception, then affirmation is composed of four concepts. Al-Dasuqi: (His statement: from four concepts) He intended by 'concept' the absolute image of the thing present in the mind, so it includes judgment. But it would have been better for him to say 'from four perceptions' because when 'concept' is used unrestrictedly, it only refers to what is opposed to judgment, unlike 'perception' for it encompasses judgment and its opposite from the three concepts. Thus it is said. And in it (the response): That the restriction of 'concept' when used absolutely to what is opposed to judgment is only according to the philosophers' statement that affirmation is judgment, and the three concepts are conditions for its existence. As for the statement that affirmation is composed of the three concepts and judgment, and we say that judgment is perception, then it necessarily follows that judgment – which is the perception that the relation is real or not real – is a concept, as the commentator said; for it cannot be an affirmation because it is part of it, nor can it be an intermediary between concept and affirmation as no one holds that. Al-'Attar: (The meaning is) submission and acceptance, and it does not go back to an act at all, as sound intuition witnesses. End.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement that if judgment (hukm) is a form of perception (idrak) rather than an act, then affirmation (tasdiq) is composed of four concepts (tasawwurat). Al-Dasuqi first clarifies that the author uses 'tasawwur' broadly to mean any mental image, including judgment. However, he notes that it would be more precise to say 'four perceptions' (idrakat) because the term 'tasawwur' normally, when used without qualification, excludes judgment and is contrasted with it. He then addresses a potential objection: the restriction of tasawwur to exclude judgment only holds on the view that tasdiq is itself judgment and that the three concepts are merely conditions for it. But on the alternative view that tasdiq is composed of three concepts and a judgment, and if we also hold that judgment is a kind of perception, then judgment itself becomes a concept (since it is a perception of the relation) and cannot be a tasdiq (because it is a part) nor an intermediary. Al-'Attar adds that the assent (tasdiq) referred to in the matn is nothing but submission and acceptance, and it is not an act (fi'l) at all, as confirmed by sound intuition. This discussion is foundational for understanding the structure of knowledge in Islamic logic, where tasdiq is the mental act of affirming a proposition and is distinguished from mere conception.

حكم
إدراك

B) Four
C) Five

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq is a composite mental state that includes judgment as one of its four components, and the term 'tasawwur' can be used broadly to include judgment.

The Four Conceptions Composing Tasdiq
Author defines tasdiq as composed of four tasawwurat and explains each component.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four conceptual components of tasdiq (assent) and distinguish each component's role in a proposition.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is not a simple act; it is a composite of four interrelated conceptions.

The author of the matn asserts that tasdiq (assent) is not a single mental event, but rather a compound consisting of four distinct conceptions. This lesson unpacks each component: the subject, the predicate, the judgment relation, and the judgment itself. Understanding this structure is crucial for analyzing how propositions convey knowledge in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four named components
Locate in the Arabic where the author lists the four tasawwurat. Notice the terms: تصور المحكوم عليه, تصور المحكوم به, تصور النسبة الحكمية, والتصور الذي هو الحكم.
These are the four parts that make up any tasdiq (assent).
2
Distinguish the conception from the object
The commentator clarifies that 'conception of the subject' means the mental image, not the actual subject. For example, in 'Zaid is standing', the conception of Zaid is the mental representation of Zaid, not Zaid himself.
This distinction is key to understanding the epistemological nature of the components.
3
Understand how the judgment is itself a conception
The fourth component, the judgment (hukm), is also a mental image. The author explains that the judgment is a conception because it is a perception in the mind, not a separate act.
This is a shift from the usual contrast between tasawwur and hukm.
4
Apply to a simple proposition
Take a proposition like 'The world is created'. Identify each of the four conceptions: the subject (world), the predicate (created), the judgment relation (the nexus of creation), and the judgment itself (the act of affirming).
Practicing with different examples solidifies the concept.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتنِ فإنْ كانَ إدراكاً؛ فالتَّصديقُ مُركَّبٌ مِنْ تَصوراتٍ أربعة: تصور المحكوم عليه، وتصور المحكوم به، وتصور النسبة الحكمية، والتصور الذي هو الحكم. وإنما وقع التصور موصوفاً بالحكم، ومضافاً إلى سائر الأجزاء؛ لأن التصور المحكوم عليه ليس بعينه هو المحكوم عليه. (قَوْلُهُ: تَصَوُّرُ الْمَحْكُوْمِ عَلَيْهِ) في الحقيقة؛ أجزاء التصديقِ المتصوَّرات من حيثُ إِنَّها مُتصوَّرات، فقولهم: تصوُّرُ المحكوم عليه؛ أي: متصوّر هو المحكوم عليه، فزيد من: زيد قائم، من أجزاء التصديقِ مِن حيثُ إِنَّه متصوَّر، وكذا يُقالُ في تَصور المحكوم به والنِّسبةِ، كذا قرَّرَ شيخُنَا العدوي نقلاً عن شيخه سيدي محمد الصغير، والشَّيخ عيد. وإذا تأمَّلْتَهُ تجده يرجعُ لِمَا قُلْنَاه من أنَّ المراد بالتّصورِ؛ الصُّورةُ الحاصلة في العقل؛ إذ المتصوَّرُ من حيثُ إِنَّه مُتصوّر هو الصُّورة المذكورة، وحينئذ فقوله: (تصور المحكوم عليه) أي: صورة المحكوم عليه، والصُّورة التي هي الحكم... إلخ. (قَوْلُهُ: مَوْصُوْفَاً بِالْحُكْمِ) أي: في قولِهِ والتَّصور الَّذِي هو الحكم، فإِنَّ الموصول صفةٌ لِلتَّصور. (قَوْلُهُ: وَمُضَافَاً ... إلخ) أي في قولِهِ: تصوُّرُ المحكوم عليه، وتصور المحكوم به، وتصور النسبة، فقد وقع التّصور مُضافاً للنِّسبةِ وَمَا معها. (قَوْلُهُ: هُوَ الْمَحْكُوْمُ عَلَيْهِ) أي: لأنَّ المحكوم عليه المتصوَّر؛ أي: الذَّات الَّتي تصوَّرت لا نفْس التَّصورِ الذي هو صورتها الحاصلة في العقل، وكذا يُقالُ فيما
Introduction of the author of the text: If it is perception, then assent (tasdiq) is composed of four conceptions: the conception of the subject of judgment, the conception of the predicate, the conception of the judgment relation, and the conception which is the judgment itself. And the term 'conception' is described by the judgment and added to the other parts only because the conception of the subject of judgment is not identical to the subject of judgment itself. (His saying: 'the conception of the subject of judgment') in reality, the parts of assent are conceived things insofar as they are conceived. So their saying 'conception of the subject of judgment' means: a conceived thing that is the subject of judgment. For example, Zaid in 'Zaid is standing' is a part of assent insofar as it is conceived. Similarly, it is said regarding the conception of the predicate and the relation. Thus our teacher al-‘Adawi established, transmitting from his teacher Sayyidi Muhammad al-Saghir and al-Shaykh ‘Aid. And if you reflect, you find it returns to what we said: that what is meant by 'conception' is the image present in the mind, for the conceived thing insofar as it is conceived is that image. And so his saying 'conception of the subject of judgment' means: the image of the subject of judgment, and the image that is the judgment... etc. (His saying: 'described by the judgment') meaning in his statement 'and the conception which is the judgment', for the relative clause is an attribute of the conception. (His saying: 'and added... etc.') meaning in his statement: 'conception of the subject of judgment, conception of the predicate, conception of the relation', for the term 'conception' occurs as an addition to the relation and what is with it. (His saying: 'it is the subject of judgment') meaning: because the subject of judgment is the conceived thing; that is, the essence that is conceived, not the conception itself which is its image present in the mind. And similarly it is said regarding the rest.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage defines tasdiq (assent) and breaks it down into its four conceptual components. The matn states: 'If it is perception, then tasdiq is composed of four conceptions.' The commentator then enumerates the four: (1) the conception of the subject of judgment (mahkum 'alayh), (2) the conception of the predicate (mahkum bihi), (3) the conception of the judgment relation (nisba hukmiyya), and (4) the conception which is the judgment (hukm) itself. The commentator clarifies that the term 'tasawwur' here is used broadly to refer to any mental image, including the judgment. He explains that the fourth component is called a conception because the judgment is itself a mental perception. The commentator al-Dasuqi then elaborates: the parts of tasdiq are considered 'tasawwurat' in terms of their being perceptions, not in terms of their specific content. For example, in the proposition 'Zaid is standing', the mental image of Zaid is a conception, the mental image of standing is a conception, and the nexus of judgment is also a conception. He emphasizes that 'conception of the subject of judgment' means the image of the subject, not the subject itself. This distinction ensures that all components are mental representations. The passage is fundamental for understanding the epistemological structure of propositions in Islamic logic.

Objection: If Tasawwurat Are Necessary, Tasdiq Cannot Be Theoretical
Author raises an objection from Imam al-Razi against the definition of tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Imam al-Razi's objection against the definition of tasdiq and evaluate the logical consistency of the exhaustive division of knowledge.

Core Idea
If all concepts are necessary, then no theoretical assent is possible — a logical contradiction that forces a redefinition of judgment.

This passage presents a critical objection attributed to Imam al-Razi, challenging the standard definition of tasdiq (assent) as composed of four tasawwurat (conceptions). The objection exposes a tension between the necessary nature of tasawwurat and the theoretical nature of many assents. Understanding this critique is essential for grasping the epistemological foundations of Islamic logic and the limits of the tasawwur/tasdiq dichotomy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target definition
What is the definition of tasdiq that is being criticized? It is the definition of tasdiq as a compound of four tasawwurat (conceptions).
2
Extract the key premise
What does Imam al-Razi hold about all tasawwurat? He holds that all conceptions are necessary (daruri), i.e., known without reflection.
3
Find the conditional argument
If all tasawwurat are necessary, and tasdiq is composed of tasawwurat, then tasdiq would also be necessary. But tasdiq can be theoretical (nazari) — a contradiction.
4
Identify the escape route
The passage suggests making judgment (hukm) a distinct type of perception not reducible to conception or assent. What does this do to the exhaustive division of knowledge?
5
Evaluate the proposed response
The author suggests that judgment could be identical to assent, preserving the exhaustive division. Does that solve the objection?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نُسِبَ إلى الإمام في أحدِ قَولَيْهِ، واعترض بأنَّ الإمام ذهب إلى أنَّ التَّصوراتِ كُلَّها ضَروريَّةٌ، والتَّصديقُ قد يكونُ نَظريًّا، فلو كانَ الحُكْمُ عندَهُ إدراكاً أيضاً؛ لَزِمَ أن تكون التصديقات كلُّها ضَروريَّةٌ أيضاً؛ اللَّهُمَّ إلَّا أن يجعلَ الحُكْم نوعاً مِنَ الإدراك غيرَ النَّصور والتَّصديقِ؛ فيبطل انحصارُ العِلْم فيهما، والمشهور الانحصار. ويمكن أن يُجَابَ بِجواز أن يكونَ الحُكْم نوعاً مِنَ الإدراك غيرَ النَّصور والتَّصديقِ، ويبقى انحصار العِلْم فيهما على القول بأن الحكم ليس جزءاً من التصديق بل هو التصديق نفسه؟
It is attributed to the Imam in one of his two statements, and it is objected that the Imam held that all conceptions are necessary, while assent may be theoretical. If judgment in his view is also perception, then it would be necessary that all assents are also necessary — unless he makes judgment a type of perception other than conception and assent, which would invalidate the exhaustive division of knowledge into them, while the exhaustive division is well-known. And it is possible to answer by permitting that judgment is a type of perception other than conception and assent, and the exhaustive division of knowledge into them remains on the view that judgment is not a part of assent but is assent itself?
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the definition of tasdiq as a compound of four tasawwurat, attributed to Imam al-Razi. The objection states: Imam al-Razi held that all tasawwurat (conceptions) are necessarily known (daruri), but tasdiq (assent) can be theoretical (nazari). If the judgment (hukm) is also considered a perception (idrak), then since the components of tasdiq are all necessary, the resulting assent would also be necessary. This contradicts the fact that many assents are theoretical. The only way out is to claim that judgment is a third type of perception distinct from both conception and assent, but this breaks the well-known exhaustive division of knowledge into conception and assent. The author suggests a possible answer: allow that judgment is a distinct type of perception, and the exhaustive division still holds if one maintains that judgment is not a part of assent but identical to assent itself. The passage critically examines the consistency of the definition with established epistemological classifications.

The Four Tasawwurat That Constitute Tasdiq
Author enumerates the four tasawwurat that make up tasdiq and explains their relationship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four components of assent and explain why the judgment (hukm) is considered a type of perception rather than a separate image.

Core Idea
Assent is composed of four images, and the judgment is the very perception that ties them together.

In this passage, the author lays out the building blocks of tasdiq. Rather than being a single act, tasdiq is a composite of four distinct mental images: the subject, the predicate, the relational judgment, and the judgment as perception. Understanding these components is crucial for grasping how logical propositions are formed and how definitive knowledge (yaqin) is produced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four tasawwurat listed
The passage explicitly lists four images: (1) the image of the subject (al-mahkum 'alayhi), (2) the image of the predicate (al-mahkum bihi), (3) the image of the relational judgment (al-nisba al-hukmiyya), and (4) the image that is the judgment itself (al-tasawwur alladhi huwa al-hukm). Note the order and phrasing.
The fourth is described not as an image of the judgment, but as the image that is the judgment.
2
Distinguish between image and thing
The author points out that the image of the subject is not identical to the subject itself. Similarly for the predicate and the relational judgment. This justifies calling each component an 'image' (tasawwur) even though they are mental representations.
This distinction prevents confusion between mental concepts and external realities.
3
Locate the judgment's special status
The passage explains that the perception (idrak) obtained after imaging the subject, predicate, and relation is the very judgment itself. Therefore, the judgment is not an additional image but the act of perceiving the connection.
The author uses 'al-tasawwur alladhi huwa al-hukm' to express that this image is identical to the judgment.
4
Confirm the moment of tasdiq
Once this judgment-perception occurs, tasdiq (assent) is achieved. The author adds that tasdiq does not depend on imaging that perception again—meaning the judgment is self-validating once the components are in place.
This emphasizes that tasdiq is the final result, not an extra layer of reflection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١. تصور المحكوم عليه . ٢. وتصور المحكوم به . ٣. وتصور النسبة الحكمية . ٤. والتصور الذي هو الحكم . وإنما وقع التصور موصوفاً بالحكم، ومضافاً إلى سائر الأجزاء؛ لأن التصور المحكوم عليه ليس بعينه هو المحكوم عليه . وكذا : تصور المحكوم به، وتصور النسبة الحكمية . وأما الإدراك الذي حصل لنا بعد تصور الطرفين والنسبة؛ فهو عين الحكم؛ فلذا جعل الحكم صفة له، فقيل : التصور الذي هو الحكم. ثم إذا حصل هذا الإدراك؛ حصل التصديق، ولم يتوقف على تصور ذلك الإدراك.
1. The image of the subject. 2. The image of the predicate. 3. The image of the relational judgment. 4. The image that is the judgment. And indeed the term 'image' occurs described by the judgment and added to the other parts because the image of the subject is not identical to the subject itself. Likewise: the image of the predicate and the image of the relational judgment. As for the perception that we obtain after imaging the two extremes and the relation, it is the very judgment; therefore the judgment is made a description of it, so it is said: the image that is the judgment. Then when this perception occurs, the assent occurs, and it does not depend on imaging that perception.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage defines the four components (tasawwurat) that constitute an act of assent (tasdiq). The author lists them: (1) the mental image of the subject, (2) the image of the predicate, (3) the image of the relational judgment (nisba hukmiyya), and (4) the image that is the judgment itself. He then explains that the term 'tasawwur' applies to all four because the image of the subject is not the same as the actual subject. The fourth component is the perceptual act that occurs after one has imaged the subject, predicate, and relation; this perception is the judgment itself. Finally, the author states that once this judgment-perception occurs, the assent (tasdiq) is produced, and that tasdiq does not require a separate imaging of that judgment-perception. This clarifies that the judgment is not an independent image but the very act of affirming.

Refining Tasdiq: Judgment as Conception or Act?
Al-Dasuqi and al-Attar refine the debate on whether judgment is a conception or an act in tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two views on the nature of judgment (ḥukm) within taṣdīq and explain why the conception view avoids infinite regress.

Core Idea
Tasdiq's judgment is either a conception or an act; only the conception view avoids regress.

In this passage, al-Dasūqī and al-‘Aṭṭār refine the definition of taṣdīq by analyzing whether the judgment (ḥukm) that completes assent is itself a conception or an act. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping how knowledge is structured in Islamic logic, especially in epistemology and the foundations of theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Find where the text states the view that judgment is a perception/conception vs. that it is an act. The first view is introduced by al-‘Aṭṭār: 'الحكم عنده إدراكا من قبيل التصور' (the judgment according to him is a perception of the type of conception). The second is indicated by 'وإن كان فعلا' (if it is an act).
2
Analyze the conception view
Notice that on this view, judgment is a conception, and taṣdīq occurs automatically after conceiving subject, predicate, and relation, without needing to conceive the judgment itself. The text says: 'ثم إذا حصل هذا الإدراك؛ حصل التصديق، ولم يتوقف على تصور ذلك الإدراك' (Then when this perception occurs, assent occurs, and it does not depend on the conception of that perception).
This avoids infinite regress.
3
Examine the regress argument
Understand why requiring a separate conception of the judgment would lead to infinite regress. Al-Dasūqī explains: 'لأن تصور تلك التصورات يحتاج أيضا إلى تصور، وتصوره يحتاج إلى تصور آخر وهكذا' (Because the conception of those conceptions also needs a conception, and its conception needs another conception, and so on). The text argues that this regress does not apply because the conception of judgment is exceptional.
Al-‘Aṭṭār adds that this type of conception is not subject to the rule that all conceptions are necessary.
4
Contrast the act view
See the alternative: if judgment is an act (fi‘l), then taṣdīq is composed of three conceptions plus the act. The text discusses how acts can be characterized as intuitive (badīhī) or acquired (kasbī), responding to the objection that acts cannot be intuitive.
This view avoids the regress problem by making judgment a separate act, not requiring conception.

مُقَدِّمَةُ الماتن وكذا: تصور المحكوم به، وتصور النسبة الحكمية. وأما الإدراك الذي حصل لنا بعد تصور الطرفين والنسبة؛ فهو عين الحكم؛ فلذا جعل الحكم صفة له، فقيل: التصور الذي هو الحكم. ثم إذا حصل هذا الإدراك؛ حصل التصديق، ولم يتوقف على تصور ذلك الإدراك. الدسوقي بعد؛ أي: ولما كان تصور المحكوم عليه غيره؛ أضيف له لوجوب مغايرة المضاف للمضاف إليه. (قوله: فلذا جعل الحكم صفة له) أي: لأن الصفة عين الموصوف. (قوله: فقيل) عطف على (جعل). (قوله: ثم إذا حصل هذا الإدراك) الظاهر أن مراده بالإدراك الحاصل: الإدراك الحاصل بعد تصور الطرفين والنسبة، وهو الإدراك الأخير، وقوله: (ولم يتوقف)؛ أي: التصديق من حيث حصوله على تصور ذلك الإدراك؛ أي: الذي هو الحكم، بحيث يصح أن يقال: تصور الحكم بالإضافة، وقرر شيخنا العدوي: أن الظاهر أن مراده بالإدراك ما يشمل التصورات الأربعة. وقوله: (ولم يتوقف... إلخ)؛ أي: التصديق من حيث حصوله على تصور ذلك الإدراك الشامل للتصورات الأربعة، وذلك لأنه لو توقف على ذلك؛ للزم التسلسل. العطار؛ الحكم عنده إدراكا من قبيل التصور، ويكون هذا التصور مخالفا بالحقيقة لسائر التصورات، مخصوصا من عموم قوله: التصورات كلها ضرورية؛ بدليل أن دلائله غير جارية في هذا القسم؛ أعني التصور الذي هو الحكم؛ فلا يلزم كون التصديقات أيضا ضرورية عنده، ولا يلزم بطلان ما هو المشهور من الانحصار، قاله المحشي. (قوله: ولم يتوقف على تصور ذلك الإدراك) أشعر بأنه يسوغ تعلق الإدراك به، وهو الحق؛ إذ لا حجر في التصورات كما قرر في الحكمة، وما توهم من عدم صحة ذلك للزوم التسلسل؛ مندفع بأن مثله ليس مما يجري فيه التسلسل؛ لطرو ذهول ونحوه، وفي عبد الحكيم؛ أن عدم ذكر متعلق التصور الرابع، بل قيل: وإن كان فعلا - والفعل مغاير للإدراك؛ إذ الإدراك انفعال والفعل يغايره -؛ فحينئذ يكون التصديق مركبا من التصورات الثلاثة والحكم. الدسوقي لأن تصور تلك التصورات يحتاج أيضا إلى تصور، وتصوره يحتاج إلى تصور آخر وهكذا، فلا يحصل التصديق، وحينئذ؛ فتكون التصورات الأربعة حاصلة غير متصورة. نعم إن حكم على تصور من تلك التصورات بأنه موجود مثلا؛ توقف التصديق بأنه موجود على تصور ذلك التصور، ولا يحتاج ذلك التصور إلى أن يتصور لما يلزم عليه من التسلسل. (قوله: وإن كان فعلا) أي: وإن كان الحكم فعلا، وجواب (إن)؛ قوله: (فحينئذ) وما بينهما جملة حالية أو اعتراضية، وهذا مقابل لقوله سابقا (فإن كان إدراكا... إلخ). فإن قلت على القول بأنه فعل؛ كيف يتصف بالبداهة والكسب مع أن الأفعال لا تتصف بهما؟ قلت: أصحاب هذا القول يمنعون كون جميع الأفعال لا توصف بهما، ويقولون: إن بعض الأفعال يتصف بهما، فإن توقف الفعل النفسي على أمور معلومة وترتب عليها؛ فهو كسبي، وإلا؛ فبديهي. (قوله: إذ الإدراك انفعال) هذا إنما يصح إذا فسر الإدراك بانتقاش الصورة الحاصلة من الشيء في العقل كما سبق. وأما إذا فسر بالصورة الحاصلة في العقل؛ كان كيفا لا انفعالا، وهذا هو التحقيق، وحينئذ؛ فلا يكون الإدراك انفعالا، كما لا يكون فعلا. (قوله: من التصورات الثلاثة والحكم) أي: الذي هو فعل على ما قيل. العطار والتصور الذي هو الحكم؛ إشارة إلى أن متعلقه تلك النسبة المتصورة، لكن من حيث الوقوع واللا وقوع. (قوله: وإن كان فعلا) عطف على (فإن كان إدراكا)، وجزاؤه قوله: (فحينئذ)، وجملة: (والفعل ... إلخ)؛ معترضة. (قوله: والفعل يغايره) اختصار لقول الرازي في شرح الأصل: والفعل لا يكون انفعالا، قال السيد: وذلك لأن الفعل هو التأثير وإيجاد الأثر، والانفعال هو التأثر.
Introduction of the author (matn): Likewise: the conception of the subject of judgment, and the conception of the relative judgment. As for the perception that occurs to us after the conception of the two terms and the relation, it is identical to the judgment; therefore, the judgment was made an attribute of it, and it was said: the conception that is the judgment. Then when this perception occurs, assent (tasdiq) occurs, and it does not depend on the conception of that perception. al-Dasuqi: After (i.e., and since the conception of the subject is other than it, it was added to it due to the necessity of the difference between the addend and the addendum). His statement: “Therefore, the judgment was made an attribute of it” means because the attribute is identical to the described. His statement: “it was said” is coordinate with (was made). His statement: “Then when this perception occurs” – apparently what he means by the occurring perception is the perception that occurs after the conception of the two terms and the relation, which is the final perception, and his statement: “and it does not depend” means: assent (tasdiq), in terms of its occurrence, does not depend on the conception of that perception, i.e., which is the judgment, such that it is correct to say: conception of the judgment in addition. Our teacher al-‘Adawi argued that apparently what he means by perception is what includes the four conceptions. And his statement: “and it does not depend... etc.” means: assent (tasdiq) in terms of its occurrence does not depend on the conception of that perception which includes the four conceptions, because if it depended on that, infinite regress would follow. al-‘Attar: The judgment according to him is a perception of the type of conception, and this conception is in reality different from other conceptions, being excepted from the generality of his statement: all conceptions are necessary; because his proofs do not apply to this category, namely the conception that is the judgment. So it does not necessitate that assents are also necessary according to him, nor does it necessitate the nullity of what is well-known of the exclusive division, as the commentator said. His statement: “and it does not depend on the conception of that perception” suggests that he permits the attachment of perception to it, and this is correct, since there is no restriction in conceptions as established in philosophy; and what is imagined of its incorrectness due to the necessary infinite regress is refuted by the fact that such is not subject to infinite regress due to the occurrence of oversight or the like. And in ‘Abd al-Hakim: that the non-mention of the object of the fourth conception, rather it was said: And if it is an act – and the act is different from perception, since perception is passivity and the act is different – then in that case assent would be composed of the three conceptions and the judgment. al-Dasuqi: Because the conception of those conceptions also needs a conception, and its conception needs another conception, and so on, so assent would not occur, and in that case, the four conceptions would be existent but not conceived. Indeed, if one judges a conception among those as existing, for instance, the assent that it exists depends on the conception of that conception, but that conception does not need to be conceived because of the infinite regress that would follow. His statement: “and if it is an act” means: if the judgment is an act, and the protasis answer is his statement: “then in that case”, and what is between them is a circumstantial or parenthetical clause, and this is contrasted with his previous statement (if it is a perception... etc.). If you say: on the view that it is an act, how is it characterized by intuitiveness (badaha) and acquisition (kasb) while acts are not so characterized? I say: proponents of this view deny that all acts are not characterized by them, and they say: some acts are characterized by them; if the internal mental act depends on known matters and is consequent upon them, then it is acquired; otherwise it is intuitive. His statement: “since perception is passivity” – this is only correct if perception is interpreted as the impression of the form obtained from the thing in the mind as previously. But if it is interpreted as the form obtained in the mind, then it is a quality, not a passivity, and this is the correct view. In that case, perception is not passivity, just as it is not an act. His statement: “from the three conceptions and the judgment” means: which is an act according to what was said. al-‘Attar: And the conception that is the judgment indicates that its object is that conceived relation, but in terms of occurrence and non-occurrence. His statement: “and if it is an act” is coordinate with (if it is a perception), and its apodosis is his statement: “then in that case”, and the clause (and the act... etc.) is parenthetical. His statement: “and the act is different from it” is an abbreviation of al-Razi’s statement in the commentary on the original: the act is not passivity; al-Sayyid said: because the act is the effect and the bringing about of the effect, while passivity is being affected.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) by al-Dasūqī and al-‘Aṭṭār on the nature of judgment (ḥukm) within assent (taṣdīq). The matn states that taṣdīq requires conceiving the subject, predicate, and relation, and then the judgment itself, which is also a conception. The ḥāshiya addresses two views: judgment as conception vs. judgment as act. 

Al-Dasūqī explains that if judgment is a conception, the additional perception (that judgment) does not require a separate conception to avoid infinite regress; otherwise, we would need an infinite chain of conceptions. Al-‘Aṭṭār clarifies that this type of conception is exceptional—unlike other conceptions, it need not be necessary (ḍarūrī), because the proofs for necessary conceptions do not apply to it. The objection that this leads to regress is refuted: regress does not apply here because of possible oversight or similar. 

Then the alternative view is presented: if judgment is an act (fi‘l) rather than a perception (idrāk), then taṣdīq is composed of the three conceptions plus the act. Al-Dasūqī points out the problem: if each conception of a conception requires another conception, we get regress, and the four conceptions would be un-conceived. However, if we judge a conception to exist, that judgment's assent depends on conceiving that conception, but the conception itself does not need to be conceived again—otherwise regress. 

The commentary then addresses how an act can be intuitive or acquired: proponents of this view say that some internal mental acts can be characterized as intuitive (badīhī) or acquired (kasbī), depending on whether they depend on prior known matters. 

Finally, al-‘Aṭṭār clarifies that perception is not essentially passivity; it can be a quality (form in the mind), which is neither passivity nor act. The judgment's object, when conceived, is the relation considered in terms of occurrence. This discussion guards against misunderstanding the nature of judgment and its role in assent, emphasizing that the logical analysis of taṣdīq does not require an infinite regress of conceptions.

Key Terms
التصديق
الحكم
الإدراك
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-‘Aṭṭār's explanation in this passage, what is the status of the conception that is the judgment (al-taṣawwur alladhi huwa al-ḥukm)?
A) It is a necessary conception like all other conceptions.
B) It is an act (fi‘l) and thus not a conception.
C) It is a conception but exceptional, not subject to the rule that all conceptions are necessary.
D) It is a perception that requires a further conception to avoid regress.

Key Takeaway
The definition of tasdiq is refined either as three conceptions plus a judgment-conception or as three conceptions plus an act; the debate centers on whether judgment is a conception or an act, with implications for infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the proposition 'The world is contingent.' Identify the three conceptions (subject, predicate, relation) and the judgment that affirms the connection. Then decide whether, on the conception view, the judgment itself needs to be conceived separately to yield assent. Explain why or why not, citing the argument from this lesson.
?
Consider the alternative view that judgment is an act. Formulate a response to the objection that an act cannot be intuitive (badihi) using the reasoning from the text about some acts being intuitive.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
